# PROGRESS

This file is maintained by the build loop, not the user. Read it at the start of every iteration. Update it at the end of every iteration.

The loop's job is to keep this file honest. If something here is out of date, fix it before doing anything else.

---

## How to use this file

Every iteration:

1. **Read** the "Current state" section to know where things stand.
2. **Read** the "Next slice" section to see what was queued last time.
3. If "Next slice" is empty, **pick** the next one based on the priorities in MISSION.md §7 (Definition of Done) and the Backlog below. Smallest end-to-end slice that moves a Definition-of-Done item closer to ticked.
4. Move the chosen slice from Backlog into "Current slice" with a plan.
5. Implement, test, self-critique.
6. On commit, move the entry from "Current slice" into the "Completed slices" log with the commit hash and a one-line summary.
7. Refresh the "Current state" section.
8. Queue the next slice in "Next slice" if obvious, otherwise leave empty.
9. Update "Definition of Done tracker" if a box just got ticked.
10. Note anything weird in "Open questions" or "Proposed scope changes" — never silently fold scope changes into the work.

If the same test or the same problem fails three iterations in a row without measurable progress, stop and write to BLOCKED.md per MISSION.md §8.

---

## Current state

**Iteration:** 50 (complete — SC1d shipped)
**Last commit:** `52fc2ec` — slice: SC1d — Thread `next=` redirect param through stock-in/out/adjust routes (DoD #3). Prior commit: `370cb3a` — slice: SC1c — Inline action forms on the scan-flow item page (DoD #3).
**Branch:** main
**Tests:** ruff ✓, mypy ✓ (28 files), pytest 1677 unit+integration ✓ (was 1661, +16 new SC1d tests across `test_movements_routes.py` + `test_scan_routes.py`), Playwright 14 e2e ✓ (no count change).

**SC1d — Thread `next=` redirect param through stock-in/out/adjust routes (DoD #3 desktop/USB leg polish, MISSION §3 "Barcode/QR workflow"):** continues SC1c. After SC1c a Workshop user could record a movement in two interactions, but the success redirect landed them on the per-action form (`/admin/items/{id}/{in,out,adjust}`) — to scan the next item they had to manually click `nav-scan`. SC1d threads an optional `next` form param through the three movement POST routes so scan-flow submits redirect back into scan flow (`/scan/item/{id}` — same item, with the post-mutation `current_qty` visible + the autofocused scan input ready for the next code). DoD #3's "two interactions" wording is unaffected — that was already met by SC1c for a single movement. SC1d makes a *multi-item* scan session viable (no manual nav-clicks between items) without adding to the per-movement interaction count. **DoD #3 still does not tick** — the camera leg (SC2) is required.

- **Helper** (`app/movements.py::_safe_scan_next`): `(raw: str) -> str | None`. Returns the trimmed value if it equals `/scan` or starts with `/scan/`; else `None`. Whitelist is conservative on purpose — covers the two scan-flow URLs the app owns, rejects open-redirect attempts (`//evil.com/x` doesn't match either pattern), rejects close prefixes (`/scanner/...` is not `/scan/`), rejects every other path. ~5 LoC; placed near the other parse helpers.

- **Route changes** (`app/movements.py`):
  - **`record_stock_in` / `record_stock_out` / `record_stock_adjustment`:** added `next_: str = Form("", alias="next")` form param to all three POST routes. The Python identifier is `next_` (avoid the builtin shadow); the URL form name stays `next` via the `alias=`. On each success path the hardcoded `RedirectResponse(url=f"/admin/items/{item.id}/<action>", ...)` becomes `target_url = _safe_scan_next(next_) or f"/admin/items/{item.id}/<action>"; return RedirectResponse(url=target_url, ...)`. ~3 LoC per route.
  - **No template changes** to `stock_in_form.html` / `stock_out_form.html` / `stock_adjust_form.html`. The error paths in `out` and `adjust direction=decrease` continue to re-render via `_render_stock_out_form` / `_render_stock_adjust_form` exactly as today (no `next` threading on the error path — drop-and-recover posture; rationale below).

- **Template** (`app/templates/scan.html`): one hidden input added to each of the three inline forms: `<input type="hidden" name="next" value="/scan/item/{{ resolved_item.id }}">`. Placed right after the existing `csrf_token` hidden input on each form. 1 LoC × 3 = 3 LoC. Form action URLs and visible inputs are unchanged.

- **Why `/scan/item/{id}` over `/scan`:** lands the user on the surface that shows the post-mutation `current_qty` (so they can verify what they just did), and the autofocused scan input on that page lets the next scan resolve to a different item. Going to `/scan` would lose the "see what you did" feedback. Pinned by the `next_to_scan_item_redirects_to_scan_flow` test on each route + the `next_to_scan_landing_redirects_to_scan_flow` test (which still allows `/scan` for any future caller that wants the landing page).

- **Why drop `next` on the error path:** the two error paths (insufficient stock on `out` and `adjust direction=decrease`) re-render the per-action form template (`stock_out_form.html` / `stock_adjust_form.html`) with form values + an error block. Threading `next` through to the re-render would require (a) the helper `_render_stock_*_form` to accept `next_` and pass it into context, (b) the templates to render a hidden `next` input, (c) tests pinning the round-trip — ~10-15 LoC + 2-3 tests across two templates for a rare path. Drop instead: when a Workshop user hits insufficient-stock from scan flow, they land on the per-action form with the error and the full context (open value, recent movements). They've left scan flow but can use the bigger surface to recover. The validation 400s (empty qty etc.) raise `HTTPException` directly with no body — nothing to preserve there either. Pinned by `test_insufficient_stock_drops_next_and_re_renders` on stock-out + `test_insufficient_stock_decrease_drops_next_and_re_renders` on stock-adjust.

- **Why no per-action form template changes (Q4 design call):** the route accepts `next: str = Form("")` from any caller; the per-action form templates don't render a hidden `next` input (would always be empty). Only `scan.html` renders it. Simplest impl; matches the "no per-action form template changes" boundary.

- **Manual sanity check** (no human required): each new redirect test posts through the route with the engine running (cost layer / FIFO consume / current_qty bump) and asserts the `Location` header is the scan-flow URL. The test_movements_e2e walk continues to pass, confirming no regression on the per-action-form caller (which doesn't pass `next`).

- **Tests** (16 new):
  - `tests/integration/test_movements_routes.py`:
    - `TestStockInNextRedirect` (5): no `next` → `/admin/items/{id}/in` (regression); `next=/scan/item/{id}` → that path; `next=/scan` → `/scan`; `next=/admin/items/X/edit` → falls back to default; `next=//evil.com/x` → falls back to default.
    - `TestStockOutNextRedirect` (5): same 4 happy/whitelist tests + `test_insufficient_stock_drops_next_and_re_renders` (qty=5 from a 2-unit layer with `next=/scan/item/{id}` returns 400, asserts "Not enough stock" in the body, asserts no `name="next"` substring in the re-rendered form).
    - `TestStockAdjustNextRedirect` (5): same shape with both `direction=increase` and `direction=decrease` happy paths, the `//evil.com/x` whitelist case, and `test_insufficient_stock_decrease_drops_next_and_re_renders` for the decrease error path.
  - `tests/integration/test_scan_routes.py`:
    - `TestScanItemPageInlineFormFields::test_each_inline_form_carries_hidden_next_input` (1): asserts each of the three inline forms includes `name="next"` + `value="/scan/item/{id}"` substrings inside its data-testid block.

**Repo health:**
- ruff: clean (`app tests`)
- mypy: clean (strict on `app/`, 28 source files — no new modules)
- pytest unit + integration: 1677 passing (was 1661, +16)
- Playwright e2e: 14 passing (no count change — same posture as SC1c; an e2e walk for the scan-flow round-trip lands when SC2 introduces unique camera-side behaviour worth covering)

**Definition-of-Done items ticked:** **4 / 12** (DoD #2 + DoD #4 + DoD #5 + DoD #6 — unchanged this iteration). SC1d polishes DoD #3's desktop/USB leg (already substantively delivered by SC1c). DoD #3 still requires the camera leg (SC2) to tick.

<!-- SC1c plan/tests detail (now superseded by SC1d) — kept commented to avoid bloating Current state but preserved in the Completed log on row I49 with hash 370cb3a.

**SC1c — Inline action forms on the scan-flow item page (DoD #3 desktop/USB leg, MISSION §3 "Barcode/QR workflow"):** continues SC1b's `/scan/item/{id}` action-picker page. Replaces the three action *links* (Stock-out / Stock-in / Adjust) with three inline *forms* that POST directly to the existing `/admin/items/{id}/{out,in,adjust}` movement routes — no route changes. After SC1c the flow on a USB-scanner desktop is **scan-Enter → fill qty (and unit_cost where required) → submit** — two interactions. The desktop/USB leg of DoD #3 is now closed; the camera leg lands in SC2 (after which DoD #3 ticks).

- **Template** (`app/templates/scan.html` — extended):
  - Replaces the three `<a class="button" data-testid="scan-action-{in,out,adjust}">` link blocks with three `<form method="post" action="/admin/items/{id}/{out,in,adjust}">` blocks, ordered out → in → adjust (Workshop's hot-path bias: stock-out first because consuming raw material in production is the most frequent scan-flow action; stock-in second; adjust third because variance corrections are the rarest and the form is the largest).
  - Each form carries the standard `<input type="hidden" name="csrf_token" value="{{ csrf_token }}">`.
  - **Stock-out form** (`<section data-testid="scan-out-form">`): one `<input data-testid="scan-out-qty-input" name="qty" required inputmode="decimal">` + `<button data-testid="scan-out-submit">`. No unit_cost (FIFO consumes per-layer), no reason (optional in the route, kept off the inline surface to keep the hot-path tight).
  - **Stock-in form** (`<section data-testid="scan-in-form">`): qty input + `<input data-testid="scan-in-unit-cost-input" name="unit_cost" required inputmode="decimal">` + submit. Unit cost is required by the underlying route (every cost layer needs a price); zero is allowed for sample/gifted stock per the existing `_parse_non_negative_decimal` posture.
  - **Adjust form** (`<section data-testid="scan-adjust-form">`): `<select data-testid="scan-adjust-direction-input" name="direction" required>` (blank `— pick one —` then `increase` + `decrease`) + qty + unit_cost (not `required` because direction=decrease ignores it, mirroring `stock_adjust_form.html`) + `<input data-testid="scan-adjust-reason-input" name="reason" required maxlength="255">` + submit. Reason is required server-side (variance attribution per MISSION §3) so it's required client-side too.
  - **No route changes** — `app/movements.py`'s `record_stock_in` / `record_stock_out` / `record_stock_adjustment` already do all validation, audit, redirect. The inline forms are pure UI surfaces. On success, the existing routes redirect to their per-action form (`/admin/items/{id}/in` etc) with a flash; the user lands there with the recent-movements table for confirmation.
  - **Archived items**: same posture as SC1b — no action forms rendered (the underlying routes 400 on archived items, so submitting would error). The archived badge + explanatory note + scan input persist so the user can scan another item.
  - The `scan-action-checkout` link stays as-is for `requires_checkout` items (separate flow with its own state machine — no inline form).
  - The scan input + autofocus stay at the top of the page on `/scan/item/{id}` so the next item's scan keystroke is captured without manual nav.

- **Why three inline forms (3a) over one form with a selector (3b) or a default-action (3c):** 3a satisfies DoD #3's "two interactions" goal directly — the user types into the qty box of the action they want; there's no separate "pick action" click. 3b would need either a re-render round-trip or JS to swap the cost field based on direction — MISSION §5 forbids JS frameworks. 3c forces a wrong default 1/3 of the time (Workshop's hot-path is stock-out, but Office uses scan for stock-in too) and re-introduces the link-click for non-default cases. Trade-off: visually busier page with three stacked forms; acceptable on a destination page (vs. a list).

- **Manual sanity check** (no human required): the four `TestScanItemPageInlineFormSubmission` tests POST end-to-end through the inline-form action URLs and assert the existing routes wire up — Workshop submits stock-in → cost layer + audit + current_qty bump; submits stock-out → FIFO consume + audit + current_qty drop; submits adjust direction=increase → positive-adjustment layer + audit + current_qty bump; submits empty qty → 400. The full submit chain is exercised via `client.post` with the same CSRF token shape the template renders.

- **Tests** (16 new + 3 existing-test reshapes in `tests/integration/test_scan_routes.py`):
  - **Existing tests reshaped** (3): `TestScanItemPageRender::test_renders_three_action_links_with_correct_hrefs` → `test_renders_three_inline_action_forms` (asserts form actions + submit-button test-ids instead of link hrefs); `TestScanItemPageArchived::test_archived_item_omits_action_buttons` (asserts no `scan-out-submit` / `scan-in-submit` / `scan-adjust-submit` / `scan-out-form` / `scan-in-form` / `scan-adjust-form`); `TestScanItemPageResolveChain::test_post_resolve_then_follow_renders_action_picker` (asserts `scan-out-form` is present on the chained-render).
  - `TestScanItemPageInlineForms` (3): each of out / in / adjust renders with `method="post"` + `action="/admin/items/{id}/..."` + a `name="csrf_token"` hidden input.
  - `TestScanItemPageInlineFormFields` (6): out form has qty input only (no unit_cost / no reason / no direction); in form has qty + unit_cost (no direction / no reason); adjust form has direction select + qty + unit_cost + reason; adjust direction select offers `increase` + `decrease` options; the qty inputs on all three forms are `required`; the reason input on adjust is `required`.
  - `TestScanItemPageInlineFormSubmission` (4): Workshop submits stock-in via inline form (POST to `/admin/items/{id}/in` → 303 + audit + current_qty=5.0000); stock-out (POST → 303 + audit + current_qty=10→7); adjust direction=increase (POST → 303 + audit + current_qty=4.0000); empty qty → 400 (route still handles the validation; the inline form is a thin posting surface).

- **Route changes** (`app/scan.py`):
  - **`POST /scan/resolve`** — same role gate (`require_role(WORKSHOP, OFFICE, MANAGER)` + Admin via the role bypass), same trim, same flash semantics for empty / no-match. **Changed**: on a successful resolve the redirect target flips from `/admin/items/{item.id}/edit` to `/scan/item/{item.id}`. The `_resolve_code` helper is unchanged (qr_code-first then sku-fallback, archived items still resolve, whitespace trimmed). The 303 status code is preserved.

Rationale: the USB-scanner workflow is "scan, see result, click action; then scan the next item without leaving scan-flow" — keeping the input on the action-picker page means the next scan is a single keystroke + Enter without manual nav.

Linking to a 400 is a dead-end; the picker omits those buttons and instead renders an `<em data-testid="scan-resolved-archived-note">This item is archived; record movements via the items list instead.</em>` note. Test-ids: `scan-action-in` / `scan-action-out` / `scan-action-adjust`. The check-out form (C2) has its own role + state gating; surfacing the link here is a polish detail that keeps the action picker consistent with `items_form.html`'s action block.
  - The flash region from `base.html` continues to handle "no match" / "empty code" feedback after the existing 303 to `/scan`. The action-picker page itself doesn't flash on render (it's a destination, not a transition).

- **Nav highlight inherited.** `base.html`'s nav already marks the link `aria-current="page"` when `request.url.path == "/scan" or request.url.path.startswith("/scan/")` — so `/scan/item/{id}` correctly highlights the Scan nav entry. No template changes needed.

**Iteration 47 chore — fix ruff PT018 in `tests/integration/test_scan_routes.py`:** the loop runner's `make check` after iteration 46's SC1a commit (`44ecff1`) reported `PT018 Assertion should be broken down into multiple parts` at `test_scan_routes.py:208`. SC1a's `TestScanGetRender::test_input_has_autofocus_and_name_code` had a single `assert tag_start >= 0 and tag_end > tag_start` two-part assertion; ruff's pytest plugin (PT018) wants each conjunct as its own assertion so a failure pinpoints which condition broke. Split into two separate `assert` lines (`assert tag_start >= 0` then `assert tag_end > tag_start`). Two-line cosmetic change inside the test — no production code touched, no test count change, no behavioural change. The original SC1a iteration's `make lint` evidently wasn't run (the prior PROGRESS.md self-report claimed "ruff: clean" — it wasn't); root cause is reporting drift, not a missing rule. No new tests needed — the existing assertion pair pins the same invariants more granularly. **Previous iteration's tests breakdown** (preserved for slice context — pinned 31 new tests in `tests/integration/test_scan_routes.py` under seven new classes: `TestScanGetRoleEnforcement` (6: anon 401, pending 403, Workshop 200, Office 200, Manager 200, Admin 200), `TestScanGetRender` (3: heading present, form has `action="/scan/resolve"` + `method="post"`, input has `name="code"` + `autofocus`), `TestScanResolveRoleEnforcement` (5: anon 401, pending 403, Workshop 303, Office 303, Manager 303 — all with valid codes), `TestScanResolveMatching` (5: by qr_code, by sku-fallback, qr_code wins on collision, whitespace trim, archived item still resolves), `TestScanResolveEmptyOrNoMatch` (3: empty/whitespace/unknown code → 303 to `/scan` + flash echoes the offending code), `TestScanReadOnly` (2: GET writes no audit, POST resolve writes no audit), `TestScanNav` (7: Workshop/Office/Manager/Admin all see `nav-scan`; pending sees no nav at all; anon sees no nav-scan; `/scan` page marks the link `aria-current="page"`)).
**Definition-of-Done items ticked:** **4 / 12** (DoD #2 + DoD #4 + DoD #5 + DoD #6). SC1a moves DoD #3 from completely unmoved (since I3) to substantially closer: Workshop now has a focused-input scan landing page that resolves a QR/SKU code to the item's existing edit surface (where in/out/adjust action links already work). The two-interaction goal of DoD #3 hasn't been reached yet — SC1a delivers a three-interaction path (scan → click action → submit form). DoD #3 ticks when SC1b/c collapse the action-click into the scan-landing page (action picker + qty/cost entry on the same surface) and SC2 adds camera-based scanning.

**SC1a — Scan-mode landing page with code-resolution (DoD #3 first step, MISSION §3 "Barcode/QR workflow"):** smallest end-to-end SC1 sub-slice. New module `app/scan.py` mounted at `/scan` with two routes (`GET /scan` renders the page; `POST /scan/resolve` resolves a code to an item and 303-redirects to its existing edit page). New template `scan.html`. New nav link `nav-scan` placed second in the primary nav (right after Home), visible to **Workshop, Office, Manager, Admin** so it's on Workshop's hot-path.

- **Route module** (`app/scan.py`):
  - `router = APIRouter(prefix="/scan", tags=["scan"])`.
  - `GET /scan` — `Depends(require_role(Role.WORKSHOP, Role.OFFICE, Role.MANAGER))` (Admin via the role bypass; pending → 403; anon → 401). Renders `scan.html`. Read-only — no audit.
  - `POST /scan/resolve` — same role gate. Form param `code: str = Form("")`. Trims leading/trailing whitespace. If empty after trim → `_flash("Please scan or type a code.")` + 303 to `/scan`. Else looks up `Item` by `qr_code == code` first (the model has a partial-unique index on `qr_code WHERE qr_code IS NOT NULL`), falling back to `Item.sku == code` (the model has a unique index). On match: 303 to `/admin/items/{item.id}/edit`. On no match: `_flash(f"No item found for code: {trimmed}.")` + 303 to `/scan`.
  - **Precedence is qr_code-first then sku-fallback.** Rationale: physical labels carry a QR code; the QR's payload is the canonical scanned value. SKUs are human-typed identifiers (e.g. `ALLOY-925-2MM`) only used as a fallback when no QR is present. Pinned by `TestScanResolveMatching::test_qr_code_wins_over_sku_on_collision` (two distinct items, one with `sku="X"` and one with `qr_code="X"`; the qr-coded one wins).
  - **Archived items still resolve.** A scanner doesn't know an item was archived; refusing the resolution would leave the user staring at the scan page with no signal. The destination edit page already renders archived items in a read-only state with the appropriate badge, so the user lands on a useful surface. Pinned by `TestScanResolveMatching::test_archived_item_still_resolves`.
  - Read-only: neither route writes an audit row. Resolution is a navigation action, not a state change. Pinned by `TestScanReadOnly`'s two tests (GET and POST resolve, comparing pre/post audit counts).
  - Pure `_resolve_code` helper: takes `(db, code)` and returns `Item | None`. The qr-vs-sku logic lives in this helper rather than inline in the route so SC1b can reuse it (e.g. resolve + execute the action in one POST without re-implementing the lookup).

- **Template** (`app/templates/scan.html`):
  - `<h1 data-testid="scan-heading">Scan</h1>` + a one-line `<p data-testid="scan-instructions">` with guidance ("Scan an item's QR code or type its SKU and press Enter.").
  - `<form data-testid="scan-form" method="post" action="/scan/resolve">` with the standard CSRF token hidden input.
  - Single `<input data-testid="scan-code-input" name="code" type="text" autocomplete="off" autofocus required maxlength="255">`. Submit button `data-testid="scan-submit"`.
  - `autofocus` is the USB-scanner-friendly choice: HID-emulating scanners send keystrokes followed by Enter; landing on the page with the input focused means the very next keystroke is captured. SC2 will overlay a camera-driven control on the same surface.
  - The flash region from `base.html` is reused for the "no match" / "empty code" feedback — no per-template error block needed.

- **Nav link** (`base.html`): `nav-scan` inserted as the *second* item (right after "Home"), visible to **Workshop + Office + Manager + Admin** (every active non-pending role). Active-state highlighting via `aria-current="page"` when `request.url.path == "/scan"` or starts with `/scan/`. Workshop today only sees Home + Items in the nav — adding Scan second pushes it onto Workshop's hot-path.

- **Router wiring** (`app/main.py`): `app.include_router(scan_module.router)` added next to the other includes. Sorted alphabetically alongside the other `app import X as X_module` lines.

- **Manual sanity check** (no human required): the loop ran a one-shot `TestClient` script that signs in as Workshop, GETs `/scan` (200, has form + autofocus), POSTs `/scan/resolve` with a valid QR code (303 → `/admin/items/{id}/edit`), POSTs with whitespace-only code (303 → `/scan`, flash present), POSTs with unknown code (303 → `/scan`, flash echoes the code), and verifies `nav-scan` is present on the home page. All paths green.

**Repo health:**
- ruff: clean (`app tests`)
- mypy: clean (strict on `app/`, 28 source files — `app/scan.py` is the +1)
- pytest unit + integration: 1632 passing (was 1601, +31)
- Playwright e2e: 14 passing (no count change)

**R5h — CSV export on the cross-item checkouts admin list (DoD #7 polish, MISSION §3 "Export any list view to CSV"):** eighth CSV-export surface. Third *new* call site of R5e's `csv_branch` helper (after R5f's locations list + R5g's taxonomy list). Extends `app/checkouts_admin.py::list_checkouts` with a `?format=csv` query branch and adds a `checkouts-admin-csv-link` "Download CSV" link to `checkouts_admin.html`.

- **Route extension** (`app/checkouts_admin.py::list_checkouts`):
  - New `format: str = ""` query param. `format == "csv"` triggers CSV via `csv_branch`; anything else (blank / `html` / garbage) renders HTML — same silent-coerce posture as `show`.
  - **Role gate inherited**: existing `Depends(require_role(Role.MANAGER, Role.OFFICE))` already blocks Workshop + pending at the dependency layer (Workshop excluded from the cross-item view per C4 — they have per-item status blocks via C2's `/checkout` page). Admin via the role bypass. No inner role-split needed.
  - Same data source as the HTML branch (`_list_open_checkouts(db, show=show, now=now)`); reuses the view-shaped dicts.
  - **Headers** (11 columns): `checkout_id`, `item_id`, `item_sku`, `item_name`, `item_archived`, `unit_serial`, `holder_email`, `checked_out_at`, `expected_return`, `is_overdue`, `days_overdue`. Mirrors the HTML table cells one-for-one (8 visual columns) plus three explicit ID/state columns: `checkout_id` + `item_id` (HTML carries them as `data-checkout-id` / `data-item-id` attributes; making them columns lets a downstream consumer join), and `is_overdue` (the HTML conflates it with `days_overdue` into a single "Status" cell; the CSV separates them so a downstream filter can target one or the other). The Actions cell (link) is presentation-only and not surfaced.
  - **`item_archived` + `is_overdue` cells**: render as the literal strings `"yes"` / `"no"` (matching R5/R5b's PO list `supplier_archived` and items list `requires_checkout` precedent — spreadsheet receivers find yes/no easier to filter on than `True`/`False`).
  - **`unit_serial` + `holder_email` cells**: empty when `None` (matching `csv_response`'s coercion). HTML renders `—` for these but a CSV cell of `—` would mis-sort against actual values.
  - **`checked_out_at`**: ISO datetime via `csv_response`'s coercion.
  - **`expected_return`**: ISO datetime when set, empty when None. The HTML formats as `%Y-%m-%d` but the CSV preserves the full datetime so a downstream consumer can sort precisely.
  - **`days_overdue`**: integer when overdue, empty when not. Matches the `is_overdue=False → days_overdue is None` pairing in `_list_open_checkouts`.
  - **Filename**: `checkouts_{show}.csv` — `checkouts_open.csv` / `checkouts_overdue.csv`. Coerced `show` is used so a user typing `?format=csv&show=garbage` gets `checkouts_open.csv`.
  - Module-level `_CHECKOUTS_ADMIN_CSV_HEADERS` constant + new `_csv_rows_for_checkouts(rows)` helper. Mirrors the seven prior surfaces' precedent.
  - **Return type widened** on `list_checkouts` from `HTMLResponse` to `Response`; `@router.get("", response_class=HTMLResponse)` decorator simplified to `@router.get("")`. The `HTMLResponse` import was removed from the module — no other route in the module used it.
  - **Walrus form**: `if (resp := csv_branch(format, filename=..., headers=..., rows=...)) is not None: return resp` — same shape as the seven prior sites.
  - **Sort survives CSV**: `_list_open_checkouts` already does its Python-side sort (overdue first, then `checked_out_at DESC, id DESC`) before returning; the CSV branch consumes the sorted list.

- **Template** (`checkouts_admin.html`): new `<a data-testid="checkouts-admin-csv-link" href="/admin/checkouts?format=csv&show={{ show }}">Download CSV</a>` link block sitting between the filter nav and the table. Href preserves active `show` value.

- **Role enforcement preserved**: anon hits the dependency and 401s before reaching the format check. Pending / Workshop hit the same dependency and 403.

- **Read-only invariant preserved**: GET-CSV writes no audit row. Pinned by `TestCheckoutsAdminCsvReadOnly::test_csv_writes_no_audit`.

**R5e — `csv_branch` helper extraction (refactor — DoD #7 polish, no behavioural change):** queued by R5d's self-critique. Five surfaces now expose `?format=csv` CSV export (variance trend + PO list + items list + stock-takes list + suppliers list); R5e centralises the recurring `if format == "csv": return csv_response(...)` branch into a single helper.

- **New helper** (`app/csv_export.py`): `csv_branch(format_value, *, filename, headers, rows) -> Response | None`. Returns `csv_response(filename=..., headers=..., rows=...)` when `format_value == "csv"`, else `None`. Delegates filename sanitisation, header/row coercion, and Content-Disposition shaping to the existing `csv_response` — no duplicated logic.

- **5 call sites migrated** to the walrus pattern `if (resp := csv_branch(...)) is not None: return resp`:
  - `app/reports.py::variance_trend` (variance trend report) — reads format from `request.query_params.get("format", "")` inline.
  - `app/purchase_orders.py::list_purchase_orders` (PO list) — typed `format: str = ""` query param.
  - `app/items.py::list_items` (items list) — `is_csv` flag retained for the inner Workshop role gate (separate concern); only the response branch was collapsed.
  - `app/stock_takes.py::list_stock_takes` (stock-takes list) — typed `format: str = ""` query param.
  - `app/suppliers.py::list_suppliers` (suppliers list) — typed `format: str = ""` query param.

- **No call-site behaviour change.** Every existing CSV integration test on every surface passes unchanged (~76 integration tests across the five surfaces all green). The 5 new unit tests pin the helper's `Response | None` contract directly.

- **Real win is centralization, not LoC.** Each call site went from a 6-line block to a 9-line walrus block (the kwargs span 4 lines either way). The savings are conceptual: the magic string `"csv"` now lives in exactly one place, so a future polish slice (e.g. case-insensitive `?format=CSV`, alternate `?download=csv`) is a one-line edit instead of five. Same posture for any future "always set X-Robots-Tag on CSV" or "always log CSV downloads" cross-cutting concern.

- **`is_csv` flag preserved in `app/items.py`** because the items list has a Workshop-vs-CSV role split that runs *before* the response branch (Workshop sees HTML but not CSV per MISSION §3 "cannot see aggregated cost data or reports"). Pulling that pre-gate into the helper would force `csv_branch` to know about role tuples, breaking its single-responsibility shape. Same posture would apply to any future CSV surface that needs a different role check than the route-level dependency.

**Repo health:**
- ruff: clean (`app tests`)
- mypy: clean (strict on `app/`, 27 source files — no new modules)
- pytest unit + integration: 1542 passing (was 1537, +5)
- Playwright e2e: 14 passing (no count change)

**R5b — CSV export on the items list (DoD #7 polish, MISSION §3 "Export any list view to CSV"):** extends `app/items.py::list_items` with a `?format=csv` query branch and adds an `items-list-csv-link` "Download CSV" link to `items_list.html`. Third CSV surface, after R5's variance-trend + PO list. Pattern reuses R5's `csv_response` helper unchanged.

- **Route extension** (`app/items.py`):
  - New `format` query param. `format == "csv"` triggers the CSV branch; anything else (blank, `html`, garbage) renders the existing HTML — same silent-coerce posture as `show` / `requires_checkout`.
  - **Role gate split**: HTML branch stays `Manager + Office + Workshop` (Workshop has read-only access per I1c). CSV branch is **`Manager + Office + Admin` only** — Workshop is rejected with 403. Rationale: MISSION §3 says Workshop "cannot see aggregated cost data or reports"; the items list HTML is a read of *current state*, but a CSV export is a *snapshot artefact* shaped like a report (downloadable, shareable, persistent). Same posture as the variance-trend + PO list CSV (Manager + Office). The split happens *inside* the route — the dependency stays at `require_role(Manager, Office, Workshop)` for the GET; the CSV branch then tests `_user.role` and 403s Workshop.
  - Same data source as the HTML branch (same `select(Item)` query with `show` / `node_id` / `requires_checkout` filters). No new helper for fetching.
  - **Headers** (10 columns): `id`, `sku`, `name`, `category`, `unit`, `tracking_mode`, `current_qty`, `reorder_threshold`, `reorder_qty`, `requires_checkout`. Mirror the HTML table cells one-for-one, plus the explicit `id` column (the HTML carries it as a `data-item-id` attribute, not a cell — making it explicit in the CSV lets a downstream consumer join).
  - **`requires_checkout` cell renders as the literal string `"yes"` / `"no"`** (not `"True"` / `"False"`) — same posture as the PO list's `supplier_archived`. Spreadsheet receivers find yes/no easier to filter on. Documented in `_csv_rows_for_items`'s docstring.
  - **Filename**: `items_{show}.csv` (`items_active.csv` for the default; `items_archived.csv` for `?show=archived`). The `requires_checkout=yes` filter doesn't propagate into the filename — the in-CSV `requires_checkout` cell tells the receiver what they got, and the filename stays short.
  - Module-level `_ITEMS_CSV_HEADERS` constant + new `_csv_rows_for_items(rows)` helper. Both follow the precedent of `_PO_LIST_CSV_HEADERS` / `_po_list_csv_rows` in `app/purchase_orders.py`.
  - **Return type widened** from `HTMLResponse` to `Response` to accommodate the CSV `Response` body. The HTML branch still returns a `templates.TemplateResponse` (which is a `Response` subclass). No callers expected the narrower type — the route is only reached via HTTP. The `@router.get` decorator's `response_class` argument was dropped (it's only used for OpenAPI hint generation; the actual return type is what matters at runtime).

- **Template** (`items_list.html`): new `<a data-testid="items-list-csv-link" href="/admin/items?format=csv&show={{ show }}{% if requires_checkout_filter %}&requires_checkout=yes{% endif %}">Download CSV</a>` link block, gated on `can_csv` (`current_user.role in (Manager, Office, Admin)` — same gate as the route's CSV branch). Sits between the requires-checkout filter nav and the items table. Workshop sees the items list HTML but not the CSV link.

- **Role enforcement preserved**: anon hits the `require_role(MANAGER, OFFICE, WORKSHOP)` dependency and 401s before reaching the format check. Pending hits the same dependency and 403s. Workshop reaches the route and the inner `is_csv` check rejects with 403.

- **Read-only invariant preserved**: GET-CSV writes no audit row. Pinned by `TestItemsListCsvReadOnly::test_csv_writes_no_audit`.

**R5 — CSV export on the variance-trend report and PO list (DoD #7 polish, MISSION §3 "Export any list view to CSV"):** new module `app/csv_export.py` with one helper (`csv_response`) plus a sanitiser (`_safe_filename`); `?format=csv` query branch added to two existing routes — `GET /admin/reports/variance-trend` (extends R4) and `GET /admin/purchase-orders` (extends PO2). Two new "Download CSV" links on the existing HTML pages. Subsequent slices can light up other list views by reusing the helper.

- **Helper** (`app/csv_export.py`, ~70 LoC):
  - `csv_response(*, filename, headers, rows) -> Response` — stdlib `csv.writer` over `io.StringIO`. `media_type="text/csv; charset=utf-8"`; `Content-Disposition: attachment; filename="<safe-name>"`. Body uses `\r\n` line terminators (RFC 4180 + Excel-on-Windows compatible — `csv.writer`'s default). `QUOTE_MINIMAL` quoting (default).
  - Cell coercion: `None → ""`; `datetime → .isoformat()`; `date → .isoformat()`; `Decimal / int / float / bool → str(value)`; everything else → `str(value)`.
  - `_safe_filename(name)` replaces non-`[A-Za-z0-9_.-]` chars with `_` so the `Content-Disposition` header doesn't break on stray quotes / semicolons / slashes / non-ASCII.
  - Pure (no DB, no Request, no audit). Empty `rows` still emits the header row — a header-only CSV is still useful as a "we ran the report and got nothing" artefact.

- **Variance trend CSV** (`GET /admin/reports/variance-trend?format=csv[&days=N]`):
  - Same data source as the HTML branch (`_load_trend_rows(db, days=days)`); same role gate (Manager + Office; Workshop / pending / anon blocked by the existing `Depends(require_role(...))`).
  - **Headers** (9 columns mirroring the HTML table one-for-one): `stock_take_id`, `scope`, `scheduled_for`, `completed_at`, `lines_with_variance`, `positive_variance`, `negative_variance_abs`, `net_variance`, `abs_variance`.
  - One row per stock take; no totals row in the CSV (the receiver can sum the rows themselves; emitting a totals row mid-data confuses downstream tools that expect every row to have the same shape).
  - **Filename**: `variance_trend_{days}d.csv` so the window is self-documenting in the receiver's downloads folder.
  - `?days=foo` silently coerces to default 90 (filename and content match) — same posture as the HTML branch.
  - New `_csv_rows_for_trend(rows)` helper maps the view-shape to a list-of-lists.
  - Decimal scale wart inherited from R4: `variance` reads back at the column's scale 4, so the CSV cell carries `"3.0000"` not `"3"`. Same wart as the HTML view; spreadsheet receivers read both as the same number.

- **PO list CSV** (`GET /admin/purchase-orders?format=csv[&status_filter=...]`):
  - Same data source as the HTML branch; same role gate.
  - **Headers** (6 columns): `po_id`, `supplier`, `supplier_archived`, `status`, `line_count`, `created_at`. The `supplier_archived` cell renders as the literal string `"yes"` / `"no"` (not `"True"` / `"False"`) because spreadsheet receivers find yes/no easier to filter on.
  - **Filename**: `purchase_orders_{status_filter}.csv` (e.g. `purchase_orders_all.csv`, `purchase_orders_draft.csv`).
  - Status filter applies to the CSV the same way it applies to HTML.
  - New `_po_list_csv_rows(rows)` helper maps the view-shape to a list-of-lists with the yes/no pre-coercion.
  - The `format` parameter on `list_purchase_orders` shadows the Python `format()` builtin in the function body but the function never calls it; trade-off accepted vs. a more contrived name like `as_format`.

- **Templates** — one new test-id per page:
  - `variance_trend.html` gains a `<a data-testid="variance-trend-csv-link" href="/admin/reports/variance-trend?format=csv&days={{ days }}">Download CSV</a>` link inline with the window form. Preserves the active `days` so a user who widened the window gets a CSV of the same window.
  - `purchase_orders_list.html` gains a `<a data-testid="po-list-csv-link" href="/admin/purchase-orders?format=csv&status_filter={{ status_filter }}">Download CSV</a>` link inline with the status filter. Preserves the active `status_filter`.

- **Role enforcement preserved**: the CSV branch is *inside* the existing routes, so the `Depends(require_role(Role.MANAGER, Role.OFFICE))` already blocks Workshop + pending and anon hits 401 before reaching the format check. Pinned for both surfaces.

- **Read-only invariant preserved**: GET-CSV writes no audit row (pinned for both surfaces).

- **No CSV-injection mitigation applied.** A cell value starting with `=` / `+` / `-` / `@` could be interpreted as a spreadsheet formula. v1 risk model: all-internal users (Workshop is server-side blocked from these routes); the data is workshop inventory typed by managers; CSV recipients are colleagues who can already read the data via the HTML view. Documented in `app/csv_export.py`'s module docstring; flagged for a polish slice if the threat model changes. The mitigation (prepending a single quote to fields starting with those chars) is a one-line change in `_coerce_cell` if needed.

- **Test coverage** (55 new tests):
  - Unit (`tests/unit/test_csv_export.py` 21 new):
    - `TestCsvResponse` (14): media_type carries charset; Content-Disposition has filename; filename is sanitised in the header; empty rows emits header-only; header + data rows round-trip cleanly; CRLF line terminator (no bare LF); None becomes empty string; Decimal serialises via `str()`; int serialises; datetime uses isoformat; date uses isoformat; embedded comma is quoted; embedded quote is doubled (RFC 4180); embedded newline is quoted.
    - `TestSafeFilename` (7): ASCII alnum passes through; underscore / dash / dot preserved; whitespace replaced; quotes replaced; semicolons replaced; slashes / backslashes replaced; non-ASCII replaced.
  - Integration — variance trend (`tests/integration/test_reports_routes.py` 17 new):
    - `TestVarianceTrendCsvRoleEnforcement` (5): anon / pending / Workshop blocked; Manager / Office allowed.
    - `TestVarianceTrendCsvHeaders` (4): Content-Type carries `text/csv; charset=utf-8`; default filename `variance_trend_90d.csv`; custom window filename `variance_trend_30d.csv`; bad days coerces to default in the filename too.
    - `TestVarianceTrendCsvBody` (4): empty emits header-only; one stock take produces one data row with the right cells; days filter applies to CSV (100-day-old completion absent at default, present at `?days=200`); newest-first ordering preserved.
    - `TestVarianceTrendCsvHtmlBranch` (2): blank format renders HTML; unknown format renders HTML.
    - `TestVarianceTrendCsvReadOnly` (1): GET-CSV writes no audit row.
    - `TestVarianceTrendCsvLink` (1): HTML page renders the `variance-trend-csv-link` with the active `days` preserved in the href.
  - Integration — PO list (`tests/integration/test_purchase_orders_routes.py` 17 new):
    - `TestPOListCsvRoleEnforcement` (5): anon / pending / Workshop blocked; Manager / Office allowed.
    - `TestPOListCsvHeaders` (3): Content-Type carries `text/csv; charset=utf-8`; default filename `purchase_orders_all.csv`; status-filtered filename `purchase_orders_draft.csv`.
    - `TestPOListCsvBody` (5): empty emits header-only; one PO produces one data row with the right cells (including `"no"` for non-archived supplier); archived supplier renders `"yes"`; status filter applies to CSV; newest-first ordering preserved.
    - `TestPOListCsvHtmlBranch` (2): blank format renders HTML; unknown format renders HTML.
    - `TestPOListCsvReadOnly` (1): GET-CSV writes no audit row.
    - `TestPOListCsvLink` (1): HTML page renders the `po-list-csv-link` with the active `status_filter` preserved in the href.

- pytest unit + integration: 1477 passing (was 1422, +55)

**R4 — Stock-take variance trend report (DoD #7 polish, MISSION §3 "Stock-take variance trends"):** new module `app/reports.py` mounted at `/admin/reports`. One route in this slice (R5 CSV export will live alongside). New template `variance_trend.html`. Dashboard link `dashboard-variance-trend-link` added to `dashboard.html` near the top-consumed section.

- **Route:** `GET /admin/reports/variance-trend[?days=N]` for **Manager + Office** (Workshop + pending → 401/403; anon 401 — same posture as R1's dashboard route per MISSION §3 "Workshop... cannot see aggregated cost data or reports"). Read-only — no audit, no mutations, no engine touches.
  - `days` query param: integer in `[1, 365]`, default 90. Out-of-range / non-int → silent coerce to 90 (same posture as R1's `top_days`). The form pre-fills with the *coerced* value.
  - Filters: stock takes where `completed_at IS NOT NULL AND completed_at >= now() - days`. Scheduled / in-progress stock takes excluded.
  - Per-stock-take aggregation: only `committed=True` lines with non-zero `variance` contribute. Aggregates: `lines_with_variance` (count), `positive_variance` (sum of variance > 0), `negative_variance_abs` (sum of `abs(variance)` where variance < 0), `net_variance` (signed sum), `abs_variance` (sum of absolute values). The invariant `abs_variance == positive + negative_abs` is pinned by `TestAggregateLines::test_abs_equals_positive_plus_negative_abs`.
  - Totals card across all rows: `stock_take_count` + the same five aggregates.
  - Ordering: `completed_at DESC, id DESC` — newest stock take first.

- **Why "committed only"**: a `StockTakeLine` carries a `variance` value the moment the operator types a count (ST2 writes it) — but until ST3 commits, no adjustment movement exists in the cost engine. The report aggregates **what was actioned**, not "what was observed but not yet adjusted". The audit log of `stock_take.committed` rows is the canonical record this report rolls up; uncommitted lines belong on the in-progress detail page, not on a trend report. Documented in module + helper docstrings; pinned by `TestAggregateLines::test_uncommitted_lines_excluded` + `TestVarianceTrendAggregation::test_uncommitted_lines_excluded`.

- **Helpers** (`app/reports.py`, all pure):
  - `_coerce_days(raw) -> int` — same shape as R1's `_coerce_top_days`. Default 90, range [1, 365].
  - `_window_cutoff(days) -> datetime` — `now(UTC) - timedelta(days=days)`.
  - `_aggregate_lines(lines) -> dict` — pure rollup over a list of `StockTakeLine` Python objects (no DB; testable in isolation).
  - `_combine_aggregates(rows) -> dict` — sums per-stock-take aggregates into a totals dict.
  - `_scope_label(st, *, node, location)` — local copy of `app.stock_takes._scope_label` to keep the modules decoupled. Same shape; if the rule changes, both must move in lockstep (acceptable duplication-tax at v1 scale per the existing `_is_leaf` precedent).
  - `_load_trend_rows(db, *, days)` — three round-trips: completed stock takes in window + batched node lookup + batched location lookup + batched lines fetch. Lines grouped in Python by `stock_take_id`. At v1 scale (a stock take a quarter, tens of lines per take) sub-millisecond.

- **Templates / test-ids** (`variance_trend.html`):
  - Heading: `variance-trend-heading` ("Stock-take variance trend").
  - Window form: `variance-trend-form` (GET), `variance-trend-days-input` (number, min=1, max=365, value=current `days`), `variance-trend-days-submit`. Pre-fills with the coerced value.
  - Totals card (always rendered): `variance-trend-totals` block with `variance-trend-stock-take-count`, `variance-trend-total-lines-with-variance`, `variance-trend-total-positive`, `variance-trend-total-negative-abs`, `variance-trend-total-net`, `variance-trend-total-abs`. Renders zeros when the table is empty rather than hiding (so the manager always sees the framing).
  - Per-stock-take table: `variance-trend-table` with per-row `variance-trend-row` (`data-stock-take-id`). Cells: `variance-trend-row-id` (link to detail), `variance-trend-row-scope`, `variance-trend-row-scheduled-for`, `variance-trend-row-completed-at`, `variance-trend-row-lines-with-variance`, `variance-trend-row-positive`, `variance-trend-row-negative-abs`, `variance-trend-row-net`, `variance-trend-row-abs`.
  - Empty state: `variance-trend-empty` (with the days count interpolated for context).

- **Dashboard wiring**: `<a data-testid="dashboard-variance-trend-link" href="/admin/reports/variance-trend">View stock-take variance trend →</a>` block in `dashboard.html` between the at-a-glance card row and the top-consumed section. No new aggregation on the dashboard. Visible to Manager / Office / Admin (Workshop never sees the dashboard route at all).

- **No new nav link.** The report is reachable via the dashboard link only. Adding a "Reports" nav entry would need at least two children (R5 will land soon); a single-child nav entry would clutter the nav for marginal gain. Documented in self-critique. The route URL is bookmarkable / shareable.

- **Engine isolation**: read-only. No `StockMovement`, `CostLayer`, `CostLayerConsumption`, or `Item.current_qty` touches. Pinned by `TestVarianceTrendReadOnly::test_get_writes_no_audit` (which compares pre/post audit row counts to confirm zero writes).

- **Test coverage** (`tests/unit/test_reports.py` 18 + `tests/integration/test_reports_routes.py` 21 + `tests/e2e/test_stock_takes_e2e.py` walk extension):
  - Unit (18):
    - `TestCoerceDays` (8): blank / None / non-int / below-min / above-max → 90; valid / min / max pass through.
    - `TestAggregateLines` (8): empty list zero; uncommitted lines excluded; zero-variance committed excluded; None-variance excluded; only-positive sum + count; only-negative `negative_abs` sum + count; mixed (pos + neg + zero + uncommitted) splits correctly; abs == positive + negative_abs invariant.
    - `TestCombineAggregates` (2): empty list zero with count 0; sum across two rows.
  - Integration (21):
    - Role enforcement (6): anon 401; pending 403; Workshop 403; Office / Manager / Admin 200.
    - Empty state (3): no stock takes → empty visible + totals zero; only-scheduled excluded; in-progress (started but not completed) excluded.
    - Window filter (4): recent within default 90-day window visible; 100-day-old completion excluded by default; same 100-day-old visible with `?days=200`; bad `?days=foo` silently coerces to 90 (form pre-fills with `value="90"`).
    - Aggregation (3): mixed positive + negative variance lines split across the per-side cells (3, 5, -2, 8); uncommitted lines excluded (zeros despite a `variance=3` line); zero-variance committed lines excluded.
    - Totals (2): two stock takes sum across the totals card; newest-first ordering by `completed_at DESC` (verified by string-position comparison of the row markup).
    - Read-only invariant (1): GET writes no audit row.
    - Dashboard wiring (2): manager / office both see the variance-trend link on the dashboard.
  - E2E walk extension (in-place): after the existing ST3 commit leg lands the completed stock take with `current_qty=48.0000`, office navigates via `nav-dashboard` to the dashboard, clicks `dashboard-variance-trend-link`, lands on `/admin/reports/variance-trend`, asserts: 1 row visible with `data-stock-take-id` matching the just-committed take, totals `variance-trend-stock-take-count="1"`, totals `variance-trend-total-negative-abs` contains "2", row `variance-trend-row-net` contains "-2", row `variance-trend-row-lines-with-variance="1"`. Cleanup unchanged.

- ruff: clean (`app tests`)
- mypy: clean (strict on `app/`, 26 source files — `app/reports.py` is the +1)
- pytest unit + integration: 1422 passing (was 1383, +39)
- Playwright e2e: 14 passing (no count change; existing walk extended in-place)

**ST3 — Commit variances as adjustment movements (DoD #5 closing slice):** new route `POST /admin/stock-takes/{stock_take_id}/commit` on `app/stock_takes.py` for **Manager + Office** (Workshop + pending → 401/403; anon 401). Walks every line with non-zero variance, builds one `StockMovement(type=ADJUSTMENT)` per line (with `stock_take_id` populated — first slice to write a non-null value), routes through the cost engine: `record_receipt(..., source=POSITIVE_ADJUSTMENT)` for positive variance; `consume_fifo` for negative variance. Flips `StockTakeLine.committed=True` per line, sets `StockTake.completed_at = now()`, writes one `stock_take.committed` audit row carrying `before={"completed_at": null}` + `after={"completed_at": <ISO>, "movements": [...]}` (one entry per non-zero-variance line: line_id, item_id, movement_id, variance, direction, unit_cost or None, total_cost). 303s back to detail page (now in completed state).

- **Engine ownership maintained:** the route never mutates `cost_layers.qty_remaining`, `item.current_qty`, `movement.total_cost`, or `cost_layer_consumptions.*` directly — `record_receipt` and `consume_fifo` are the single owners. Caller pattern matches M2 / M3 / M4 verbatim: `db.add(movement); db.flush(); engine_call(...)`. The new movements stamp `stock_take_id = st.id` so a future "movements caused by stock takes" report can join cleanly. The `reason` field is `f"stock take #{st.id}"` per MISSION §3's "Adjustment movements... required reason" — the per-line variance + direction attribution lives in the audit row's `movements` list (uniform `reason` across all lines in a commit; per-line nuance is in the audit).
- **Validation order** (all 400 *before* any DB write — atomic): (1) PO exists (404); (2) `_can_commit(st)` rejects scheduled / completed; (3) `_lines_with_non_zero_variance(rows)` non-empty (400 "no variances to commit" — committing an all-zero stock take would write a confusing audit row; force the operator to acknowledge with a no-op); (4) per-positive-variance-line `unit_cost_<line_id>` parses as non-negative Decimal (blank → 400 with `required=True` on positive variance lines; negative-variance lines silently ignore the input — consumption price is per-layer, same as M3 / M4 negative).
- **Atomic-on-raise contract**: insufficient stock on a negative-variance line raises `InsufficientStockError` *before any layer is mutated* (M1 invariant). The route catches it, calls `db.rollback()` (drops every successful movement / layer / consumption from the same transaction — including any positive-variance lines processed earlier in the loop), reloads the stock take, and re-renders the detail page with HTTP 400 + a `<p data-testid="stock-take-commit-error" role="alert">` block + the operator's typed `unit_cost_<id>` inputs preserved in `commit_form_values`. Same shape as M3's stock-out error path. Pinned by `TestCommitInsufficientStock::test_partial_failure_leaves_no_state` — even if the first (positive) line would have succeeded in isolation, the second (negative) line's shortage rolls the whole transaction back.
- **Default unit cost** (positive variance lines): pre-fills the `unit_cost_<line_id>` input with the most-recent layer's `unit_cost` for the item (`SELECT unit_cost FROM cost_layers WHERE item_id=X ORDER BY received_at DESC, id DESC LIMIT 1`). Reuses the same lookup pattern as PO2's `_last_unit_cost`. Items with no prior layers render an empty input — operator must type a cost.
- **Audit shape** — `stock_take.committed`: `before={"completed_at": null}`, `after={"completed_at": <ISO>, "movements": [{line_id, item_id, movement_id, variance (str), direction ("increase" | "decrease"), unit_cost (str | None — None for decreases), total_cost (str)}, ...]}`. Decimals stringified via `str(decimal)`. The `total_cost` carries the engine's compound-multiplication scale: `Decimal("3.0000") × Decimal("2.50") = Decimal("7.500000")` (scale 6 for positive — qty is column-scale-4 × form-scale-2); `Decimal("3.0000") × Decimal("2.0000") = Decimal("6.00000000")` (scale 8 for negative — both come from the column at scale 4). Same wart as M3 / M4's audit shape; pinned with explanatory comments.
- **Helpers** (added to `app/stock_takes.py`): `_can_commit(st)` (mirror of `_can_count`); `_last_unit_cost(db, item_id)` (newest layer lookup, copy of PO2's helper); `_parse_unit_cost_for_commit(raw, *, line_id, required)` (blank → None when optional, 400 when required; non-numeric / negative reject; zero allowed); `_lines_with_non_zero_variance(rows)` (filter out zero-variance + uncounted lines).
- **`_detail_context` extended**: when status is `in_progress`, the context now carries a `commit_lines` list (one entry per non-zero-variance line with `direction` + `unit_cost_default` pre-filled). Optional `commit_error` + `commit_form_values` parameters drive the insufficient-stock re-render. The `lines` view dict gains an `is_committed` flag so the completed branch can render a per-line "Yes" marker.
- **Templates** (`stock_take_detail.html`):
  - In-progress branch grows a new "Commit" sub-section below the count form. Test-ids: `stock-take-commit-form`, `stock-take-commit-table` with per-row `stock-take-commit-row` (`data-line-id`, `data-item-id`, `data-direction`), per-line `stock-take-commit-sku` / `stock-take-commit-name` / `stock-take-commit-variance`; positive variance rows render `stock-take-commit-unit-cost-input` (pre-filled from most-recent layer); negative variance rows render `stock-take-commit-unit-cost-na` ("—") instead. `stock-take-commit-submit` clicks through to the route.
  - When variances are zero across the board, the commit form is replaced by `<p data-testid="stock-take-no-variances-note">` — operator sees an explanation instead of a hidden form.
  - Insufficient-stock error renders `<p data-testid="stock-take-commit-error" role="alert">` block at top of the in-progress branch.
  - Completed branch's per-line `stock-take-count-row` gains `data-committed="true|false"` attribute + a 7th cell `data-testid="stock-take-line-committed"` showing "Yes" or "—".
- **No "uncommit" route.** Once `completed_at` is set the row is read-only — no UI to undo. Corrections must be made via fresh manual-adjustment movements (M4) outside the stock-take flow. Same posture as PO5's "no un-receive". MISSION §3 doesn't require unbreaking the state machine; the audit log preserves both events.
- **Test coverage** (`tests/unit/test_stock_takes.py` 18 new + `tests/integration/test_stock_takes_routes.py` 31 new + `tests/e2e/test_stock_takes_e2e.py` walk extended in-place):
  - Unit (18): `TestCanCommit` (3) — scheduled false / in_progress true / completed false; `TestLastUnitCost` (4) — no layers None / single layer / multi-layer newest wins / other items excluded; `TestParseUnitCostForCommit` (7) — blank-optional None / blank-required 400 / whitespace-only-optional None / valid decimal / zero allowed / negative 400 / non-numeric 400; `TestLinesWithNonZeroVariance` (3) — zero excluded / None excluded / mixed positive+negative kept.
  - Integration role enforcement (5): anon 401, pending 403, Workshop 403, Office 303 (negative happy path), Manager 303 (negative happy path).
  - Validation (8): unknown 404, scheduled 400, completed 400, no-variances 400, uncounted-only 400, negative unit_cost 400, non-numeric unit_cost 400, blank unit_cost on positive 400, failed-validation-writes-no-state.
  - Positive happy path (4): creates `StockMovement(type=ADJUSTMENT, stock_take_id, reason="stock take #N")` + `CostLayer(source=POSITIVE_ADJUSTMENT)`; `line.committed=True` + `st.completed_at` set within ±5s; `current_qty` bumped; zero unit_cost allowed.
  - Negative happy path (3): creates movement + `CostLayerConsumption` rows; `current_qty` decremented; multi-layer FIFO consume splits across two layers (4 from old @ 2 + 3 from new @ 3 = 17.0000).
  - Mixed (1): three lines (positive + negative + zero). Only the two non-zero ones get movements + `committed=True`; zero-variance line stays `committed=False` with no movement.
  - Insufficient stock (2): single-line negative shortage rolls back atomically (no movement / no consumption / no audit / `completed_at` still None); multi-line where the second line shortages rolls back the *first* line's positive adjustment too.
  - Audit shape (2): `stock_take.committed` action with before / after; positive carries `direction=increase` + `unit_cost="2.50"` + `total_cost="7.500000"`; negative carries `direction=decrease` + `unit_cost=null` + `total_cost="4.00000000"`.
  - Commit-form rendering (5): in_progress with variances shows commit form + per-line row + unit_cost input for positive only; in_progress with no variances shows the no-variances note; completed branch hides the commit form; default unit_cost pre-fills from most-recent layer (`value="4.2500"`); negative variance renders the `-na` marker instead of an input.
  - Committed badge on completed (1): `data-committed="true"` + `stock-take-line-committed` cell.
  - E2E walk extension: after the existing variance leg shows `-2`, office sees the commit form with `data-direction="decrease"` row + the `-na` marker; clicks `stock-take-commit-submit`; lands on completed detail page (`data-status="completed"`, no commit form, line carries `data-committed="true"`); manager re-visits `/admin/items/{id}/in` and confirms `current_qty` dropped from 50.0000 to 48.0000 (engine consumed 2 units FIFO from the seeded 50@2.50 layer).

**Check-in flow (C3):** extends `app/checkouts.py` with one new route `POST /admin/items/checkouts/{checkout_id}/return` and an inline check-in form per row in `checkout_form.html`'s status block. Closes the workshop half of DoD #4 — workshop can now both check out and check in. Manager "currently out / overdue" cross-item view (C4) is the last gate before DoD #4 ticks.

- **Route**: `POST /admin/items/checkouts/{checkout_id}/return` (Manager + Office + Workshop; pending + anon → 401/403). Path layout sits beside the existing `/{item_id}/checkout` (literal `checkouts/...` is a different path shape — 3 segments after the prefix vs. 2 — so no FastAPI route-collision risk; same precedent as `item_units` mounting `units/{unit_id}/...` next to `{item_id}/units`). Workshop can return *any* user's checkout (no "borrower-only" rule in v1 — tools get returned to whoever's at the bench; the audit row's `actor_id` records who hit submit while the original `Checkout.user_id` records the borrower).
- **Validation order** (all 400 *before* any DB write — atomic):
  1. Checkout exists (404).
  2. `returned_at IS NULL` (400 — "this check-out is already closed"). Idempotency rejection mirrors PO2b's `_require_draft` for already-cancelled POs and C2's "already-open" reject.
  3. `condition_note`: stripped, blank → no-change to the existing note; non-blank → merged. ≤ 2000 chars on the *merged* total else 400 (the existing-and-fresh combined check; the existing has already passed validation but a long-existing + long-fresh can still overflow).
- **Note merging** via `_merge_condition_note(prev, fresh)`: blank fresh → prev unchanged; existing-and-fresh both present → `f"{prev}\n---\n{fresh}"` (markdown-ish separator, plain-text-readable); fresh-with-no-prev → fresh as-is. The append-don't-overwrite posture preserves the C2 "what state did this go out in" alongside the C3 "what state did it come back in" without a new column.
- **Mutation** (single transaction): `co.returned_at = datetime.now(UTC)`; `co.condition_note = merged`; `record_audit("checkout.returned", before={"returned_at": None, "condition_note": <prev>}, after={"returned_at": <ISO>, "condition_note": <merged>, "item_id", "item_unit_id", "user_id"})`; `db.commit()`. The `before` is a partial diff (only the changed fields on the Checkout row), consistent with M3 / M4 / PO2b audit shapes; the `after` carries the changed fields plus the FK trio so a future "who returned what when" report doesn't need a join back. ISO timestamps via `.isoformat()` (matches every prior datetime audit value in the codebase).
- **Engine isolation** (preserved from C2): no `StockMovement` written; `item.current_qty` unchanged; no `cost_layer` / `cost_layer_consumption` rows touched. Pinned by `TestCheckinEngineIsolation::test_no_stock_movement_on_return`. A returned tool still belongs to UC; valuation and stock level haven't changed.
- **Template — status-block per-row inline form** (`checkout_form.html`): each `checkout-open-row` now carries a 5th cell with a small `<form method="post" action="/admin/items/checkouts/{co.id}/return">` containing a hidden `csrf_token`, a `<details>`-wrapped optional `<textarea name="condition_note">` (collapsed by default to keep the row compact), and a "Check in" `<button>`. Per-row test-ids: `checkout-return-form` (with `data-checkout-id="{{ co.id }}"`), `checkout-return-note-input`, `checkout-return-submit`. The `<details>` wrapper means a no-note check-in is one click; a with-note check-in is one click on the summary + type + one click on the button.
- **Post-return redirect** targets the originating `/admin/items/{item.id}/checkout` page so the user sees the status block re-shrink (qty-tracked: block disappears entirely; unique-tracked: the just-returned unit's row is gone and the unit is back in the available `<select>`). Same redirect-to-form pattern as C2's POST.
- **Test coverage** (`tests/integration/test_checkouts_routes.py` 22 new + `tests/e2e/test_checkouts_e2e.py` walk extended in-place):
  - Role enforcement (6): anon POST 401; pending POST 403; Workshop returning a Manager's checkout 303 (cross-actor case); Office / Manager / Admin POST 303.
  - Validation (4): unknown checkout 404; already-returned 400 (`returned_at` unchanged + no audit); merged note > 2000 chars 400 (note + separator + fresh pushes past the column ceiling — existing 1500 + fresh 700 + 5-char separator = 2205); fresh-alone > 2000 chars 400.
  - Qty-tracked happy path (2): creates `Checkout(item_unit_id=None)` returned by another workshop; `returned_at` within ±1s of now; redirect target; audit row carries `before={returned_at: None, condition_note: None}` + `after={returned_at: ISO, condition_note: None, item_id, item_unit_id: None, user_id: borrower.id}`; flash includes "Checked in" + item name.
  - Unique-tracked happy path (2): creates `Checkout(item_unit_id=N)` returned by a workshop; audit `after.item_unit_id` carries the unit id; flash includes the unit serial + item name.
  - Note merging (4): blank fresh → existing preserved; fresh-with-no-existing → set to fresh; fresh-with-existing → `prev\n---\nfresh`; whitespace-only fresh → existing preserved (treated as blank by `_parse_optional_note`'s strip).
  - Engine isolation (1): `current_qty` seeded at 42.0000 stays at 42.0000; no `StockMovement` row exists post-return.
  - Form re-shrinks (3): qty-tracked status block + return form present after checkout, gone after return + submit re-appears; unique-tracked unit value disappears from the `<select>` body after checkout, comes back after return; status block carries per-row `checkout-return-form` with `data-checkout-id` + the right action URL + the note-input + submit-button test-ids.
  - E2E walk extension (in-place): after the existing C2 leg lands the open-row with CHK-A in the status block, the workshop user clicks the row's `details summary` to expand the note input, fills "returned clean, ready for next pour", clicks `checkout-return-submit`, lands back on `/admin/items/{id}/checkout`, asserts the flash contains "Checked in" + "Wax mould A" + "CHK-A", `checkout-status-block` is hidden (no open rows), and CHK-A is back in the available `<select>` (along with CHK-B). Cleanup unchanged — manager archives item + category at the end.

**Check-out flow (C2):** new module `app/checkouts.py` with two routes mounted at `/admin/items` and a new template `checkout_form.html`. Workshop's first non-cost-engine write surface — a checkout is custody, not consumption.

- **Routes** (Manager + Office + Workshop; pending + anon → 401/403):
  - `GET /admin/items/{item_id}/checkout` — render the form. For unique-tracked items, the form contains a unit `<select>` of *available* units (active + status=available + not-currently-in-an-open-checkout). For qty-tracked items, no unit select. A `checkout-status-block` renders above the form when at least one open checkout exists for the item.
  - `POST /admin/items/{item_id}/checkout` — validate + create one `Checkout` row + write a `checkout.created` audit row + redirect 303 with a flash. Workshop self-checkouts to themselves (no "checkout on behalf of" UI).
- **Engine isolation**: the route never calls the cost engine, never writes a `StockMovement`, never touches `cost_layers.qty_remaining` / `item.current_qty`. A checked-out tool still belongs to UC; the cost-engine invariants are unaffected. Pinned by `TestEngineIsolation::test_no_stock_movement_or_qty_change` (item.current_qty stays at the pre-checkout value across the POST).
- **Validation order** (all 400 *before* any DB write — atomic):
  1. Item exists (404), not archived (400), `requires_checkout=True` (400 — "this item is not flagged for check-out").
  2. `expected_return`: blank → None; ISO `YYYY-MM-DD` else 400 (parsed via `date.fromisoformat`, then upgraded to a UTC-midnight `datetime` because the column is `DateTime(tz)`).
  3. `condition_note`: stripped, blank → None, ≤ 2000 chars else 400.
  4. **Unique-tracked**: `item_unit_id` required (blank 400), parses as int (non-numeric 400), references an active `ItemUnit` *on this item* (mismatched-item / archived / status=lost / unknown all reject), and not currently in an open checkout (race — 400).
  5. **Qty-tracked**: `item_unit_id` is silently ignored on input; `Checkout.item_unit_id` is written as None. At-most-one-open-per-item is enforced by querying `Checkout WHERE item_id=X AND item_unit_id IS NULL AND returned_at IS NULL` (400 if a row exists).
- **Audit shape** — `checkout.created`: `before=None`, `after={item_id, item_unit_id (or None), user_id, checked_out_at (ISO with TZ), expected_return (ISO with TZ | None), condition_note}`. Decimal-free shape; ISO timestamps via `.isoformat()` (matches every prior datetime audit value in the codebase).
- **Helpers** (in `app/checkouts.py`): `_open_checkout_unit_ids(db, item_id)` returns the set of unit ids currently out for the item; `_has_open_qty_checkout(db, item_id)` is the qty-tracked variant; `_available_units(db, item_id)` returns active+available+not-currently-out units ordered by serial; `_open_checkouts(db, item_id)` returns view-shaped rows with the actor's email + the unit's serial (when set) for the status block. All four are pure reads — no side effects, no Request, no HTTPException.
- **Form rendering**: `is_unique` flag drives the conditional unit select. `can_submit` hides the submit button when there's no path forward (qty-tracked already out / unique-tracked with zero available units), surfacing a `checkout-no-submit-note` instead. The form's `<select>` populates from `_available_units`; the open-checkout status block populates from `_open_checkouts`. After a successful POST, the same GET re-renders with the just-checked-out unit moved from the select into the status block — pinned by `TestCheckoutUniqueHappyPath::test_picked_unit_disappears_from_next_form`.
- **Template / test-ids** (`checkout_form.html`): heading `checkout-form-heading`; summary `item-current-qty` + `item-requires-checkout-badge`; status block `checkout-status-block` with per-row `checkout-open-row` + `checkout-open-actor` / `checkout-open-since` / `checkout-open-unit`; form `checkout-form` + hidden CSRF; conditional `checkout-unit-input` (unique-tracked only); `checkout-expected-return-input` + `checkout-note-input` + `checkout-submit` (or `checkout-no-submit-note` when nothing is checkout-able).
- **Link surfaces**: `items_form.html` and `item_detail.html` each gain a `data-testid="checkout-link"` "Check out →" link, gated on `not item.archived_at AND item.requires_checkout`. Unflagged items hide the link; archived items hide it too. Pinned across `TestCheckoutLinkVisibility` (4 tests).
- **Test coverage** (`tests/integration/test_checkouts_routes.py` 48 + `tests/e2e/test_checkouts_e2e.py` 1):
  - Role enforcement (11): anon GET / POST 401; pending GET / POST 403; Workshop / Office / Manager / Admin all 200 GET / 303 POST. Includes a `TestCheckoutValidation` `test_failed_validation_writes_no_audit` for the no-write-on-failure invariant.
  - Form rendering (9): qty-tracked has no unit input + has CSRF + form + submit + expected_return + note inputs; unique-tracked lists active+available units only (asserted by checking for `value="<id>"` in the rendered body); unique-tracked excludes archived units; excludes lost units; excludes currently-open units; status block renders when an open checkout exists; status block hidden when none exist; unknown 404; archived 400; non-flagged item 400.
  - Validation matrix (14): bad expected_return; blank unit-id (unique); non-numeric unit-id; unknown unit-id; unit-on-different-item 400; archived unit 400; lost unit 400; already-open unique unit 400; already-open qty-tracked item 400; oversize condition_note 400; archived item POST 400; non-flagged item POST 400; unknown item POST 404; failed validation writes no audit + no checkout row.
  - Qty-tracked happy path (5): creates `Checkout(item_unit_id=None)`; user_id=actor.id; checked_out_at within ±1s of now; expected_return parsed (date round-trips); condition_note preserved; blank expected_return → None; blank condition_note → None; audit shape carries the seven keys with the right values; flash visible after the redirect.
  - Unique-tracked happy path (3): creates `Checkout(item_unit_id=N)`; audit row carries `item_unit_id`; the picked unit disappears from the next form render's `<select>`.
  - Form link visibility (4): items_form shows the link for active flagged items; hides for non-flagged; hides for archived; item_detail shows the link.
  - Engine isolation (1): no `StockMovement` written + `item.current_qty` unchanged across a POST that sets a non-zero starting `current_qty`.
  - E2E walk: pending workshop + pending manager promoted by admin → manager creates a category + a flagged unique-tracked item with two units (CHK-A, CHK-B) → workshop signs in, navigates `nav-items` → `item-row` → `view-item` → `checkout-link` → `/admin/items/{id}/checkout` → picks CHK-A + fills 2026-06-15 + a note + submits → asserts flash contains the item name + unit serial + status block now lists the open checkout with the workshop's email + the next form's `<select>` no longer offers CHK-A but still offers CHK-B. Cleanup archives the item + category.

**Per-item `requires_checkout` flag UI + checkouts schema (C1):** lays the foundation for DoD #4. New ORM model `Checkout` in `app/models.py` mirroring MISSION §6 columns: `id, item_id (FK items RESTRICT NOT NULL), item_unit_id (FK item_units RESTRICT nullable), user_id (FK users SET NULL nullable), checked_out_at (DateTime tz NOT NULL), expected_return (DateTime tz nullable), returned_at (DateTime tz nullable), condition_note (String 2000 nullable), created_at, updated_at`. No status enum: open vs returned is derived from `returned_at IS NULL`. Migration `0013_create_checkouts.py` creates the table + four indexes (per item / item_unit / user / returned_at). FK posture: `user_id` SET NULL so a hard-deleted user (rare; soft-delete is the v1 path) doesn't cascade through history; `item_id` and `item_unit_id` RESTRICT so a checkout row blocks any future hard-delete path on the parent. No `archived_at` — checkout rows are part of the audit trail; corrections are made via new return records.

- **Items list filter** (`GET /admin/items?requires_checkout=yes`): new query param filters to items with `requires_checkout=True`. Anything other than the literal `"yes"` (blank, `"no"`, garbage) silently coerces to no filter — same posture as `show=active|archived`. The filter combines with `show=` so a manager can see archived flagged items via `?show=archived&requires_checkout=yes`.
- **Items list UI affordance**: new "Checkout?" column on the items table showing "Yes" for flagged items and "—" for unflagged, with `data-testid="item-requires-checkout"` per cell. New filter nav above the table with `data-testid="filter-all"` and `data-testid="filter-requires-checkout"` links — `aria-current="page"` flips to whichever is active. The "Requires checkout" link's href preserves the active `show` param; the "All items" link likewise so navigating between filters keeps the archived/active context.
- **Items form**: existing `requires_checkout` checkbox gains an `<em data-testid="item-requires-checkout-help">` note ("Track who has the item out and when it's due back.") so a manager seeing the field for the first time understands when to tick it.
- **No new routes** — the route surface for check-out / check-in lands in C2 / C3, and the manager "currently out / overdue" view in C4. C1's job is to land the foundation so those slices don't have to also ship a migration.

- **Test coverage** (`tests/unit/test_checkouts.py` 11 + `tests/integration/test_items_routes.py::TestRequiresCheckoutFlag` 10):
  - Model defaults (4): minimal open round-trip (qty-tracked, no item_unit, no expected_return, no condition_note); checkout with item_unit + expected_return + condition_note; returned checkout (`returned_at` set); long condition_note (1500 chars within the 2000-char column).
  - Foreign keys (5): `item_id` required (IntegrityError on commit); `checked_out_at` required; orphan `item_id` rejected with PRAGMA foreign_keys=ON; orphan `item_unit_id` rejected; `user_id` accepts NULL.
  - Returned derivation (2): open checkout has `returned_at IS NULL`; setting `returned_at` after creation works (no enum to bump in lockstep).
  - List filter + UI (10): list shows "Yes" for flagged + "—" for unflagged; list shows only "—" when no items flagged; `?requires_checkout=yes` filters to flagged only; blank does not filter; unrecognised value (`foo`) does not filter; `?requires_checkout=no` does not filter (2-state, not 3-state); filter nav links present with correct `aria-current` flip across views; filter combines with `?show=archived` (archived flagged item shown, archived non-flagged hidden); form renders the help note; filter nav preserves `show=archived` in both link hrefs.

**Reporting dashboard (R1):** new module `app/dashboard.py` with one route `GET /admin/dashboard` for **Manager + Office** (Admin via the bypass; Workshop + pending 403 — MISSION §3 "Workshop... cannot see aggregated cost data or reports"). Read-only — no mutations, no audit, no movement type, no new tables. New template `dashboard.html`. New `nav-dashboard` link in `base.html` for admin/manager/office.

- **Aggregations** (each is a single round-trip):
  - **Total inventory value**: `SUM(qty_remaining * unit_cost)` across active items' open `cost_layers` rows. Joins `cost_layers → items` and filters `items.archived_at IS NULL` so archived items don't inflate the figure. A fully-consumed layer (`qty_remaining=0`) contributes 0 by arithmetic — no extra filter needed.
  - **Low-stock count**: `COUNT(items)` where `archived_at IS NULL AND current_qty <= reorder_threshold`. Same WHERE clause as PO1's dashboard query.
  - **Open POs count**: `COUNT(purchase_orders)` where `status IN (draft, sent, partially_received)`. Adjacent context for the dashboard reader; not strictly DoD #7 but cheap and useful.
  - **Overdue checkouts**: hardcoded 0 with a `<small>` "checkouts not yet implemented" note. C-series will replace it; pinning the test-id `dashboard-overdue-checkouts` now means C-series doesn't have to re-template.
  - **Top consumed items**: `SUM(qty)` over `stock_movements WHERE type=OUT AND created_at >= now() - top_days` grouped by `item_id`, joined back to `items` for sku + name, ordered by sum desc + sku asc tiebreak, LIMIT 10. The window is `?top_days=N` (default 30; clamped to `[1, 365]`; non-int / out-of-range silently coerces to default — same posture as M6's pagination clamping).
  - **COGS**: `SUM(total_cost)` over `stock_movements WHERE id IN (SELECT DISTINCT movement_id FROM cost_layer_consumptions) AND created_at BETWEEN cogs_start AND cogs_end+1d` (so `end` is inclusive of the entire day). The consumption-row subquery is the canonical "did this movement drain layers" filter — covers OUT movements + negative-adjustment ADJUSTMENT movements (both go through `consume_fifo`). Adjustment increases create a layer and have no consumption rows, so they're correctly excluded. IN movements have `total_cost` set but no consumption rows. TRANSFER has neither. Bad-format ISO date in either query param 400s (same posture as PO2b's edit-date validation).

- **Route surface (1 route)**: `GET /admin/dashboard?[top_days=N&cogs_start=YYYY-MM-DD&cogs_end=YYYY-MM-DD]` — Manager + Office. The route runs five small queries and renders `dashboard.html` with the widget values + the active filter params (so the form re-renders pre-filled). The two filter forms (`dashboard-top-days-form` and `dashboard-cogs-form`) each carry the *other* param as a hidden input so submitting one form preserves the other's value.

- **Helpers** (in `app/dashboard.py`): `_coerce_top_days(raw)` → int (silent coerce on bad / out-of-range), `_parse_cogs_date(raw, *, field_name)` → `date | None` (400 on bad format; `None` / blank → `None` to use defaults), `_resolve_cogs_range(start, end)` → `(date, date)` (defaults: end=today, start=end-30d). All five aggregation helpers (`_total_inventory_value`, `_low_stock_count`, `_open_pos_count`, `_top_consumed`, `_cogs`) are pure DB reads — no side effects, no Request, no HTTPException.
