- **Decimal handling**: `func.coalesce(func.sum(...), 0)` returns a Decimal under SQLAlchemy's `Numeric(14,4)` round-trip but mypy types `scalar_one()` as `Any`. The two helpers (`_total_inventory_value` + `_cogs`) defensively branch: `if isinstance(total, Decimal): return total` else `return Decimal(str(total))`. The `Decimal(str(...))` path lands when SQLite reports the SUM as an int (the all-zero-rows case). Both paths produce a deterministic Decimal output with no precision loss.

- **Templates / test-ids**: new `dashboard.html` with five test-id surfaces — at-a-glance: `dashboard-heading`, `dashboard-total-value`, `dashboard-low-stock-count`, `dashboard-open-pos-count`, `dashboard-overdue-checkouts`. Top consumed: `dashboard-top-consumed-table` with per-row `dashboard-top-consumed-row` (carrying `data-item-id`) + cells `dashboard-top-consumed-sku` / `dashboard-top-consumed-name` / `dashboard-top-consumed-qty` / `dashboard-top-consumed-detail-link` + empty state `dashboard-top-consumed-empty`. Filter forms: `dashboard-top-days-form` + `dashboard-top-days-input` + `dashboard-top-days-submit` and `dashboard-cogs-form` + `dashboard-cogs-start-input` + `dashboard-cogs-end-input` + `dashboard-cogs-submit`. COGS card: `dashboard-cogs-amount`. `base.html` gains a `nav-dashboard` link (between Home and Suppliers) visible to Admin / Manager / Office; Workshop hidden. The `aria-current` is on `path == "/admin/dashboard" or startswith("/admin/dashboard/")` (same tightening pattern as PO2's `nav-reorder` fix).

- **Test coverage** (`tests/integration/test_dashboard_routes.py` 32 + `tests/integration/test_layout.py` 5 + `tests/e2e/test_dashboard_e2e.py` 1):
  - Role enforcement (6): anon 401; pending 403; Workshop 403; Manager / Office / Admin 200.
  - Total inventory value (5): empty zero; single layer with `total_value="25.0000"` (10 × 2.50 column-quantised); multi-item sum (10×2 + 5×3 = 35); archived item's layers excluded (only the active item contributes); fully-consumed layer (qty_remaining=0) contributes 0 + the new layer at 5×3 contributes 15.
  - Low-stock count (3): zero state; positive count (2 below + 1 above-threshold = 2); archived items excluded.
  - Open POs count (2): zero; counts draft + sent + partially_received but excludes received + cancelled (3 of 5 in the seed).
  - Top consumed (7): empty when no OUTs; orders by sum(qty) desc with tiebreak (B=20 > C=10 > A=5); window excludes 100-day-old OUT (default 30-day window); `?top_days=200` includes the 100-day-old OUT; `?top_days=foo` coerces to 30; `?top_days=99999` coerces to 30; TRANSFER movements not counted.
  - COGS (8): zero with no movements; sums OUT total_cost (3 × 2 = "6.0000"); sums ADJUSTMENT decreases AND excludes ADJUSTMENT increases (only the 2-unit decrease counts: 2 × 2 = "4.0000"); IN movements not counted (zero); date range filters old movements (default window picks only the recent OUT: 6.0000); explicit `?cogs_start=&cogs_end=` 90-day window picks up the 60-day-old OUT (7 × 2 = 14); bad `cogs_start` 400; bad `cogs_end` 400.
  - Read-only invariant (1): GET writes no audit row (compares pre/post audit ids).
  - Layout / nav (5): manager / office / admin nav-dashboard visible; workshop nav-dashboard hidden; `aria-current` on `/admin/dashboard` page sets it on the dashboard link.
  - E2E walk: a manager promoted from pending creates a category + item (threshold=0), stocks in 100 @ 2.50 (current_qty=100), stocks out 30 (current_qty=70), visits `/admin/dashboard` via the nav link, asserts: total value = 175.0000 (70 × 2.50), low-stock count = 0 (qty=70 > threshold=0), open POs count = 0, overdue checkouts = 0, top-consumed table has 1 row with sku=DASH-1 + qty=30.0000, COGS = 75.0000 (30 × 2.50), top-days input pre-fills with "30". Cleanup archives the item + category.

**Receive against a PO (PO5):** extends `app/purchase_orders.py` with two more routes on the existing `/admin/purchase-orders` prefix. `GET /admin/purchase-orders/{po_id}/receive` (Manager + Office; Workshop + pending 403) renders a receive form — per-line `received_<line_id>` (default empty / 0) + `cost_<line_id>` (default to line's `expected_unit_cost`) + per-row outstanding cell. `POST /admin/purchase-orders/{po_id}/receive` (async — per-line dynamic keys; same precedent as PO2b's edit) validates per-line, builds one `StockMovement(type=IN, po_id=po.id)` + one `CostLayer(source=PO_RECEIPT)` per line with received qty > 0 via `record_receipt`, increments `line.qty_received`, flips `po.status` based on cumulative state (RECEIVED if every line fully received else PARTIALLY_RECEIVED), writes a `purchase_order.received` audit row, commits, 303 to detail. Status guard: only `sent` + `partially_received` accept receipts (draft / received / cancelled all 400). The new migration `0012_add_stock_movements_po_id_fk.py` activates the FK that M1 deferred (`stock_movements.po_id` → `purchase_orders.id`, `ON DELETE RESTRICT`); SQLite-compat via `op.batch_alter_table`. Detail page (`purchase_order_detail.html`) gains a `data-testid="po-receive-link"` link in the read-only branch, gated on `is_receivable` (status in `(sent, partially_received)`).

- **Engine ownership maintained:** route never mutates `cost_layers.qty_remaining`, `item.current_qty`, or `movement.total_cost` directly — those are M1's invariants and `record_receipt` is the single owner. Caller pattern is M2's: `db.add(movement); db.flush(); record_receipt(...)`. Each line with received > 0 generates one movement + one cost layer with `source=CostLayerSource.PO_RECEIPT`. Lines with received == 0 generate no movement and no audit entry.
- **Validation order** (all 400 *before* any DB mutation — atomic): (1) PO exists (404); (2) `_require_receivable(po)` rejects draft / received / cancelled; (3) per-line first pass parses `received_<id>` (blank → 0; non-numeric / negative reject) and `cost_<id>` (only validated when received > 0; blank-with-qty rejects so the operator must affirm a price; non-numeric / negative reject); (4) per-line cumulative `line.qty_received + new_received <= line.qty_ordered` (over-receipt rejects). Only after every line passes does the second pass write movements + layers + audit. Failed validation writes nothing — `test_failed_validation_writes_no_state` pins this.
- **Cost only required when received > 0**: a line that's blank or 0 in the received column doesn't validate the cost field. The operator can leave the cost blank for lines that aren't arriving in this delivery; the route doesn't write a movement for them anyway. When received > 0, blank cost rejects (`test_blank_cost_with_qty_is_400`) — the operator must affirm a price even if it's the same as the expected. Zero cost is allowed on a non-zero received line (sample / gifted stock — same as M2 / M4).
- **No over-receipt**: cumulative `line.qty_received + new_received <= line.qty_ordered`. Two test scenarios pin both directions: `test_over_receipt_is_400` (single shot of 11 against ordered=10) and `test_over_receipt_after_partial_is_400` (first 6 of 10 lands; second 5 rejects because only 4 outstanding). The operator who orders 100 but expects to receive 110 must edit the qty_ordered first via PO2b's edit route — which is gated on draft status, so today's path is "record a manual stock-in for the +10 outside the PO". Documented in self-critique as an out-of-scope follow-up.
- **All-zero submit is a no-op** (no movement, no layer, no audit, no status change) — flashes "no receipts entered" + 303s back to detail. Two tests pin this: `test_all_zero_submit_writes_no_state` (no `received_*` keys at all) and `test_explicit_zero_submit_writes_no_state` (an explicit "0" in the received cell). Both leave `po.status == SENT` and `line.qty_received == Decimal("0")`. This makes the receive form forgiving when the user submits in error before scanning anything in.
- **Cumulative status decision** runs across *every* line on the PO (not just lines received this transaction): `fully = all(line.qty_received >= line.qty_ordered for line in lines)`. So a multi-line PO with line A fully received in transaction 1 + line B partially received in transaction 1 + line B fully received in transaction 2 → status flips to PARTIALLY_RECEIVED after T1 and to RECEIVED after T2. Single-line + multi-line tests both pin the transitions.
- **Audit shape — `purchase_order.received`**: `before={"status": prev_status_value}`, `after={"status": new_status_value, "lines": [{"line_id", "received_qty" (str), "actual_unit_cost" (str), "movement_id"} ...]}`. Only lines with received > 0 appear in `lines`. The `movement_id` lets the audit row pin to the exact `StockMovement` row this transaction created — the cost layer is reachable from there via `cost_layers.source_movement_id`. Decimals stringified via `str(decimal)` (matches every prior cost-engine audit). The transaction-scoped audit list is intentional: an audit reader who wants the *full* receipt history walks `audit_log WHERE entity_id=po.id ORDER BY created_at` and gets one row per receive transaction (and PO5's tests show the multi-receive case writes two `purchase_order.received` rows, not one combined).
- **`stock_movements.po_id` FK migration** (`0012_add_stock_movements_po_id_fk.py`): SQLite cannot `ALTER TABLE ... ADD CONSTRAINT`; Alembic's `op.batch_alter_table` recreates the table and copies the data, which is the standard SQLite-compat path. The constraint is `ON DELETE RESTRICT` (consistent with `cost_layers.source_movement_id` and the rest of the cost-engine FKs). The column stays nullable — manual M2 stock-ins still write `po_id=None`. Model column on `StockMovement` updated to declare the ForeignKey; the prior plain-Integer column stays compatible with existing rows because the values are NULL or — post-PO5 — match a real PO.
- **Detail page bimodal extension**: previously {draft → edit form, non-draft → read-only}. Now the read-only branch gains an `is_receivable` flag from the route context that lights up a `data-testid="po-receive-link"` block in the `(sent, partially_received)` cases. Received and cancelled hide the link. Tested across all five status values via `TestPOReceiveDetailRender`.
- **Templates / test-ids**: new `purchase_order_receive_form.html` with the form (`po-receive-form` + `po-receive-submit`), per-line row (`po-receive-line-row` with `data-line-id` + `data-item-id`), `po-receive-line-sku` / `po-receive-line-qty-ordered` / `po-receive-line-qty-received` / `po-receive-outstanding`, plus per-line `po-receive-received-input` + `po-receive-cost-input` (both with `data-line-id`). On the detail page: `po-receive-link-block` + `po-receive-link` (under the read-only banner when receivable). The `cost_<line_id>` input pre-fills with the line's `expected_unit_cost` (or empty when null) — the operator usually receives at the expected price, so the default reduces typing for the common case.
- **Test coverage** (`tests/integration/test_purchase_orders_routes.py` 47 new + `tests/e2e/test_reorder_e2e.py` walk extension):
  - Role enforcement (9): anon GET / POST 401; pending GET / POST 403; Workshop GET / POST 403; Manager / Office / Admin GET 200 (POST 303 covered via happy-path tests).
  - Status guard (7): unknown PO GET / POST 404; draft GET / POST 400; received GET 400; cancelled GET 400; partially_received GET 200 (the receive form re-opens for a PO that already received once).
  - Validation (8): negative received 400; non-numeric received 400; negative cost 400; non-numeric cost 400; blank cost with received > 0 400; over-receipt 400 (single-shot); cumulative over-receipt 400 (after partial); failed validation writes no state (no movement / cost layer / status flip / audit).
  - Single-full happy path (8): status flips to RECEIVED; movement carries `type=IN`, `po_id=po.id`, qty, total_cost (engine quantises 10 × 2.50 → "25.0000"); cost layer with `source=PO_RECEIPT`, qty_received + qty_remaining = received qty, unit_cost = actual cost (column-quantised "2.5000"); `line.qty_received` bumped; `item.current_qty` bumped; audit row shape with `before={"status":"sent"}`, `after.status="received"`, `after.lines=[{line_id, received_qty="10", actual_unit_cost="2.50", movement_id=int}]`; redirect to detail; flash includes "fully received".
  - Single-partial happy path (3): partial 5/10 flips to PARTIALLY_RECEIVED; second receive completes to RECEIVED with `line.qty_received=10`; multi-receive creates two cost layers at different unit costs (2.0000 + 2.2000), both with `source=PO_RECEIPT`.
  - Multi-line happy path (3): mixed full + partial flips to PARTIALLY_RECEIVED; zero-received line writes no movement (only the non-zero line's audit + movement); both movements carry the same `po_id`.
  - No-op submit (2): all-zero submission (no `received_*` keys) writes nothing; explicit 0 received with cost present writes nothing.
  - Detail render delta (5): draft hides receive link (drafts go through PO4 send first); sent shows the link + read-only banner; partially_received shows the link; received hides the link; cancelled hides the link.
  - Form render (2): receive form renders with the line row + outstanding equal to `qty_ordered` for a fresh sent PO; after a partial receipt, the form re-renders with reduced outstanding (10 → 4).
  - E2E walk extension: after PO4's send leg lands a sent PO with status="sent" + `po-receive-link` visible, the manager clicks the link, fills 120 + 2.00, submits, lands back on detail with status="received" + receive-link gone + `po-line-qty-received="120.0000"` + the linked item's `current_qty=120.0000` (verified via the items stock-in form) + the reorder dashboard's empty state (verifies the cost engine actually bumped stock above threshold). Cleanup unchanged.

**Edit + cancel a draft PO (PO2b):** extends `app/purchase_orders.py` with two more routes on the existing `/admin/purchase-orders` prefix. `POST /admin/purchase-orders/{po_id}` (Manager + Office; Workshop + pending 403) applies a sparse diff to a draft PO — top-level `expected_date` / `notes` plus per-line `qty_ordered_<line_id>` / `expected_unit_cost_<line_id>` form fields. `POST /admin/purchase-orders/{po_id}/cancel` (same role surface) flips status to `cancelled`. Both 400 if the PO isn't `status=draft`, 404 on unknown id. Audit shapes split: `purchase_order.updated` carries a sparse top-level diff plus a per-line list of changed-fields-only entries; `purchase_order.cancelled` carries `before={"status":"draft"}` / `after={"status":"cancelled"}`.

- **The detail page (`purchase_order_detail.html`) is now bimodal:** when `po.status == draft` it renders an *edit form* — the line cells become `<input type="text" inputmode="decimal">` for qty + cost, plus top-level `<input type="date">` for expected_date and `<textarea>` for notes, plus a "Save changes" submit and a separate `<form>` with a "Cancel this draft" submit. When the PO is *not* draft (sent / partially_received / received / cancelled), the page renders the existing read-only cells plus a `po-readonly-banner` paragraph saying "This PO is {status}; it cannot be edited." The status badge already carries the indicator. **The previous PO2 read-only test-ids** (`po-line-qty-ordered`, `po-line-expected-unit-cost`, `po-line-cost-empty`) are now only present on the read-only render path; PO2's `test_lines_render_in_sku_order_with_correct_cells` and `test_null_expected_cost_shows_empty_marker` were updated to use a non-draft status (SENT) so they continue to exercise that path. The e2e walk's draft-PO assertions were flipped from text-cell test-ids to `po-edit-qty-input` / `po-edit-cost-input` value checks.
- **`update_purchase_order` is `async def`** because it `await request.form()` to read the per-line `qty_ordered_<line_id>` and `expected_unit_cost_<line_id>` keys (line ids aren't known at function-signature time). FastAPI caches the parsed form body after the typed `Form()` parameters extract, so the second read is free. Same precedent as `app/items.py`'s `create_item` / `update_item` for custom-field reads.
- **Validation order** (all 400 *before* any DB mutation — atomic): (1) PO exists (404); (2) `_require_draft(po)` rejects non-drafts with the message naming the current status; (3) parse top-level `expected_date` (blank → None; ISO else 400) and `notes` (strip; blank → None; ≤ 2000 chars else 400); (4) iterate the existing PO lines, parsing each `qty_ordered_<line_id>` (positive Decimal else 400) and `expected_unit_cost_<line_id>` (blank → None; non-negative Decimal else 400). Missing line keys are 400 (would mean a line was added/removed in another tab; safer to error than silently drop). Extra form keys whose `line_id` suffix isn't on the PO are silently ignored.
- **Sparse diff is computed in memory before any mutation** so a no-op submit can be detected and the audit row skipped entirely. Top-level fields enter `before` / `after` only when changed. Per-line entries enter `before["lines"]` / `after["lines"]` only for lines where at least one field changed; each entry carries `{"line_id": N}` plus the changed field(s) (only changed fields per line — minimal information). Audit-row write is skipped when `not has_top_change and not has_line_change`. The route still 303s + flashes "no changes" so the user gets explicit feedback that the form did submit.
- **Decimal equality across scale boundaries:** Numeric(14,4) round-trips a stored `Decimal("10.0000")`. A form-submitted `"10"` parses as `Decimal("10")`. Python's Decimal compares numerically equal across scales (`Decimal("10") == Decimal("10.0000")` → True), so the diff logic correctly identifies it as a no-op. Stringification for audit uses `str(decimal)` which preserves the *parsed* scale (`"10"` for the just-parsed value, `"10.0000"` for the column-quantised value) — matches the audit shape established by M2-M5 + PO2.
- **`_require_draft` shared by both edit and cancel** so the status-guard rule is consistent. The error message "PO is {status}; only drafts can be edited" is used for both routes (the cancel route reuses the same predicate; in practice the user only sees the error if they POST against a stale page).
- **Cancel is non-destructive on lines:** `PurchaseOrder.status` flips, lines stay attached. No-undo path; operator must create a fresh draft if they want a new try. Idempotency rejection: cancelling an already-cancelled PO 400s (vs. silently succeeding) — pinned by `test_cancel_already_cancelled_po_is_400`. Same posture as `_require_draft` for edit.
- **`is_draft` is now in the detail context.** The `purchase_order_detail` GET handler computes `is_draft = po.status == POStatus.DRAFT` and passes it to the template; the template branches on this. The `expected_date` / `notes` `<dl>` rows are now in the read-only branch only (the draft branch surfaces them as form inputs instead).
- **Audit shape — `purchase_order.updated`** (sparse): `before` and `after` are dicts that contain only the changed top-level fields (`expected_date` and/or `notes`). When line(s) changed, both dicts also carry a `lines` list of `{line_id, <changed_field>, ...}` entries — only the fields that changed per line, with the previous string value in `before` and the new string value in `after`. Decimals via `str(decimal)`; null costs serialise as `None`. **A no-op submit writes no audit row.**
- **Audit shape — `purchase_order.cancelled`**: `before={"status": "draft"}`, `after={"status": "cancelled"}`. No line snapshot.
- **Test coverage** (`tests/integration/test_purchase_orders_routes.py` 43 new + 2 existing PO2 tests flipped to non-draft status + `tests/e2e/test_reorder_e2e.py` walk extended in-place):
  - Role enforcement (9): anon POST update / cancel 401; pending POST update / cancel 403; Workshop POST update / cancel 403; Manager POST update + cancel 303; Office POST update 303.
  - Status guard (6): edit `sent` 400, edit `received` 400, cancel `sent` 400, cancel already-cancelled 400, edit unknown 404, cancel unknown 404.
  - Validation (11): bad expected_date 400; notes > 2000 chars 400; qty blank / zero / negative / non-numeric (4); cost negative / non-numeric (2); missing line qty key 400; missing line cost key 400; failed validation writes no audit + leaves line value unchanged.
  - Edit happy path (8): change qty writes audit with `{line_id, qty_ordered: "10.0000"}` → `{line_id, qty_ordered: "42"}` shape (no top-level keys when only lines changed); change cost from null → value; clear cost to null; change top-level notes; change top-level expected_date; multi-line edit emits only the changed line in the audit list; no-op submit writes no audit row; flash on save includes "saved".
  - Cancel happy path (4): status flips to `cancelled`; audit row carries the correct before/after + entity_id; redirects to detail; lines + supplier preserved.
  - Detail render delta (5): draft renders the edit form + cancel button; sent renders the read-only banner + no edit form; received renders read-only; cancelled renders read-only; draft input pre-fills with the line's qty (10 → "10.0000").
  - E2E walk extension (in-place): after the existing dashboard / PO-create leg lands the manager on the draft PO detail page, the manager fills `po-edit-qty-input=120` + `po-edit-cost-input=1.50` + `po-edit-notes-input="rush order"`, clicks `po-edit-submit`, asserts the redirect re-renders the form with `po-edit-qty-input=120.0000` + `po-edit-cost-input=1.5000` + `po-edit-notes-input="rush order"`. Then navigates to the PO list via `nav-pos`, clicks `po-row-detail-link`, lands on the detail page, clicks `po-cancel-submit`, asserts the redirect lands on the same detail URL with `po-status-badge=cancelled` + `po-readonly-banner` visible + `po-edit-form` count=0. Cleanup unchanged (the cancelled PO stays in the test DB; each session uses a fresh schema).

**Draft PO from a supplier group (PO2):** new module `app/purchase_orders.py` with three routes mounted across two prefixes — `POST /admin/reorder/draft-po` (creates a draft PO from a supplier group; the action button on PO1's dashboard targets this), `GET /admin/purchase-orders` (list, status-filterable), `GET /admin/purchase-orders/{po_id}` (read-only detail). All three are **Manager + Office** (Admin via bypass; Workshop + pending 403). New tables `purchase_orders` + `purchase_order_lines` + new `POStatus` enum (draft / sent / partially_received / received / cancelled). New templates `purchase_order_detail.html` + `purchase_orders_list.html`. New `nav-pos` link in `base.html` for admin/manager/office. The `reorder_dashboard.html` gains a "Draft PO" form button per **active** supplier group; archived-supplier groups and the synthetic "(no supplier)" group instead render a blocked-note explaining why no button is shown. PO2 only writes the `draft` status; PO3 / PO4 / PO5 will exercise the other transitions.

- **Migration `0011_create_purchase_orders.py`** creates two tables.
  - `purchase_orders`: `id, supplier_id (FK suppliers RESTRICT NOT NULL), status (String(20), SAEnum-backed POStatus, server_default 'draft'), expected_date (Date nullable), sent_at (DateTime(tz) nullable), notes (String(2000) nullable), created_by (FK users.id SET NULL nullable), created_at, updated_at`. Indexes: per-supplier, per-status, per-created_at.
  - `purchase_order_lines`: `id, po_id (FK purchase_orders CASCADE NOT NULL), item_id (FK items RESTRICT NOT NULL), qty_ordered (Numeric(14,4) NOT NULL), qty_received (Numeric(14,4) NOT NULL default 0, server_default '0'), expected_unit_cost (Numeric(14,4) nullable)`. Indexes: per-po, per-item.
  - **Not** updating `stock_movements.po_id` to a real FK in this migration — the column is currently always NULL (no PO5 yet); adding the FK is PO5's responsibility (the receive path is what activates the link). M1's migration explicitly defers this.
  - The `purchase_order_lines.po_id` FK is `ON DELETE CASCADE` (vs. RESTRICT elsewhere). PO2 has no UI to delete a PO; the cascade is a forward-looking parity for a future "destroy a never-sent draft" UX. RESTRICT would have been fine for PO2 in isolation; CASCADE keeps the schema clean for that follow-up without a follow-up migration.
- **Models** in `app/models.py`:
  - `POStatus(StrEnum)` — `DRAFT, SENT, PARTIALLY_RECEIVED, RECEIVED, CANCELLED`. Stored as `String(20)` via SAEnum + `values_callable`, matching every other enum on this codebase.
  - `PurchaseOrder` mirroring the migration. `status` defaults to `POStatus.DRAFT` (Python-side) and `'draft'` (server_default) — both halves required by SQLAlchemy when the column has a non-null NOT NULL constraint.
  - `PurchaseOrderLine` with `qty_received` defaulting to `Decimal("0")`. No `archived_at` — lines are part of the PO and don't soft-delete independently. Cancelling a PO sets its status to `cancelled`; the lines stay attached.
- **Route surface (3 routes total)**:
  - `POST /admin/reorder/draft-po` — Manager + Office. Form input: `supplier_id` (string). The CSRF middleware enforces the token on POST.
  - `GET /admin/purchase-orders[?status_filter=all|draft|sent|partially_received|received|cancelled]` — Manager + Office. Newest-first ordering (`created_at DESC, id DESC`). The status_filter param defaults to `all` and silently coerces unknown values back to `all`. The query joins `Supplier` to surface the supplier name; line counts are computed via a per-row `func.count(PurchaseOrderLine.id)` query (one extra round-trip per PO row in the list — acceptable for tens of POs in v1; flagged as a perf follow-up if the list grows).
  - `GET /admin/purchase-orders/{po_id}` — Manager + Office. 404 on unknown. Lines are fetched in SKU order (`JOIN items ORDER BY items.sku`).
- **Validation on draft-PO create** (all 400, *before* any DB write so failures are atomic):
  - `supplier_id` parses as int (blank / non-int reject).
  - References an existing **active** `Supplier` (unknown / archived both reject — the dashboard hides the Draft PO button on archived-supplier groups, but a stale POST is still rejected server-side; defence in depth).
  - The supplier must have at least one active item below threshold (`Item.archived_at IS NULL AND Item.supplier_id == :sid AND Item.current_qty <= Item.reorder_threshold`) — same WHERE clause as PO1's dashboard, narrowed to one supplier. Otherwise 400 — typically a stale POST after a concurrent stock-in cleared the threshold.
- **Default `qty_ordered` selection** (per line):
  - Preference 1: `item.reorder_qty` when `> 0` (the manager's intent).
  - Preference 2: the deficit `threshold - current_qty` when *that* is `> 0` (someone forgot to set a reorder qty but the deficit is genuine).
  - Fallback: `Decimal("1")` (the at-threshold-zero-reorder-zero-deficit cohort — order at least one to keep the line meaningful; the operator can edit later in PO2b).
- **Default `expected_unit_cost` selection** (per line): the most recent `CostLayer.unit_cost` for the item (`ORDER BY received_at DESC, id DESC`) or `None` when the item has no layers yet. Note: a fully-consumed layer is still the most recent unit-cost signal — the lookup doesn't filter by `qty_remaining > 0`. A zero unit_cost (e.g. sample / gifted stock) carries through faithfully; the operator can edit if zero is wrong for their context.
- **Audit shape** — `purchase_order.created`: `action="purchase_order.created"`, `entity_type="purchase_order"`, `entity_id=po.id`, `before=None`, `after={supplier_id, status="draft", expected_date=None, notes=None, lines=[{item_id, qty_ordered (str), expected_unit_cost (str | None)}, ...]}`. Decimals stringified via `str(decimal)` (matches M2 / M3 / M4 / M5's audit convention; the column round-trip yields scale-4 Decimals so e.g. `qty_ordered="50.0000"` not `"50"`). The lines snapshot is the audit primary; line ids are reconstructable from `purchase_order_lines.po_id` if needed.
- **Templates / test-ids**:
  - `purchase_order_detail.html`: `po-detail-heading` / `po-status-badge` (with `data-status`) / `po-supplier-name` / `po-created-by` / `po-created-at` / `po-expected-date` / `po-notes` / `po-lines-table` / per-line `po-line-row` (with `data-line-id` + `data-item-id`) / `po-line-sku` / `po-line-name` / `po-line-qty-ordered` / `po-line-qty-received` / `po-line-expected-unit-cost` (with a `po-line-cost-empty` `<span>` inside when null) / `po-detail-no-lines` / `po-back-to-list` / `po-back-to-reorder`.
  - `purchase_orders_list.html`: `po-list-heading` / `po-status-filter-form` / `po-status-filter` (auto-submitting `<select>`) / `po-list-empty` / `po-list-table` / per-row `po-row` (with `data-po-id`) / `po-row-supplier` / `po-row-status` (with `data-status`) / `po-row-line-count` / `po-row-created-at` / `po-row-detail-link` / `po-list-reorder-link`.
  - `reorder_dashboard.html`: per active-supplier group, an inline `<form action="/admin/reorder/draft-po" method="post">` with hidden `csrf_token` + `supplier_id` and a submit button (`reorder-draft-po-form` / `reorder-draft-po-button`). Archived-supplier groups carry `reorder-draft-po-blocked-archived` instead; the no-supplier bucket carries `reorder-draft-po-blocked-no-supplier`. Both blocked-notes have distinct test-ids so a future tweak can pin which scenario the user hit.
  - `base.html`: new `nav-pos` link (visible to admin/manager/office; hidden for workshop) targeting `/admin/purchase-orders`. The `nav-reorder` aria-current was tightened from `startswith("/admin/reorder")` to `path == "/admin/reorder" or startswith("/admin/reorder/")` — without the tighten, the future GET endpoint under `/admin/reorder/<x>/...` (or even the POST target `/admin/reorder/draft-po`) would mark Reorder as "current" on a totally different page. The PO list page does NOT light up nav-reorder (pinned by `test_reorder_aria_current_does_not_match_pos_path`).
- **Test coverage** (`tests/integration/test_purchase_orders_routes.py` 38 + `tests/integration/test_layout.py` 6 + `tests/integration/test_reorder_routes.py` 3 + `tests/e2e/test_reorder_e2e.py` extension):
  - Role enforcement (10): anon GET-list / GET-detail / POST-create all 401; pending POST 403; Workshop POST + GET-list + GET-detail all 403; Manager / Office / Admin all 200 on GET-list.
  - POST validation (7): blank / non-int / unknown / archived supplier all 400; supplier with zero low-stock items 400; supplier with only above-threshold items 400; failed validation writes no PO + no lines + no audit row.
  - POST happy path (7): single-line PO carries the right supplier_id / status / created_by / qty_ordered / qty_received / expected_unit_cost + redirect target (`/admin/purchase-orders/{po_id}`); multi-line PO ordered by SKU (insert in C-3 / A-1 / B-2 order, asserted as A-1 / B-2 / C-3); above-threshold items excluded; archived items excluded; other suppliers' items excluded; audit row carries supplier_id / status / expected_date=None / notes=None / lines=[full snapshot]; flash includes supplier name + line count.
  - Default qty_ordered (3): reorder_qty=75 → 75; reorder_qty=0 + qty=3 + threshold=10 → deficit=7; reorder_qty=0 + qty=0 + threshold=0 → fallback=1.
  - Default expected_unit_cost (3): no layers → `None`; single layer → that layer's unit_cost; multi-layer with distinct received_at → newest layer's unit_cost (oldest at 2.00, newest at 3.00 → 3.00 wins).
  - GET list (4): empty state; populated newest-first (po2 inserted second appears before po1); `?status_filter=draft` shows drafts excludes sent; `?status_filter=sent` shows sent excludes drafts.
  - GET detail (4): unknown 404; populated heading + supplier + status badge; lines render in SKU order with right cells (qty_ordered=10 / qty_received=0 / `po-line-cost-empty` for the null-cost line; qty_ordered=20 + 2.50 cost rendered for the priced line); null expected_unit_cost shows the empty marker.
  - Layout / nav (6): manager / office / admin nav-pos visible; workshop nav-pos hidden; aria-current on `/admin/purchase-orders`; nav-reorder aria-current does NOT match the PO list page (the tightening pin).
  - Reorder dashboard (3): active-supplier group renders the form + button + hidden supplier_id + CSRF; archived-supplier group renders the blocked-archived note (and no button within the section); no-supplier group renders the blocked-no-supplier note.
  - E2E walk extension: after PO1's existing dashboard load showing `RD-LOW`, the manager clicks the supplier-group's `reorder-draft-po-button`, lands on the PO detail page (asserts `po-detail-heading` visible, exactly 1 line, supplier="Reorder Bullion Co", status="draft", line sku=RD-LOW, qty_ordered=100.0000, `po-line-cost-empty` visible because RD-LOW had no prior layer), navigates via `nav-pos` to the PO list (asserts 1 row, supplier name, line_count=1), navigates back to the dashboard via `nav-reorder` (asserts RD-LOW still listed — the PO doesn't change `current_qty`), then continues with the existing stock-in → empty-dashboard cleanup steps.

**Reorder dashboard (PO1):** new module `app/reorder.py` with one route `GET /admin/reorder` for **Manager + Office** (Admin via the bypass; Workshop + pending 403). New template `reorder_dashboard.html`. Read-only — no mutations, no audit, no movement type, no new tables. Workshop's `nav-reorder` is hidden (matches MISSION §3 "Workshop... cannot manage POs").

- **Query:** `select(Item, Supplier).outerjoin(Supplier, Item.supplier_id == Supplier.id).where(Item.archived_at.is_(None)).where(Item.current_qty <= Item.reorder_threshold).order_by(Item.sku)`. Single round-trip; the supplier-side ordering happens in Python after bucketing.
- **Bucketing:** the route iterates the result once, grouping rows by `supplier_id` (or `None` for items with no supplier). Named-supplier groups sort alphabetically by supplier name (the *un-suffixed* name, so an archived "Old Co" still sorts to "O", not to the bottom); the synthetic "(no supplier)" bucket renders last. Within each bucket, rows preserve the SQL-side SKU order.
- **View shape per group:** `{supplier_id: int|None, supplier_label: str, supplier_archived: bool, rows: [{item, current_qty, threshold, reorder_qty, deficit}]}`. `deficit = reorder_threshold - current_qty` — always ≥ 0 since the WHERE clause guarantees `current_qty <= reorder_threshold`. `supplier_label` carries `"(archived)"` suffix for archived suppliers; the `supplier_archived` flag drives a `data-supplier-archived="true"` attribute on the section so future styling / filtering can light up archived rows differently.
- **Edge cases:**
  - **Threshold trigger is `<=`, not `<`**: an item with `current_qty == reorder_threshold` is *included* (deficit=0). The trigger means "at or below the threshold" — an item exactly at threshold is at the trigger point, not safely above. Pinned by the `at_threshold_is_included` test.
  - **Zero threshold + zero qty**: included (deficit=0). The interpretation is "no threshold set, also no stock — surface this so the user can decide whether to set a real threshold or order some". Zero threshold + positive qty is *excluded* (`1 > 0`).
  - **Archived items** are filtered out at the SQL level — even when below threshold, they don't show. Un-archiving brings them back the next request.
  - **Archived suppliers** still bucket their items; the supplier section just gets the "(archived)" label suffix. Items can be moved out of an archived supplier (item-side edit clears `supplier_id`) and immediately drop into the no-supplier bucket — pinned by the `clearing_supplier_drops_into_no_supplier_bucket` test.
- **No mutations / no audit**: PO1 is purely a read. PO2 lands the first write surface (draft PO from selection) and starts using `record_audit("po.created", ...)`. The dashboard explicitly does not select / batch-mark items — that workflow lives in PO2's "create draft from selection" UI.
- **Templates / test-ids**: `reorder-heading`; whole-page empty-state `reorder-empty`; per-supplier `reorder-group` (with `data-supplier-id="<id|none>"` and conditional `data-supplier-archived="true"`); per-row `reorder-row` (`data-item-id`); cells `reorder-item-sku` / `reorder-item-name` / `reorder-current-qty` / `reorder-threshold` / `reorder-reorder-qty` / `reorder-deficit`; row links `reorder-detail-link` (→ `/admin/items/{id}/detail`) and `reorder-stock-in-link` (→ `/admin/items/{id}/in`). `base.html` gains a `nav-reorder` link visible to admin/manager/office.
- **Test coverage** (`tests/integration/test_reorder_routes.py` 23 + `tests/integration/test_layout.py` 5 + `tests/e2e/test_reorder_e2e.py` 1):
  - Role enforcement (6): anon 401; pending 403; Workshop 403; Office / Manager / Admin 200.
  - Empty state (2): no items → empty visible + no groups; only above-threshold items → empty + no rows.
  - Single-supplier rendering (3): one group + one row visible; cells correct (qty=3, threshold=10, reorder_qty=100, deficit=7); detail-link + stock-in-link href to the right URLs.
  - No-supplier bucket (2): supplier_id IS NULL → "(no supplier)" group with `data-supplier-id="none"`; coexists with named-supplier group when both exist.
  - Multiple suppliers (2): groups ordered alphabetically by supplier name (Alpha before Zebra); rows within a group ordered by SKU (A-1 → B-2 → C-3).
  - Threshold edge (2): `qty == threshold` included (deficit=0); `qty > threshold` excluded.
  - Archived item filter (2): archived items hidden even when below threshold; un-archiving restores.
  - Archived supplier surfacing (2): "(archived)" label suffix + `data-supplier-archived="true"` on the section; clearing the item's supplier drops it into the "(no supplier)" bucket.
  - Zero threshold (2): zero threshold + zero qty included (deficit=0); zero threshold + positive qty excluded.
  - Layout / nav (5): manager/office/admin nav-reorder visible; workshop nav-reorder hidden; `/admin/reorder` page sets `aria-current="page"` on the nav link.
  - E2E walk: a fresh manager (promoted from pending by admin) creates a supplier + a category + two items (`RD-LOW` and `RD-OK`, both threshold=10, supplier="Reorder Bullion Co"), records a stock-in to push `RD-OK` above threshold (qty=50), visits `/admin/reorder` via the nav link, asserts only `RD-LOW` is in the supplier's group (not `RD-OK`), asserts deficit=10 on the row, clicks the row's `reorder-stock-in-link`, lands on `/admin/items/{low_id}/in`, records a receipt of qty=25, returns to the dashboard via the nav link, and asserts the empty state is visible. Cleanup archives both items + the supplier + the category.

**Transfer between locations (M5):** `app/movements.py` gains two more routes mounted under `/admin/items` for **Manager + Office + Workshop**: `GET /admin/items/{item_id}/transfer` renders the transfer form (current-location read-only display, to-location select excluding the current location and archived rows, qty input pre-filled with `current_qty`, optional reason + note); `POST /admin/items/{item_id}/transfer` validates, snapshots the from-location id, builds a `StockMovement(type=TRANSFER, total_cost=None)`, flushes, **flips `item.location_id`** to the target, writes a `stock_movement.transfer` audit row, commits, and 303s back with a flash. The form reuses the M2 / M3 / M4 recent-movements list (same `movements-table` / `movement-row` test-ids).

- **Engine isolation is the headline contract:** transfer is the **only** `MovementType` that bypasses the cost engine. The route never calls `record_receipt` or `consume_fifo`. No `CostLayer` is created, no `CostLayerConsumption` is written, `cost_layers.qty_remaining` is unchanged across all open layers, `item.current_qty` is unchanged, and `movement.total_cost` stays `None`. This is the by-design behaviour: transfers move an item between locations without changing inventory level or valuation. The route mutates `item.location_id` directly — that's the *only* `Item` column it touches besides the `StockMovement` insert (and `current_qty` / `cost_layers.*` are owned by the engine, not by `Item`-level routes).
- **Validation** (all 400 *before* any DB write — atomic): item exists (404), not archived (400), has a current `location_id` set (400 with "this item has no location yet — set one via the edit form before transferring"; transfer presupposes a "from"); `to_location_id` parses as int and references an *active* `Location` (archived rejects with "target location is not active"); `to_location_id` differs from current `location_id` (no-op transfers reject — would write a confusing audit row); `qty` parses as a positive Decimal (reuses `_parse_positive_decimal`). `reason` and `note` are stripped, blank → None (optional, same as M2 / M3; M4 differs because adjustments require attribution, transfers don't — moving stock between two of your own locations is a routine operation, not a variance).
- **Audit shape**: `action="stock_movement.transfer"`, `entity_type="stock_movement"`, `entity_id=movement.id`, `before={"location_id": from_location_id}`, `after={"item_id", "qty", "from_location_id", "to_location_id", "reason", "note"}`. The `before` carries only the changed field on the item (the location_id), keeping the diff narrow and consistent with the existing `item.updated` audit shape. The `after` carries the route inputs plus the resolved from/to ids (so the audit row is self-contained for reporting; a future "by-location movement report" can read this row without joining back to the movement + item). `from_location_id` appears in both `before` and `after` — that's deliberate, not a bug: `before` documents what changed on the *Item*, `after` documents the full transfer record. **No `total_cost`, no `unit_cost`, no `source`, no `received_at`** — transfer rows don't carry any of those fields, consistent with the contract that transfers don't go through the engine.
- **Form**: `qty` defaults to `current_qty` (most transfers are wholesale). For the v1 single-location-per-item data model, the qty is informational on the movement row only — the location pointer flips wholesale regardless of the qty value. Documented in the form's `<em>{{ item.unit }} — recorded for audit; transfers don't change current quantity or valuation</em>` hint and in the route docstring. (Partial-qty transfers across multiple "stock-by-location" rows is a v2 multi-location feature; out of scope for v1 per MISSION §3 "between locations (if multi-location is enabled)" and the §6 data model showing one `location_id` on `Item`.)
- **No in-form 400 carve-out** (unlike M3 / M4): every M5 validation error is a "user typed something wrong" case (parse error, out-of-options, same-as-current), not a data-dependent runtime error like M3's insufficient-stock. The bare-400 page is the right posture, matching every other validation 400 in the app outside M3 / M4's data-dependent stock-shortage carve-out. (The one *almost*-data-dependent failure is "the target location was archived between form load and submit" — but that's vanishingly rare and the user can re-pick from the refreshed dropdown.)
- **M6 timeline integration**: TRANSFER rows render with no direction sign — `_attach_directions_and_breakdown`'s defensive `else` branch in `app/movements.py` (already in place from M6) leaves `direction = ""` for movements that don't go through the engine. The `data-direction=""` attribute lets future styling distinguish them. The `total_cost` cell shows "—" via the existing `{% if m.total_cost is not none %}` template logic. **No layer-breakdown sub-row** appears for transfers (since the engine never wrote a consumption row for them). M6 needs zero template changes for M5 — the existing rendering accommodates transfers naturally. From/to location names are *not* surfaced on the timeline (they live in the audit row only); enriching the render to display them is queued as a self-critique item.
- **Templates**: new `stock_transfer_form.html` mirroring `stock_out_form.html`'s shape (header + form + recent-movements). Test-ids: `stock-transfer-form`, `stock-transfer-from-location` (read-only display of the current location label), `stock-transfer-to-location-input`, `stock-transfer-qty-input`, `stock-transfer-reason-input`, `stock-transfer-note-input`, `stock-transfer-submit`. `items_form.html` gains a fourth `data-testid="stock-transfer-link"` "Transfer →" link in the same `{% if not item.archived_at %}` block as in / out / adjust. `item_detail.html` likewise gets a `data-testid="stock-transfer-link"` action link in the in / out / adjust action block.
- **Test coverage** (`tests/integration/test_movements_routes.py` 46 new + `tests/e2e/test_movements_e2e.py` extension):
  - Role enforcement (10): anon GET / POST 401; pending 403; Workshop / Office / Manager / Admin all 200 GET / 303 POST.
  - Form rendering (10): inputs + CSRF; current-location label visible; to-location options exclude the current location AND archived rows (asserted by slicing the rendered HTML to the `<select>` block and checking the excluded ids don't appear there); qty pre-fills with `current_qty`; recent-movements empty state; unknown 404; archived item 400; item-without-location 400.
  - Validation matrix (13): blank to_location 400; non-int 400; unknown 400; archived target 400; same-as-current 400; qty blank / zero / negative / non-numeric (4); archived item POST 400; item-without-location POST 400; failed validation writes no audit + no movement row + no location flip; the no-flip assertion runs across two distinct failure paths (same-location reject + bad-target reject) to prove the route doesn't half-commit.
  - Happy path (5): creates `StockMovement(type=TRANSFER)` with qty + reason + note + total_cost=None + user_id=actor.id; flips `item.location_id` from old to new; audit row with the right `before` (`{"location_id": from_id}`) and `after` (full route inputs + from/to ids) shape; whitespace-strip on reason; blank reason / note → None; flash includes "Transfer recorded" + both location names + the item name.
  - Engine isolation (3): no `CostLayer` row created (count + qty_remaining unchanged on the seeded layer); no `CostLayerConsumption` row created at all; `item.current_qty` unchanged after transfer (verified at scale 4 — `Decimal("42.0000")`).
  - Transfer link visibility (2): edit form shows the link for active items; hides for archived.
  - Detail-page rendering (2): TRANSFER row carries `data-direction=""` and renders "—" for total cost; no `layer-breakdown` `<tr>` follows the row.
  - Detail-link visibility (2): detail page shows the transfer link for active items; hides for archived.
  - E2E walk extension: in the existing single walk, the manager-setup step now creates two locations (`Movements From Bench`, `Movements To Storage`) and assigns `Movements From Bench` to the item on create. After the existing M6 detail-page leg (current_qty=75), workshop deep-links to `/transfer`, asserts the from-location shows "Movements From Bench", picks "Movements To Storage" via `select_option(label=...)`, fills qty=75 + reason="end of shift", submits, asserts the flash contains both location names, the recent-movements row's first row carries "transfer" + qty 75, and the form's from-location label has flipped to "Movements To Storage" (because the route just committed the location change). Re-visits `/detail` and asserts the timeline now has 5 rows (was 4) with still 2 layer-breakdown blocks (TRANSFER doesn't add one) + `current_qty` unchanged at 75.0000. Cleanup-step extension: the manager archives both locations after the item + category to keep downstream walks' active lists clean.

**Workshop read-only items list + form (I1c):** Closes the UX gap flagged in M2 / M3 / M4 / M6 self-critiques: Workshop has had deep-link access to `/in`, `/out`, `/adjust`, `/detail` for four iterations but no UI path to *find* an item without a deep-link or QR scan. After I1c, Workshop browses `/admin/items` and clicks into a per-item read-only view that surfaces every metadata field (category, unit, tracking mode, supplier, location, QR code, notes, custom field values + their values) — a superset of what M6's detail page shows. Implementation is small + boring: extend `require_role` on the two existing GET handlers, add a `_can_save_item` predicate, thread two new template flags (`can_edit_item` on the list, `can_save` on the form), and add a `disabled` toggle on every form input. The POST routes (`POST /admin/items`, `POST /admin/items/{id}`, archive, unarchive) keep their existing `require_role(MANAGER)` / `require_role(MANAGER, OFFICE)` shape — Workshop hits them with 403, server-enforced, plus the disabled form inputs as defense-in-depth.

- **Routes** (`app/items.py`): `GET /admin/items` and `GET /admin/items/{item_id}/edit` now accept `Role.WORKSHOP` in addition to Manager + Office (and Admin via the bypass). All POST routes unchanged. `GET /admin/items/new` still 403s for Workshop (no point GET-ing a create form they can't submit). New helper `_can_save_item(user) -> bool` returns True for Manager + Office + Admin, False for Workshop. The `edit_item_form` route now branches the title between "Edit {name}" (saveable) and "View {name}" (read-only) based on `_can_save_item`. The `new_item_form` always sets `can_save=True` (Workshop can't reach it).
- **Templates** (`items_list.html`, `items_form.html`, `base.html`):
  - `items_list.html`: per-row Edit link conditionally renders as `<a data-testid="view-item">View</a>` when `not can_edit_item`. Same URL either way (it's the role that constrains write access, not the path) but the label is honest. The existing `can_create` / `can_archive` flags already evaluated to False for Workshop because Workshop role isn't in `(MANAGER, ADMIN)`, so the New CTA + per-row archive/unarchive forms hide automatically.
  - `items_form.html`: a single `{% set ro = (can_save is defined) and (not can_save) %}` at the top drives every input's `disabled` attribute (sku, name, category, unit, tracking_mode, requires_checkout, reorder_threshold, reorder_qty, supplier, location, qr_code, notes — plus every custom-field input across all seven types). The submit button is wrapped in `{% if not ro %}` so it disappears entirely for Workshop. A `<p data-testid="item-form-readonly-note"><em>View only — your role cannot edit items.</em></p>` block renders above the form when `ro` is True. The "Stock in / Stock out / Adjust / Details / Manage units" action links remain visible (they're gated on `not item.archived_at`, not on role — Workshop has access to all of them).
  - `base.html`: extend the `nav-items` visibility condition from `("admin", "manager", "office")` to `("admin", "manager", "office", "workshop")`. The `aria-current` on `/admin/items*` paths still works.
- **Test coverage** (`tests/integration/test_items_routes.py` 16 new + `tests/integration/test_layout.py` 1 flipped + `tests/e2e/test_movements_e2e.py` 1 leg-set):
  - `TestRoleEnforcement` — flipped `test_workshop_get_list_is_403` → `test_workshop_get_list_is_200`; added `test_workshop_get_edit_form_is_200`, `test_workshop_get_new_form_is_403`, `test_workshop_update_is_403` (POST returns 403 + sku/name unchanged + no audit row), `test_workshop_archive_is_403`, `test_workshop_unarchive_is_403`. The existing `test_workshop_create_is_403` stays — POST `/admin/items` still 403s.
  - New `TestWorkshopReadOnlyView` class (10 tests): list shows "View" not "Edit" link for Workshop; list hides New CTA for Workshop; list hides archive/unarchive forms for Workshop; list shows "Edit" link for Office (sanity-check the link-label split); form inputs all carry `disabled` attribute (sampled across 10 test-ids); form has no `item-submit` test-id for Workshop; form renders the read-only note for Workshop; form title is "View {name}" for Workshop; form still shows the in/out/adjust/detail action links for Workshop; form disables custom-field inputs for Workshop; form for Manager keeps the submit button + omits the read-only note (sanity).
  - `test_layout.py`: flipped `test_workshop_nav_excludes_items_link` → `test_workshop_nav_includes_items_link` (asserts both `data-testid="nav-items"` and `href="/admin/items"` are present in the rendered nav for Workshop).
  - E2E walk extension: in `test_movements_e2e.py`'s existing single walk, after the Workshop user signs in (and before the deep-link to `/in`), Workshop now navigates via `nav-items`, asserts the New CTA is hidden, sees the manager-created item row, asserts the row shows `view-item` (not `edit-item`) and hides the archive button, clicks `view-item`, asserts the form renders with the read-only note + no submit + the `stock-in-link` still visible. Walk file's docstring updated to reflect the new posture.

**Item detail page (M6):** new `GET /admin/items/{item_id}/detail` route on `app/movements.py` for **Manager + Office + Workshop** (mirrors M2 / M3 / M4). Read-only page that consolidates the cost-engine outputs: item header (name + sku + archived flag), summary line (current_qty + open_value + reorder_threshold), action links (in / out / adjust / edit / manage units), open-layers table, paginated movement timeline with per-row layer breakdown for OUT and negative-adjust rows. No state-changing routes, no audit. First place in the codebase with proper pagination (`?page=N&page_size=20`).

- **Engine ownership maintained:** route never mutates `item.current_qty`, `cost_layers.qty_remaining`, `movement.total_cost` — pure read.
- **Helpers** (added next to the existing `_recent_movements` etc.): `_PAGE_SIZE = 20`; `_open_layers(db, item_id)` returns layers with `qty_remaining > 0` ordered FIFO `(received_at ASC, id ASC)` as view-shaped dicts; `_count_movements(db, item_id)` returns the integer total (used by the paginator); `_movements_page(db, item_id, *, page, page_size)` returns a single page newest-first `(created_at DESC, id DESC)` as view-shaped dicts (mirrors `_recent_movements`'s shape so the timeline can reuse the layout); `_attach_directions_and_breakdown(db, movements)` mutates the page-of-movements list in place to add `direction` (`"+"`/`"-"`/`""`) and `breakdown` (list of consumption rows with layer received_at + qty_consumed + unit_cost_at_consumption) to each row; `_paginate(total, page, page_size)` returns the metadata dict (page / page_size / total / page_count / has_prev / has_next), clamping out-of-range pages to `[1, page_count]`; `_can_edit_item(user)` returns True for Manager + Office + Admin (matches I1b's items-edit role surface — drives the edit-link visibility).
- **Direction derivation**: a movement is positive if it has a row in `cost_layers` with `source_movement_id == movement.id` (i.e. IN or POSITIVE_ADJUSTMENT created a layer); negative if it has rows in `cost_layer_consumptions` with `movement_id == movement.id` (i.e. OUT or negative-adjustment consumed layers). Both relationships are queried in batch over the page's movement ids — two extra queries per page (one for the layer-side ids, one for the consumption rows + their parent layers' received_at). For TRANSFER (M5) — which has neither — the defensive `else` branch leaves `direction = ""` and the row renders with no sign; will revisit when M5 lands.
- **Pagination clamping is silent**, not 400: a stale `?page=99` link lands on the last page rather than an error page. Friendlier UX for cached / shared URLs. Tests pin both clamping paths (`?page=99` → last; `?page=0` → first).
- **Archived item posture**: detail page renders for archived items (it's a read of *history*) but suppresses the in / out / adjust action-link block (`{% if not item.archived_at %}`) — same posture as `items_form.html`. The `data-testid="item-detail-archived"` marker tells the user the item is archived. Archived-different from M2 / M3 / M4 form routes, which 400 on archived (write paths must reject; read paths must allow).
- **Templates:** new `item_detail.html` with seven test-id surfaces — `item-detail-heading` / `item-detail-sku` / `item-current-qty` / `item-open-value` / `item-detail-threshold` / `item-detail-archived`; `cost-layers-table` with per-row `cost-layer-row` (`cost-layer-qty-remaining` / `cost-layer-unit-cost` / `cost-layer-source` per cell) plus empty state `cost-layers-empty`; `movements-timeline` with per-row `timeline-row` (`timeline-qty` carrying the directional sign concatenated with qty, `timeline-total-cost`); per-row `layer-breakdown` block (a follow-up `<tr>` containing a `<ul>` of `layer-breakdown-row` items showing qty_consumed × unit_cost_at_consumption + the layer's received_at) appearing only when `m.breakdown` is non-empty; pagination footer `pagination` with either `pagination-single-page` (when `page_count <= 1`) or `pagination-info` + conditional `pagination-prev` / `pagination-next` links carrying `?page=…` URLs. `items_list.html` gains a `data-testid="detail-link"` "Details" link in the per-row Actions cell; `items_form.html` gains a `data-testid="detail-link"` "Details →" link in the same `{% if item %}` block as the existing in / out / adjust links (so the link is visible on every saved item, including archived ones — detail read works for archived).
- **Test coverage** (`tests/integration/test_movements_routes.py` 34 new + `tests/e2e/test_movements_e2e.py` extension):
  - Role enforcement (6): anon 401; pending 403; Workshop / Office / Manager / Admin all 200.
  - Rendering (5): unknown item 404; archived item still renders + shows archived flag + suppresses in / out / adjust links; item header (name / sku / current_qty / open_value / threshold) all present; action-link visibility for active item (in / out / adjust / edit-item-link); workshop sees in/out/adjust but not the edit-item-link.
  - Cost layers (5): empty state when no layers; single layer rendered with all columns; multi-layer with mixed sources (manual_in + positive_adjustment); fully-consumed layer (qty_remaining=0) excluded; layers ordered FIFO via order-of-appearance check.
  - Movements timeline (6): empty state when no movements; IN row direction `+` + `total_cost = 14.00`; OUT row direction `-` + total_cost `6.0000` (column-quantised scale 4 from M3's audit-shape wart); adjustment-increase direction `+`; adjustment-decrease direction `-`; ordering newest-first.
  - Layer breakdown (5): IN row has no breakdown; OUT row has 1 breakdown row; negative-adjustment has breakdown; positive-adjustment has none; multi-layer OUT shows 2 breakdown rows.
  - Pagination (5): empty state replaces the pagination; ≤ page_size renders single-page footer; > page_size renders 2 pages with prev/next nav (page 1 has next-no-prev with 20 rows; page 2 has prev-no-next with 1 row); out-of-range `?page=99` clamps to last; `?page=0` clamps to first.
  - Detail-link visibility (2): items list shows the link per row; items edit form shows the link in the action block.
  - E2E walk extension: after the M4 leg-2 (decrease, current_qty=75), workshop deep-links to `/detail`. Asserts: heading contains "Casting alloy", current_qty=75.0000, open_value contains "197.5" (= 55 × 2.50 + 20 × 3.00), 2 cost-layer rows, 4 timeline rows, 2 layer-breakdown blocks (one for OUT, one for adjust-decrease — IN and adjust-increase don't get one), pagination-single-page visible, in-link visible, edit-link absent (workshop role).

**Manual adjustment route (M4):** `app/movements.py` gains two more routes mounted under `/admin/items` for **Manager + Office + Workshop**: `GET /admin/items/{item_id}/adjust` renders an adjust form (qty + direction + unit_cost + reason + note) plus the same recent-movements + open-value summary used by stock-out; `POST /admin/items/{item_id}/adjust` validates, builds a `StockMovement(type=ADJUSTMENT)`, flushes, **dispatches on direction**: `increase` calls `record_receipt(..., source=CostLayerSource.POSITIVE_ADJUSTMENT, received_at=now())` (creates a layer + bumps qty); `decrease` calls `consume_fifo(...)` (writes consumption rows + decrements qty). Either path writes a single `stock_movement.adjustment` audit row, commits, and 303s back with a flash. The decrease path inherits M3's atomic-on-raise insufficient-stock contract verbatim — `InsufficientStockError` caught, `db.rollback()` drops the orphan movement, item reloaded via `_get_item_or_404`, form re-rendered at HTTP 400 with `<p data-testid="stock-adjust-error">Not enough stock: requested {N}, only {M} available.</p>` block + qty / direction / unit_cost / reason / note all preserved.

- **Two new helpers** (added near the existing `_parse_*` helpers): `_parse_required_reason(raw) -> str` (strip; blank → 400 — distinct from M2 / M3 where reason is optional, because MISSION §3 requires variance attribution); `_parse_direction(raw) -> str` (must be `"increase"` or `"decrease"` — anything else 400). New `_render_stock_adjust_form` factors GET-and-error rendering symmetric with M3's `_render_stock_out_form` (the same parametric error path on the only data-dependent failure case in this route — same carve-out justification as M3).
- **Engine wiring**: route never touches `cost_layers.qty_remaining`, `cost_layer_consumptions.*`, `movement.total_cost`, or `item.current_qty`. Increase: `record_receipt` is the single owner. Decrease: `consume_fifo` is the single owner. Caller pattern is identical to M2 / M3.
- **Audit shape**: `action="stock_movement.adjustment"`, `entity_type="stock_movement"`, `entity_id=movement.id`, `before=None`, `after`:
  - **Increase**: `{item_id, qty, direction="increase", unit_cost, total_cost, source="positive_adjustment", reason, note, received_at}`. Decimal scale on `total_cost` is the input scale (e.g. `"12.50"` for `5 × 2.50`) because `record_receipt` computes the product in memory before the column round-trip.
  - **Decrease**: `{item_id, qty, direction, total_cost, reason, note}`. **No `unit_cost` / `source` / `received_at`** (varies per layer; matches M3's stock-out audit shape). `total_cost` carries the column-quantised scale 4 (e.g. `"8.0000"`) because the engine reads `layer.unit_cost` back from `Numeric(14,4)` storage — same wart as M3's stock-out audit.
- **`unit_cost` field is rendered for both directions** but only parsed + required for increase. For decrease, garbage in the field is accepted (and ignored). The form's `<em>required for increases; ignored for decreases</em>` hint is the user-facing cue. Conservative: doesn't need HTMX swap (still no concrete second use case for HTMX).
- **Templates**: new `stock_adjust_form.html` mirroring `stock_out_form.html` with the addition of a `direction` `<select>` (`stock-adjust-direction-input` test-id; both `increase` and `decrease` options) and the always-rendered `unit_cost` input. Reason input is HTML-required + `*`-marked. Test-ids: `stock-adjust-form`, `stock-adjust-qty-input`, `stock-adjust-direction-input`, `stock-adjust-unit-cost-input`, `stock-adjust-reason-input`, `stock-adjust-note-input`, `stock-adjust-submit`, `stock-adjust-error`. `items_form.html` gains a third `data-testid="stock-adjust-link"` "Adjust →" link in the same `{% if not item.archived_at %}` block as in / out.
- **Test coverage** (`tests/integration/test_movements_routes.py` 45 new + `tests/e2e/test_movements_e2e.py` extension):
  - Role enforcement (10): anon GET / POST 401; pending 403; Workshop / Office / Manager / Admin all 200 GET / 303 POST. Increase POST tests don't need a seed; decrease POST tests in this matrix go through the increase path so a layer isn't needed.
  - Form rendering (5): inputs + CSRF + both directions + reason marked required; current_qty + open_value surfaced; recent-movements empty state; unknown 404; archived 400.
  - Validation matrix (16): qty blank / zero / negative / non-numeric (4); direction blank / invalid (2); reason blank / whitespace-only (2); unit_cost on increase blank / negative / non-numeric (3); zero unit_cost on increase allowed (1); unit_cost ignored on decrease (1); unknown 404 + archived 400 on POST (2); failed validation writes no audit (1).
  - Increase happy path (4): creates `StockMovement(type=ADJUSTMENT)` + `CostLayer(source=POSITIVE_ADJUSTMENT)` + bumps current_qty; total_cost = qty × unit_cost (e.g. `60.00`); audit content with `direction=increase`, `unit_cost`, `source`, `received_at` present; whitespace strip on reason / note; flash includes `+qty`.
  - Decrease happy path (4): creates `StockMovement(type=ADJUSTMENT)` + `CostLayerConsumption` rows + decrements current_qty; total_cost is layer-weighted; audit content with `direction=decrease`, no unit_cost / source / received_at; blank-note-becomes-None; flash includes `-qty`.
  - Insufficient stock on decrease (3): atomic rollback (no movement / consumption / qty mutation; layer.qty_remaining unchanged); in-form error block + preserved inputs (incl. direction value); no audit on insufficient stock.
  - Multi-layer FIFO on decrease (1): two layers (4 @ 2.00 + 6 @ 3.00, distinct received_at), decrease 7 → consumes 4 from old + 3 from new; total_cost = 4×2 + 3×3 = 17.00; consumption rows ordered correctly; current_qty = 3.
  - Adjust link on edit form (2): visible for active item; hidden for archived.
  - E2E walk extension: after the existing OUT + insufficient-stock legs (current_qty=70 at that point), workshop deep-links to `/admin/items/{id}/adjust`. Leg 1 (increase): qty=20, unit_cost=3.00, reason="found extra" → flash with `+20`, current_qty=90, recent-movements row with reason + 20 + 60. Leg 2 (decrease): qty=15, reason="damaged batch" → flash with `-15`, current_qty=75, recent-movements row.

**Manual stock-out route (M3):** `app/movements.py` gains two more routes mounted under `/admin/items` for **Manager + Office + Workshop**: `GET /admin/items/{item_id}/out` renders a form (qty + reason + note — *no* unit_cost; consumption price is per-layer, not per-movement) plus the existing recent-movements table and a new "open value" summary line (sum across the item's open FIFO layers, computed via `open_value`); `POST /admin/items/{item_id}/out` validates, builds a `StockMovement(type=OUT)`, flushes for an id, calls `consume_fifo(db, item=..., qty=..., movement=...)`, writes a `stock_movement.out` audit row, commits, 303s back with a flash. The handler-level body mirrors `record_stock_in` line-for-line (different engine call + audit action + redirect), so the helper set introduced by M2 (`_parse_positive_decimal`, `_get_item_or_404`, `_reject_archived`, `_flash`, `_recent_movements`) is reused as-is. One new helper: `_render_stock_out_form` factors the GET-and-error rendering paths so the insufficient-stock 400 path doesn't fork.

- **Insufficient-stock path (the new shape choice in M3):** the engine raises `InsufficientStockError(item_id, requested, available)` *before* any mutation (atomic-on-raise tested in M1). The route catches the error, calls `db.rollback()` (drops the unflushed `StockMovement` we added before the engine call — the engine itself never mutated anything, so the rollback's only job is to discard the orphan movement row), reloads the item via `_get_item_or_404` (because the rolled-back transaction left the original `item` reference detached), and re-renders the form via `_render_stock_out_form` with HTTP 400, the user's qty / reason / note preserved in the inputs, and an `<p data-testid="stock-out-error" role="alert">` block carrying the message "Not enough stock: requested {N}, only {M} available." This is the **only** form in the app today that re-renders on validation 400 — every other settings form (suppliers / locations / taxonomy / field-defs / items / item-units / stock-in) lets a 400 land on FastAPI's bare exception page. The carve-out is justified because insufficient-stock is a *data-dependent* failure (changes minute-by-minute as other actors consume) where typing the form again is more friction than re-typing a typo. The other validation 400s (blank qty, negative qty, archived item, etc.) follow the existing convention — bare 400 — so this is one carve-out, not a new pattern. Self-critique flags the inconsistency for a future "in-form errors" sweep across all seven forms.
- **Engine wiring**: route never touches `cost_layers.qty_remaining`, `cost_layer_consumptions.*`, `movement.total_cost`, or `item.current_qty` — those are M1's invariants and `consume_fifo` is the single owner. Caller pattern is the same as M2: `db.add(movement); db.flush(); consume_fifo(...); record_audit(...); db.commit()`. The route does not surface a backdated `created_at` UI in M3 — same gap as M2.
- **Audit shape**: `action="stock_movement.out"`, `entity_type="stock_movement"`, `entity_id=movement.id`, `before=None`, `after={item_id, qty, total_cost, reason, note}`. **No `unit_cost`** (varies per layer — the layer-weighted sum is captured in `total_cost`). **No `source`** (consumes don't carry one). The layer-level breakdown is queryable from `cost_layer_consumptions WHERE movement_id = ?` — also append-only-by-engine per M1's contract — so duplicating it in the audit row would re-encode information already durably stored. Decimals are stringified via `str(decimal)` to preserve the column-quantised representation through JSON (the engine reads `layer.unit_cost` back from `Numeric(14,4)`, so `total_cost = qty * unit_cost` carries scale 4 — see the test for `total_cost == "8.0000"` not `"8"`).
- **Templates**: new `stock_out_form.html` — same shape as `stock_in_form.html` but without the unit_cost input, with an "Open value" summary line (`data-testid="item-open-value"`), and with an `{% if error %}<p data-testid="stock-out-error" role="alert">` block above the form for the insufficient-stock case. Test-ids: `stock-out-form` / `stock-out-qty-input` / `stock-out-reason-input` / `stock-out-note-input` / `stock-out-submit` / `stock-out-error`. `items_form.html` gains a `data-testid="stock-out-link"` "Stock out →" link alongside the existing "Stock in →" link, on the same conditions (item not archived; visible to whoever can see the edit form — Manager + Office today).
- **Test coverage** (`tests/integration/test_movements_routes.py` 37 new + `tests/e2e/test_movements_e2e.py` extension = 37 integration + 1 e2e leg-pair):
  - Role enforcement (10): anonymous GET / POST 401, pending 403, Workshop / Office / Manager / Admin all succeed (200 GET / 303 POST). Role POST tests seed a layer first via `_seed_layer` (a tiny helper that goes through `record_receipt` so the seed itself exercises the receipt path).
  - Form rendering (7): inputs + CSRF present; no `name="unit_cost"` in the body; current_qty + open_value surfaced; open_value=0 for an item with no layers; recent-movements empty state; recent-movements populated after a seed; unknown item 404; archived item 400.
  - Validation (7): blank / zero / negative / non-numeric qty 400; unknown item 404 on POST; archived item 400 on POST; failed validation writes no audit row.
  - Happy path (5): single-layer consume creates `StockMovement(type=OUT)` with the right total_cost (3 × 2.50 = 7.50 for the headline assertion), one `CostLayerConsumption` row pointing at the right layer / movement / qty / unit_cost_at_consumption, decremented `layer.qty_remaining`, decremented `item.current_qty`; whitespace strip on reason + note; blank reason + note → None; audit row keys + values (incl. `total_cost == "8.0000"`, no `unit_cost`, no `source`); flash includes item name.
  - Insufficient stock (4): consume more than open layers → 400 + form re-rendered + error block + qty / reason / note preserved + no movement / consumption / current_qty / qty_remaining mutation; consume from item with no layers at all → 400 + error block; no audit row written on insufficient stock; consume *exactly* the open balance succeeds (303, layer drained to qty_remaining=0 but kept).
  - Multi-layer FIFO (2): two layers with distinct received_at → consume 7 of (4, 6) takes 4 from old + 3 from new; total_cost = 4×2.00 + 3×3.00 = 17.00; old layer drained, new partially consumed; consumption rows ordered correctly. Recent-movements list correctly shows both the seed IN and the new OUT for the same item.
  - Stock-out link (2): edit form shows the "Stock out →" link for an active item; hides it for an archived item.
  - E2E walk extension: after the existing stock-in step, workshop deep-links to `/admin/items/{id}/out`, asserts current_qty=100.0000 + open_value contains "250", fills qty=30 / reason="Production run", submits; flash, bumped current_qty=70.0000, OUT row showing "Production run" + 30 + 75 (total_cost = 30 × 2.50). Then a second leg: fills qty=1000, submits, asserts the `stock-out-error` block contains "Not enough stock", inputs preserved, current_qty unchanged at 70.0000.

**Manual stock-in route (M2):** `app/movements.py` exposes two routes mounted under `/admin/items` for **Manager + Office + Workshop**: `GET /admin/items/{item_id}/in` renders a form (qty + unit_cost + reason + note) plus a recent-movements table (last 10, newest first); `POST /admin/items/{item_id}/in` validates, builds a `StockMovement(type=IN)`, flushes for an id, calls `record_receipt(...)` with `source=MANUAL_IN`, writes a `stock_movement.in` audit row, commits, and 303s back to the same form with a flash. Workshop's first positive-write surface — CSRF + role gating both server-enforced.

- **Validation** (all 400, *before* any DB write so failures are atomic): `qty` parses as a strictly-positive `Decimal` (blank, zero, negative, non-numeric all reject); `unit_cost` parses as a non-negative `Decimal` (blank, negative, non-numeric reject; zero allowed for sample/gifted stock); `reason` and `note` stripped, blank → `None`. Item must exist (404) and not be archived (400 — same posture as taxonomy/items "no new structure under archived").
- **Engine wiring**: route never touches `cost_layers.qty_remaining`, `movement.total_cost`, or `item.current_qty` — those are M1's invariants and `record_receipt` is the single owner. Caller pattern is exactly what M1 documented: `db.add(movement); db.flush(); record_receipt(db, ..., movement=movement); record_audit(...); db.commit()`. The route does *not* set `received_at` to anything other than `now()` in M2 — backdated UI is deferred to PO5/M4 even though the engine supports it.
- **Audit shape**: `action="stock_movement.in"`, `entity_type="stock_movement"`, `entity_id=movement.id`, `before=None`, `after={item_id, qty, unit_cost, total_cost, source, reason, note, received_at}`. Decimals are stringified via `str(decimal)` to preserve precision through JSON (same convention as I2's custom-field audit shape). The cost layer and any future consumption rows are reconstructable from `cost_layers.source_movement_id` and `cost_layer_consumptions.movement_id`.
- **Templates**: new `stock_in_form.html` (page-shaped, not HTMX-partial — HTMX swap deferred until a second use case exists). Renders the form + a `data-testid="movements-table"` with one `data-testid="movement-row"` per recent movement (columns: when / type / qty / total_cost / actor / reason). Empty-state `data-testid="movements-empty"` when no movements yet. `items_form.html` gains a `data-testid="stock-in-link"` "Stock in →" link visible to the edit form's audience (Manager + Office) when the item is not archived.
- **Test coverage** (`tests/integration/test_movements_routes.py` 38 + `tests/e2e/test_movements_e2e.py` 1 = 39 new):
  - Role enforcement (10): anonymous GET 401, anonymous POST 401, pending 403, every active role (Workshop, Office, Manager, Admin) succeeds on GET 200 and POST 303.
  - Form rendering (6): inputs + CSRF present; current_qty surfaced; recent-movements empty state; recent-movements list populated (asserts row count via `data-testid="movement-row"`); unknown item 404; archived item 400.
  - Validation matrix (12): blank/zero/negative/non-numeric qty 400; blank/negative/non-numeric unit_cost 400; zero unit_cost allowed; unknown item 404 on POST; archived item 400 on POST; failed validation writes no audit row.
  - Happy path (6): single receipt creates movement (with type=IN, item_id, qty, user_id, reason, note, total_cost, po_id=None, stock_take_id=None) + cost layer (with qty_received=qty_remaining=qty, unit_cost, source=MANUAL_IN, source_movement_id=movement.id) + bumps item.current_qty; whitespace-strip on reason + note; blank reason + note → None; audit row keys + values; flash message after redirect; decimal precision preserved on qty + unit_cost.
  - Multi-receipt (3): two consecutive receipts create two layers with the right unit_costs + accumulate qty; recent-movements newest-first ordering; sibling items don't show each other's movements.
  - Stock-in link (2): edit form shows the "Stock in →" link for an active item; hides it for an archived item.
  - E2E walk (1): pending workshop user is admin-promoted; pending manager user is admin-promoted (admin signs in twice — once per promotion since role + status are two POSTs); manager creates a category + item; workshop deep-links to `/admin/items/{id}/in`, asserts the empty-movements state + zero current_qty, fills qty=100 / unit_cost=2.50 / reason="First receipt", submits, asserts the flash + bumped current_qty=100.0000 + the new movement row showing the reason + qty + total_cost (250). Cleanup archives the item + the category.

**FIFO cost engine (M1):** `app/cost_engine.py` exposes three pure functions and one exception. The engine is the single owner of `item.current_qty`, `cost_layers.qty_remaining`, and `stock_movements.total_cost` going forward — every M2-M6 / PO5 / ST-series route must call into it rather than touching those columns directly.

- `record_receipt(db, *, item, qty, unit_cost, source, movement, received_at=None) -> CostLayer` — creates a layer with `qty_received=qty_remaining=qty`, increments `item.current_qty`, sets `movement.total_cost = qty * unit_cost`. Validates `qty > 0`, `unit_cost >= 0` (zero allowed for sample/gifted stock), and that `movement.id` is set (caller must `db.flush()` first).
- `consume_fifo(db, *, item, qty, movement) -> Decimal` — walks open layers in `(received_at ASC, id ASC)` order, creates one `CostLayerConsumption` per layer touched, decrements `qty_remaining`, accumulates total cost, decrements `item.current_qty`, sets `movement.total_cost`. Atomic — raises `InsufficientStockError(item_id, requested, available)` *before any mutation* if open layers don't sum to `qty`. Validates `qty > 0` and flushed movement.
- `open_value(db, item) -> Decimal` — read-only sum of `qty_remaining * unit_cost` across the item's layers with `qty_remaining > 0`. Returns `Decimal("0")` for an item with no open layers.

**Schema (migration `0010_create_cost_layers_and_movements.py`):** three new tables, in dependency order (`stock_movements` first so the cost tables can FK into it).

- `stock_movements`: `id, item_id (FK RESTRICT, NOT NULL), item_unit_id (FK RESTRICT nullable), type (String(16), SAEnum-backed: in/out/adjustment/transfer), qty (Numeric(14,4)), user_id (FK SET NULL nullable), reason (String(255) nullable), note (String(2000) nullable), po_id (Integer nullable, NO FK in M1), stock_take_id (Integer nullable, NO FK in M1), total_cost (Numeric(14,4) nullable — engine sets it), created_at`. Five indexes: per-item, per-item_unit, per-user, per-type, per-created_at. `po_id` and `stock_take_id` are plain integers (no FK) because the `purchase_orders` and `stock_takes` tables don't exist yet — the FK constraint is added in PO2 / ST1's migration.
- `cost_layers`: `id, item_id (FK RESTRICT, NOT NULL), qty_received (Numeric(14,4) NOT NULL — immutable post-insert), qty_remaining (Numeric(14,4) NOT NULL — only the engine decrements this), unit_cost (Numeric(14,4) NOT NULL — immutable), received_at (DateTime(tz) NOT NULL — caller-supplied or now()), source (String(20), SAEnum-backed: po_receipt/manual_in/positive_adjustment), source_movement_id (FK stock_movements.id RESTRICT NOT NULL), created_at`. Three indexes: per-item, per-source_movement, plus the composite `ix_cost_layers_item_received` on `(item_id, received_at, id)` that covers the FIFO ORDER BY.
