---

**Self-critique notes (rolling) — R5g:**

- **Pattern is fully mechanical at seven surfaces.** Same shape as R5f: ~8 LoC route + ~5 LoC template + 19 tests. Adding an eighth CSV surface (e.g. movements list, users list, reorder dashboard, checkouts admin) is now copy-paste-modify. R5e's `csv_branch` helper continues to pay for itself: a new surface no longer thinks about magic strings, Content-Type, or sanitisation.
- **Sub-category list (`list_sub_categories`) deliberately excluded.** That route is per-parent (`/admin/taxonomy/{parent_id}/children`), so a single CSV would either need a parent-id-in-filename convention (`taxonomy_sub_{parent_id}_{show}.csv`) or scope-across-all-parents semantics (which the current route doesn't support). Trade-off: the per-parent CSV is mechanically the same as the top-level CSV (just one extra filter), but the URL convention divergence means it's a separate slice's worth of decisions. Queued informally as R5h. Flagged.
- **`leaf_ids` lookup ordering preserved.** The CSV branch sits *before* the `leaf_ids` query, so `?format=csv` skips that round-trip entirely. The HTML branch still runs it (no behaviour change for HTML). Net win: CSV is one DB query, HTML is two — same shape as R5f's locations CSV (locations also have no extra HTML-only query, but the principle holds).
- **`archived_at` not in CSV body.** Same posture as R5d / R5f — the filename encodes the active partition; an extra column would be redundant given the `?show=` filter. A user wanting both buckets in one file would have to download two files and concat. Acceptable for v1; flagged.
- **`created_at` / `updated_at` not in CSV.** The HTML view also hides these; the CSV mirrors HTML one-for-one. A historian wanting "when was each category added" hits the audit log instead. Same posture as R5d / R5f. Documented.
- **Sub-category exclusion test** (`test_sub_categories_not_in_csv`) — pins that the `parent_id IS NULL` filter survives any future refactor of the query. Without this, a refactor that accidentally widened the scope (e.g. removing the `parent_id` filter, or joining sub-cats in for a new feature) wouldn't fail the existing tests. Cheap insurance; worth it.
- **CSV-injection mitigation still not applied.** Category names are manager-typed; recipients are office/manager colleagues with HTML access to the same data. Same v1 risk model as R5/R5b/R5c/R5d/R5f; the one-line `_coerce_cell` mitigation lands when the threat model changes. Documented.
- **No e2e walk for the CSV link.** Same posture as R5f — Playwright doesn't simulate the OS file-save dialog, and the link visibility is pinned by integration tests. Existing `test_taxonomy_e2e.py` already exercises the HTML page end-to-end; clicking the CSV link would only re-test what the integration tests pin. Flagged.
- **Workshop + Office + Pending all gated to 403 at the dependency layer.** Pinned by `TestTaxonomyListCsvRoleEnforcement`'s six tests. The HTML page also doesn't render to those roles, so a "link absence" test isn't needed here — the link only renders when the page renders, and the page only renders to Manager + Admin. Same posture as R5d / R5f.
- **`format` param shadows Python's `format()` builtin** — same wart as R5/R5b/R5c/R5d/R5f. Seven surfaces now, all shadowing. Renaming would break the URL convention. Acceptable.
- **Return type widened on `list_taxonomy` from `HTMLResponse` to `Response`.** Necessary because the CSV branch returns a non-HTML `Response`. The `@router.get` decorator's `response_class` argument was dropped (only affects OpenAPI hint generation; runtime behaviour unchanged). No callers depend on the narrower type. `HTMLResponse` import retained — still used by `/new` + `/{id}/edit` + sub-category form routes.
- **No new helper module.** Header constant + rows helper sit in `app/taxonomy.py` next to the route — same shape as the six prior surfaces. The cross-cutting concerns (filename sanitisation, cell coercion, Content-Type/Disposition shaping, the CSV-vs-HTML branch decision) all live in `app/csv_export.py`; the per-surface concerns (which columns, what filename pattern, what data shape) stay local. The split feels right at seven surfaces.
- **`TaxonomyNode` ORM model passed directly to the rows helper** — same shape as R5d/R5f. No join + count needed (unlike R5's PO list); the helper just reads attributes. Documented.

<!-- R5e plan (now shipped) — kept commented for audit-trail context only.

**R5e — `csv_branch` helper extraction (refactor — collapses 5 duplicate branches into one helper):** queued by R5d's self-critique. With five surfaces now carrying the same `if format == "csv": return csv_response(...)` block (variance trend + PO list + items list + stock-takes list + suppliers list), the indirection finally pays its way. Pure refactor; existing CSV tests pass unchanged. No DoD impact, no MISSION-§3 surface change — reduces tech debt for the next CSV surface.

- **Helper** (`app/csv_export.py`): new `csv_branch(format_value, *, filename, headers, rows) -> Response | None`. Returns `csv_response(...)` when `format_value == "csv"`, else `None`. Preserves the same kwargs-only call shape and the same coercion / filename-sanitisation semantics — it's literally `if format_value != "csv": return None` followed by a delegated `csv_response(...)` call.

- **Why None vs. raise**: a None return lets each call site use the walrus operator pattern `if (resp := csv_branch(...)): return resp` — the route's HTML-render path stays explicit on the next line. An exception-based design would force `try/except` at every site and obscure the HTML branch. The current `format == "csv"` test is exactly this pattern; the helper just hides one line of it.

- **Migration of the 5 call sites**:
  - `app/reports.py::variance_trend` (variance trend report) — `format` is read inline from `request.query_params.get("format")`; collapses cleanly.
  - `app/purchase_orders.py::list_purchase_orders` (PO list) — `format` is a typed `Form()`-style query param.
  - `app/items.py::list_items` (items list) — uses `is_csv = format == "csv"` for an early role-gate (Workshop blocked from CSV). The role-gate stays as-is using `is_csv`; only the response-build branch collapses to `csv_branch`. Two distinct concerns; keeping them separate preserves readability.
  - `app/stock_takes.py::list_stock_takes` (stock-takes list).
  - `app/suppliers.py::list_suppliers` (suppliers list).

- **No call-site behaviour change**: same filename, same headers, same rows. Existing integration tests (`TestVarianceTrendCsvBody` / `TestVarianceTrendCsvHeaders` / etc. across all five surfaces) verify the unchanged contract.

- **`format_value` param name**: chose `format_value` (not `format`, not `fmt`) to avoid shadowing the Python builtin in the helper's body. The call sites still use `format` as the local URL-param variable — that shadow already exists at the route level and renaming there is out of scope (would touch the URL convention).

- **Test coverage** (`tests/unit/test_csv_export.py` 5 new):
  - `TestCsvBranch::test_returns_none_when_format_is_blank` — `csv_branch("", ...)` returns None.
  - `TestCsvBranch::test_returns_none_when_format_is_html` — `csv_branch("html", ...)` returns None.
  - `TestCsvBranch::test_returns_none_when_format_is_garbage` — `csv_branch("xml", ...)` returns None.
  - `TestCsvBranch::test_returns_response_when_format_is_csv` — `csv_branch("csv", ...)` returns a Response with the right Content-Type + Content-Disposition.
  - `TestCsvBranch::test_csv_branch_delegates_body_through_csv_response` — content of returned Response matches what `csv_response` would produce directly with the same args (header + data row + CRLF).

- **No new integration tests**: the existing CSV integration tests on all five surfaces remain the contract for end-to-end behaviour. Adding integration tests for the helper would be redundant (the unit tests pin the helper; the existing integrations pin the call-site delegation).

- **Repo health target**: ruff clean; mypy clean (27 source files unchanged); pytest unit + integration 1542 passing (was 1537, +5 new helper tests); Playwright 14 passing (no count change).

-->

---

**Self-critique notes (rolling) — R5e:**

- **LoC at each call site barely changed** — went from a 6-line `if format == "csv": return csv_response(...)` block to a 9-line `if (resp := csv_branch(...)) is not None: return resp` walrus block (the `csv_branch` keyword args are identical and span 4 lines either way). The R5d note had estimated "collapse to one line"; in practice the multi-line kwargs prevent a one-liner. **The real win is conceptual centralization**, not LoC: the magic string `"csv"` now lives in exactly one place (`app/csv_export.py::csv_branch`), so a future surface adds one call to `csv_branch` instead of remembering "what format value triggers CSV". Future polish slices that want to e.g. accept `?format=CSV` (case-insensitive) or `?download=csv` (alias) now have a single edit point instead of five.
- **Walrus + `is not None` ceremony** is intentional. A bare `if (resp := csv_branch(...)):` would treat any falsy `Response` as "no CSV branch", but FastAPI Responses are always truthy, so practically it'd work — `is not None` is the explicit form and matches the helper's `Response | None` signature. Five sites all use the same shape; uniform.
- **`csv_branch` returns `None`, doesn't raise.** Considered raising a `BranchNotMatched` exception with `try/except` at each call site, but that obscures the HTML render path behind exception handling for a non-error condition (`format != "csv"` is the *common* path). The walrus + None pattern keeps the HTML branch on the next line.
- **`format_value` param is positional-only by convention** (no `/` marker — the codebase doesn't use position-only syntax elsewhere). Routes pass it positionally; `filename` / `headers` / `rows` are kwargs. Rationale: the format value is the *condition* for the branch (always first positional arg), the response shape is the *content* (kwargs match `csv_response`'s shape verbatim).
- **`is_csv` flag in `app/items.py` was preserved** — it gates the role check (Workshop is allowed to see the items list HTML but not the CSV) which runs *before* the format-branch decision. The role gate and the response branch are two distinct concerns; collapsing the role check into the helper would force the helper to know about role tuples, which breaks its single-responsibility shape (response building, not authorization). Same posture would apply if a future CSV surface needs a similar pre-gate.
- **`rows` is computed eagerly even when the format isn't CSV.** All five call sites already build `rows` before the format check (the same data drives both HTML and CSV), so passing rows eagerly to `csv_branch` doesn't add work. If a future surface wanted rows lazily-computed only when CSV is requested, the helper would need a callable param (`rows_factory: Callable[[], Iterable[Iterable[Any]]]`) — flagged but not done; YAGNI for v1.
- **No call-site behaviour change.** All existing CSV integration tests across all five surfaces (variance trend, PO list, items list, stock-takes list, suppliers list — ~76 integration tests across them) pass unchanged. The 5 new unit tests pin the helper's contract: returns None for blank / "html" / garbage; returns Response with correct Content-Type + Content-Disposition for "csv"; body matches `csv_response` direct-call output.
- **Helper sits in `app/csv_export.py` next to `csv_response`** because both are response-shaping utilities for the same surface. A separate module would be over-engineering at two helpers (csv_response + csv_branch); flagged for revisit if the file grows past ~200 LoC.
- **Walrus + parenthesis layout** is verbose (`if (resp := csv_branch(...)) is not None: return resp`) and ruff is happy with it. An alternative `resp = csv_branch(...); if resp is not None: return resp` is one line shorter but loses the "branch decision is one expression" framing. Left as-is across all 5 sites for consistency; flagged.
- **No `csv_branch` integration tests added.** The helper is delegation-thin (one `if` + a delegated call); the unit tests cover its contract directly, and the existing integration tests on all 5 routes verify that the call-site delegation works end-to-end (a regression in `csv_branch` would surface as a 200 HTML response when CSV was requested, which the existing `test_content_type_is_csv` and `test_content_disposition_default_filename` style tests already catch).
- **`reports.py`'s call site reads `format` inline from `request.query_params.get("format", "")`** rather than promoting it to a typed `format: str = ""` route param. Keeps the parameter list short (the route only needs `request` + `db` + `user`); the param shadowing concern that the other 4 sites have (where `format` shadows the Python builtin in the function body) is sidestepped. Flagged as a minor inconsistency — could be unified later as a polish pass; both shapes work.



<!-- R5d plan (now shipped) — kept commented for audit-trail context only.

**R5d — CSV export on the suppliers list (DoD #7 polish, MISSION §3 "Export any list view to CSV"):** extends `app/suppliers.py::list_suppliers` with a `?format=csv` query branch and adds a `suppliers-list-csv-link` "Download CSV" link to `suppliers_list.html`. Fifth CSV surface, after R5's variance-trend + PO list, R5b's items list, and R5c's stock-takes list. Pattern reuses R5's `csv_response` helper unchanged.

- **Route extension** (`app/suppliers.py::list_suppliers`):
  - New `format` query param (default `""`). `format == "csv"` triggers the CSV branch; anything else (blank, `html`, garbage) renders the existing HTML — same silent-coerce posture as `show`.
  - **Role gate inherited**: the existing `Depends(require_role(Role.MANAGER))` already blocks Workshop + Office + pending at the dependency layer (suppliers are Manager-owned per MISSION §3). Admin always passes via `require_role`. No inner role-split needed.
  - Same data source as the HTML branch.
  - **Headers** (5 columns): `id`, `name`, `email`, `phone`, `notes`. The `archived_at` column is *not* exposed because the filename already encodes the filter (`suppliers_active.csv` vs `suppliers_archived.csv`).

---

**Self-critique notes (rolling) — R5d:**

- **Pattern is now ripe for `csv_branch` helper extraction.** R5c's self-critique flagged: "Not worth it yet at four surfaces; flagged once a fifth lands." R5d *is* the fifth. Five routes now carry the same shape:
  ```python
  if format == "csv":
      return csv_response(
          filename=...,
          headers=_X_CSV_HEADERS,
          rows=_csv_rows_for_x(...),
      )
  ```
  A `csv_branch(format, *, filename, headers, rows) -> Response | None` helper would collapse ~6 LoC at each call site to one. Estimated savings ~25 LoC across five routes. Trade-off: an indirection vs. line savings; the explicit shape currently in each route is locally readable. **Queueing R5e — `csv_branch` helper extraction** as the natural next slice (mechanical refactor, no DoD impact, but reduces tech debt for the next CSV surface). Not done in R5d because it would mix a feature slice with a refactor.
- **`archived_at` is not a column in the CSV body.** Trade-off vs R5's PO list which exposes `supplier_archived` because the PO list mixes archive states (no `?show` filter on archive-status — the filter is by status). Suppliers list partitions by `?show=active|archived`, so the filename does the work; an extra column would be redundant. A user wanting both buckets in one file would have to download two files and concat. Acceptable for v1; flagged.
- **`created_at` / `updated_at` not exposed.** The HTML view also hides these; the CSV mirrors the HTML one-for-one. A historian wanting "when was each supplier added" would have to hit the audit log instead. Same posture as R5b's items CSV (which also doesn't carry timestamps). Documented.
- **Filename uses the *coerced* `show`.** A user typing `?format=csv&show=garbage` gets `suppliers_active.csv` (not `suppliers_garbage.csv`). Same posture as R5c. Pinned indirectly by the default-filename test (no explicit show → active).
- **CSV-injection mitigation still not applied.** Supplier names + notes are manager-typed; recipients are office/manager colleagues with HTML access to the same data. Same v1 risk model as R5 / R5b / R5c; the one-line `_coerce_cell` mitigation lands when the threat model changes. Documented.
- **No e2e walk for the CSV link.** Same posture as R5 / R5b / R5c — Playwright doesn't simulate the OS file-save dialog, and the link visibility is already pinned by the integration tests. Flagged.
- **Workshop + Office + Pending all gated to 403 at the dependency layer.** Pinned by `TestSuppliersListCsvRoleEnforcement`'s six tests. The HTML page also doesn't render to those roles, so a "link absence" test isn't needed here — the link only renders when the page renders, and the page only renders to Manager + Admin.
- **`format` param shadows Python's `format()` builtin** — same wart as R5 / R5b / R5c. Benign; renaming would break the URL convention. Acceptable.
- **Return type widened on `list_suppliers` from `HTMLResponse` to `Response`.** Necessary because the CSV branch returns a non-HTML `Response`. The `@router.get` decorator's `response_class` argument was dropped (only affects OpenAPI hint generation; runtime behaviour unchanged). No callers depend on the narrower type.
- **No new helper module.** The CSV header constant and rows helper sit in `app/suppliers.py` next to the route, same as the four prior surfaces. If `csv_branch` extraction lands as R5e, the constants and rows helpers stay where they are; only the call-site shape collapses.
- **`Supplier` ORM model passed directly to the rows helper.** Other surfaces pass view-shaped dicts (e.g. PO list passes `(po, supplier_name, supplier_archived, line_count, created_at)` rows). Suppliers don't need a join + count, so the ORM model is enough; the helper just reads attributes. Documented.

---

**Self-critique notes (rolling) — R5c:**

- **`format=csv` is a route-internal split, not a separate route.** Same posture as R5 / R5b — the same path serves HTML and CSV depending on a query param. Pattern is now well-established across four routes (variance trend, PO list, items list, stock-takes list).
- **Pattern ripe for a tiny generalisation pass.** Four CSVs use the same `format == "csv"` branch + `csv_response(filename, headers, rows)` call shape; a `csv_branch(format, *, filename, headers, rows) -> Response | None` helper could collapse the ~5 LoC at each call site to one. Trade-off: an indirection vs. line savings (~12 LoC total across four routes). Not worth it yet at four surfaces; flagged once a fifth lands.
- **Filename uses the *coerced* `show`.** A user typing `?format=csv&show=garbage` gets `stock_takes_open.csv` (not `stock_takes_garbage.csv`) because `_coerce_show` runs before the filename is built. This is the right posture — the CSV body is the open list, so the filename should match. Pinned by `TestStockTakesListCsvHeaders::test_content_disposition_default_filename` (no explicit show → open) and the body content tests; an explicit unknown-show test would only re-verify the coercion logic that the existing `TestList::test_unrecognised_show_falls_through_to_open` already pins.
- **`created_by_email` cell is empty (not `—`) when the creator was deleted.** The HTML view renders `—` for visual contrast; the CSV uses an empty string because spreadsheet receivers expect missing values as blanks (`—` would parse as text and break a NULL filter). Pinned by `TestStockTakesListCsvBody::test_deleted_creator_renders_empty_email_cell`.
- **`created_at` is the raw `datetime.isoformat()`** (e.g. `2026-05-07T14:30:00.123456+00:00`). Same trade-off as the PO list CSV: spreadsheet receivers can parse it, but a date-only column might be friendlier. Picked full-fidelity to match the PO list's posture; flagged for a polish slice that could quantise across surfaces.
- **`scheduled_for` is a `date` (not a `datetime`).** The CSV cell renders as `2026-06-01` via `_coerce_cell`'s `date.isoformat()` branch — the right posture for spreadsheet receivers (no spurious time component). Verified by `TestStockTakesListCsvBody::test_one_stock_take_one_data_row` checking `cells[2] == "2026-06-01"`.
- **`scope` cell carries the human-readable label** (e.g. `Category: Tools`, `Location: Workshop bench`, `All items`) rather than two separate `scope_node_id` / `scope_location_id` columns. Trade-off: human-readable for a CSV consumer vs. machine-joinable. Picked human-readable to match the HTML rendering one-for-one. The `id` column at the start is the join key for any consumer who needs to follow the FK back; `_list_rows` exposes only the label, not the underlying ids, and changing the data shape would have rippled into the existing list tests. Flagged.
- **Workshop is server-side gated to 403** at the dependency layer (the route is `Manager + Office` only). No inner role-split was needed — unlike R5b's items list where Workshop *can* see the HTML but not the CSV. Pinned by `TestStockTakesListCsvRoleEnforcement::test_workshop_csv_is_403`. The HTML page also doesn't render to Workshop, so the link visibility test isn't needed.
- **CSV-injection mitigation still not applied.** Stock-take scope labels are derived from manager-typed taxonomy node names + location names; recipients are office colleagues with HTML access to the same data. Same v1 risk model as R5 / R5b; the one-line mitigation in `_coerce_cell` lands when the threat model changes. Documented.
- **No `?node_id` / `?location_id` filter exists on the stock-takes list.** Unlike the items list (which has a `?node_id` URL filter) and the PO list (which has `?status_filter`), the stock-takes list only supports `?show=open|completed`. The CSV inherits the same filter set. If a future polish slice adds per-scope filters, they'd flow into the CSV branch automatically (the data source is shared).
- **No movements list / suppliers list / locations list / categories list / users list CSV yet.** R5c brings the surface count to 4 (variance trend, PO list, items list, stock-takes list). The remaining list views aren't viewing data shaped like reports; the natural next surfaces if the user asks are movements (per-item timeline on item detail) and suppliers (a real list view but small data). Documented.
- **No new e2e walk.** Same posture as R5 / R5b — the existing stock-takes e2e already lands on the list, and clicking "Download CSV" would only re-test the link visibility the integration tests pin. Playwright doesn't simulate the OS file-save dialog. Flagged.
- **Return type widened on `list_stock_takes` from `HTMLResponse` to `Response`.** Necessary because the CSV branch returns a non-HTML `Response`. Same posture as R5b's items-list change — `@router.get("")` decorator's `response_class` argument was dropped (only affects OpenAPI hint generation; runtime behaviour unchanged). No callers depend on the narrower type.
- **`format` param shadows Python's `format()` builtin** — same wart as R5 / R5b. The function never calls `format()`, so the shadow is benign; renaming would break the URL convention (`?format=csv`). Acceptable.



<!-- R5 plan (now shipped) — kept commented for audit-trail context only.

- **New module `app/csv_export.py`** with one helper function:
  - `csv_response(*, filename, headers, rows) -> Response` — builds a `text/csv; charset=utf-8` response with `Content-Disposition: attachment; filename="<name>.csv"`. Uses Python stdlib `csv.writer` over an `io.StringIO` (no third-party dep needed; `csv` is RFC 4180-ish with `QUOTE_MINIMAL`). The body uses `\r\n` line terminators (RFC 4180 + the default `csv.writer` behaviour for compatibility with Excel-on-Windows). `headers` is a list of column names; `rows` is an iterable of lists/tuples of cell values. Cell coercion: `None` → `""`; `Decimal` / `int` / `float` → `str(value)`; `datetime` → `value.isoformat()`; `date` → `value.isoformat()`; everything else → `str(value)`. Filename is sanitised: ASCII-safe, no quotes/semicolons (so the `Content-Disposition` header doesn't break) — `_safe_filename(name)` replaces non-`[A-Za-z0-9_.-]` chars with `_`.
  - The helper is pure (no DB, no Request, no audit) — testable in isolation.

- **Variance trend CSV** (extends `app/reports.py`):
  - The existing `GET /admin/reports/variance-trend` route grows a `format` query param. `format=csv` triggers the CSV branch; anything else (blank, `html`, garbage) renders the existing HTML — same silent-coerce posture as the `days` param.
  - Same data source: `_load_trend_rows(db, days=days)`. No new aggregation logic.
  - **Headers**: `stock_take_id`, `scope`, `scheduled_for`, `completed_at`, `lines_with_variance`, `positive_variance`, `negative_variance_abs`, `net_variance`, `abs_variance`. Nine columns mirroring the HTML table cells one-for-one.
  - **One row per stock take**; no totals row (the receiver of the CSV can sum it themselves; emitting a totals row mid-data confuses downstream tools that expect every row to have the same shape).
  - **Empty result** → CSV with just the header row (still useful as a "we ran the report and found nothing" artefact; consistent with how the HTML always renders the totals card with zeros). Pinned.
  - **Filename**: `variance_trend_{days}d.csv` so the window is self-documenting in the receiver's downloads folder.
  - The CSV branch ignores the `days=foo` coercion the same way the HTML branch does (silent coerce to default). Pinned.
  - Extends `_load_trend_rows`'s output usage — no new helper there.

- **PO list CSV** (extends `app/purchase_orders.py`):
  - The existing `GET /admin/purchase-orders` route grows a `format` query param. Same silent-coerce posture as the `status_filter` param ("anything-not-csv" → HTML).
  - Same data source: the existing `select(PurchaseOrder, Supplier).join(...)` query plus the per-row `_count_lines` fetch.
  - **Headers**: `po_id`, `supplier`, `supplier_archived`, `status`, `line_count`, `created_at`. Six columns. The `supplier_archived` column emits the literal string `"yes"` or `"no"` (not `"true"`/`"false"`) because spreadsheet receivers tend to find yes/no easier to filter than a boolean column; documented in the helper.
  - **Filename**: `purchase_orders_{status_filter}.csv` (e.g. `purchase_orders_all.csv`, `purchase_orders_draft.csv`).
  - Status filter applies before the CSV is built — same WHERE clause as the HTML branch.
  - Empty result → header row only.

- **HTML link surfaces** (one per page):
  - `variance_trend.html` gains a `<a data-testid="variance-trend-csv-link" href="/admin/reports/variance-trend?format=csv&days={{ days }}">Download CSV</a>` link near the form. The href preserves the active `days` param so a user who widened the window gets a CSV of the same window.
  - `purchase_orders_list.html` gains a `<a data-testid="po-list-csv-link" href="/admin/purchase-orders?format=csv&status_filter={{ status_filter }}">Download CSV</a>` link near the filter. The href preserves the active `status_filter`.

- **Role enforcement preserved**: the CSV branch sits *inside* the existing routes, so the `Depends(require_role(...))` already gates Workshop + pending. Anon hits the `require_role` dependency and 401s before reaching the format check. Pinned for both surfaces.

- **Read-only invariant preserved**: the CSV branch is a read+render; no audit, no mutation. Pinned by extending the existing `TestVarianceTrendReadOnly` test class.

- **Test coverage** (target: ~30 new tests):
  - Unit (`tests/unit/test_csv_export.py` — new file, ~15 tests):
    - `TestCsvResponse`: response media type carries the charset; Content-Disposition has the filename; filename quoted; the body is the header row joined with the data rows; `\r\n` line terminator; empty rows still emits a header row; embedded commas / quotes / newlines escaped per RFC 4180; `None` → empty string; `Decimal("3.50")` → `"3.50"`; `datetime`/`date` → `isoformat()`.
    - `TestSafeFilename`: ASCII-safe; whitespace / quotes / semicolons replaced with `_`; preserves dots and dashes; preserves underscores.
  - Integration — variance trend (extends `tests/integration/test_reports_routes.py`, ~9 new tests):
    - Role enforcement (CSV inherits the role check): anon / pending / Workshop CSV → 401/403; Manager / Office CSV → 200.
    - Content-Type + Content-Disposition: `text/csv; charset=utf-8` and `attachment; filename="variance_trend_90d.csv"` for default; `..._30d.csv` for `?days=30`.
    - Header row always present even when no rows.
    - One row per stock take; CSV cell values match the aggregates.
    - Days filter applies (100-day-old completion absent at default 90, present at `?days=200`).

- **CSV-injection mitigation**: not applied. A field starting with `=`/`+`/`-`/`@` could be interpreted as a formula by Excel; the standard mitigation is to prepend a single quote. v1 risk model: all users are internal (Workshop is server-side blocked from these routes), the data is workshop inventory (supplier names + scope labels typed by managers), and a malicious payload would require a manager to attack a colleague — which is the same trust boundary the audit log already records. Documented in self-critique; flagged for a polish slice if a real CSV-injection concern arises.

- **No nav-level "Reports" entry**. R4 noted it'd be worth adding once a second `/admin/reports/*` page exists; R5 is just the CSV variant of the existing one, not a new page. The flag stays open for the next reports surface that lands.

The dashboard's COGS amount + top-consumed table also surface aggregations, and they're worth exporting too — but the dashboard is a multi-aggregation view, not a list view, and a "Download CSV" link there raises "which widget am I exporting?" UX questions. Out of scope for R5; flagged for a polish slice.

- **No CSV export on the items list / movements list / stock takes list / suppliers list / etc.** R5 lights up exactly the two surfaces named in MISSION §3's reporting bullet ("variance trends" + the PO list, which is a workhorse). Subsequent slices can extend the CSV pattern to other list views using the `csv_response` helper landed here.

---

**Self-critique notes (rolling) — R5b:**

- **`format=csv` query param is a route-internal split, not a separate route.** The same path serves HTML and CSV depending on a query param. Pro: the link href is just `?format=csv` away from the HTML page; CSP / role-gate / filter logic shared. Con: a developer reading the route handler sees a branchy function. Same posture as R5's two surfaces (variance trend + PO list); pattern is now well-established across three routes.
- **Workshop sees the items list HTML but not the CSV link.** A workshop user who manually types `?format=csv` into the URL bar gets a 403 (server-side gate is the canonical guard; the link absence is just UX). Pinned by `TestItemsListCsvRoleEnforcement::test_workshop_csv_is_403` and `TestItemsListCsvLink::test_html_hides_csv_link_for_workshop`. The two-layer enforcement (link gate + route gate) is intentional belt-and-braces; if a future slice loosens one, the other still holds.
- **Filename doesn't reflect the `requires_checkout` filter.** A user pulling `?requires_checkout=yes` and `?show=archived` simultaneously gets `items_archived.csv`, not `items_archived_requires_checkout.csv`. Trade-off: shorter filenames vs. self-documenting filenames. Picked short; the in-CSV `requires_checkout` cell tells the receiver what they got. Flagged — if real users find downloads confusing, the filename can absorb more state.
- **`node_id` filter doesn't propagate into the CSV link href.** The route accepts `?node_id=N` (and the CSV branch honours it) but the items list page doesn't surface a node filter UI yet, so the CSV link doesn't include `node_id`. A power user typing `?node_id=5` directly into the URL bar would lose that filter when they click "Download CSV". Acceptable for v1 (the filter is URL-only, not UI-driven); flagged for the polish slice that adds a node filter widget.
- **Decimal scale wart inherited from R4 / R5.** `current_qty`, `reorder_threshold`, `reorder_qty` round-trip via the column at scale 4 (`Decimal("10.0000")` → `"10.0000"`). Same wart as variance trend's variance column. Test `TestItemsListCsvBody::test_one_item_one_data_row` works around by parsing each numeric cell back to `Decimal` for comparison; spreadsheet receivers read `"10.0000"` and `"10"` as the same number.
- **CSV-injection mitigation still not applied.** Items SKU + name are manager-typed; CSV recipients are colleagues who can already read the data via the HTML view. Same posture as R5; documented in `app/csv_export.py`'s module docstring.
- **No new e2e walk.** The existing items-list e2e walks (in `test_items_e2e.py`) already navigate to `/admin/items`; adding a "click Download CSV" leg would only re-test what the integration tests pin. Playwright doesn't simulate the OS file-save dialog. Flagged.
- **Return type widened on `list_items` from `HTMLResponse` to `Response`.** Necessary because the CSV branch returns a non-HTML `Response`. The `@router.get("")` decorator's `response_class` argument was dropped (it only affects OpenAPI schema generation; runtime behaviour unchanged). No callers depend on the narrower type.
- **`_csv_rows_for_items` accesses `r["item"]` four times.** A small inline binding (`item = r["item"]`) would be tidier but the comprehension form is what the PO list helper uses too — keeping the shape uniform across the three CSV mappers. Documented.
- **No CSV export on movements list / stock takes list / suppliers list / locations list / categories list / users list / dashboard widgets.** R5b lights up the items list — the most-trafficked list view. Subsequent slices can extend the pattern; each will be ~25 LoC + ~15 tests reusing `csv_response`. Documented.
- **`is_csv` check happens after the `require_role` dependency but before the query.** A pending or anon user hits the dependency gate first (401/403); a Workshop user passes the dependency, then the inner `is_csv` check rejects with 403. Pinned by the role-enforcement tests for all five subjects.
- **The csv_response helper handles the trailing `\r\n` automatically** — `csv.writer.writerow` always appends one. Empty `rows` still produces a header row + one trailing `\r\n` (which is what `TestItemsListCsvBody::test_empty_emits_only_header_row` asserts). Consistent with R5's two surfaces.

---

**Self-critique notes (rolling) — R5:**

- **CSV-injection mitigation not applied.** A cell value starting with `=` / `+` / `-` / `@` could be interpreted as an Excel formula. v1 risk model: all-internal users (Workshop is server-side blocked from these routes); data is workshop inventory typed by managers; CSV recipients are colleagues who can already read the data via the HTML view. The mitigation (prepending a single quote in `_coerce_cell`) is a one-line change if the threat model changes. Documented in `app/csv_export.py`'s module docstring; flagged.
- **Decimal scale wart inherited from R4 / M3 / M4 / ST3.** A variance `Decimal("3.0000")` exports as `"3.0000"`, not `"3"`. The HTML view has the same wart. Acceptable — spreadsheet receivers read both as the same number; flagged for a future quantise-on-read pass that would clean it up across all surfaces simultaneously. The integration test `TestVarianceTrendCsvBody::test_one_stock_take_one_data_row` works around the wart by parsing each cell back to `Decimal` and comparing numerically.
- **No CSV export on dashboard widgets / items list / movements list / stock takes list / suppliers list / locations list / categories list / users list.** R5 lights up exactly the two surfaces flagged in the Next slice note (variance trend + PO list). Subsequent slices can extend the pattern using `csv_response`. Documented; no scope expansion.
- **No new e2e walk for R5.** The existing `test_office_schedules_a_stock_take` walk already lands on the variance-trend page (via the dashboard link); the existing `test_reorder_e2e.py` walk already lands on the PO list. Adding a "click Download CSV" leg would only re-test the link visibility the integration tests already pin; Playwright doesn't simulate the OS file-save dialog. Flagged for a polish slice if cross-browser CSV behaviour ever needs verification.
- **`format` param shadows Python's `format()` builtin** in `list_purchase_orders`'s body. The function never calls `format()`, so the shadow is benign; renaming to `as_format` would break the URL convention (`?format=csv` is the obvious user-facing param name). Acceptable trade-off; documented.
- **`_safe_filename` is conservative — non-ASCII chars replaced with `_`.** A future filename derived from a user-supplied string (e.g. a supplier name embedded in `suppliers_acme_co.csv`) with international characters would render as underscores. v1 filenames are static templates (`variance_trend_{days}d.csv`, `purchase_orders_{status_filter}.csv`), so the limitation is theoretical. Flagged for the polish slice that adds a user-name-in-filename surface.
- **No CSV upload / import path.** MISSION §3 requires "Export any list view to CSV" — export only. R5 honours that scope.
- **Helper takes list-of-lists, not list-of-dicts.** Callers each have a small `_csv_rows_for_*` mapper. Pushing the dict-to-list conversion into `csv_response` would add a `column_keys` param and complicate the unit tests; keeping the helper unstrict (just iterate-and-coerce) maximises caller flexibility. Trade-off documented.
- **Filename collision risk.** Two CSVs downloaded at the same window into the same downloads folder collide; the browser appends `(1)`. Same posture as the PO PDF's filename. Acceptable.
- **Workshop server-side gated to 403.** Pinned by `TestVarianceTrendCsvRoleEnforcement::test_workshop_csv_is_403` and `TestPOListCsvRoleEnforcement::test_workshop_csv_is_403`. The CSV link doesn't render for Workshop because Workshop can't reach either page in the first place.
- **No "Reports" nav entry yet.** R4's self-critique flagged this; R5 doesn't add a new page (just a CSV branch on the existing one), so the flag stays open. Once a third reports surface lands, the nav menu becomes worth adding.
- **PO list CSV's `created_at` is the raw `datetime.isoformat()`** (e.g. `2026-05-07T14:30:00.123456+00:00`). Spreadsheet receivers can parse it but a date-only column might be friendlier in some workflows. Trade-off: full-fidelity vs. spreadsheet-ergonomics. Picked full-fidelity because the HTML view also renders `.isoformat()`. Flagged.
- **Tests assert exact CSV body shape** (e.g. `"a,b\\r\\n1,2\\r\\n3,4\\r\\n"`). Brittle if a future change adjusts column ordering or quoting — but exact-match tests catch regressions in the CSV writer's behaviour, which is exactly what a CSV consumer cares about. Acceptable; a quoting-rule change would correctly fail these tests.
- **`format=""` default vs. `format=None`.** Picked `""` so the comparison `format == "csv"` doesn't have to handle the None case. Marginal cosmetic choice.

---

**Self-critique notes (rolling) — R4:**

- **Discovery via dashboard link only — no nav entry.** A Manager browsing `nav-*` won't find the variance trend without going through the dashboard. Trade-off: adding a "Reports" nav entry for a single-page report would clutter the nav for marginal gain; once R5 (CSV export) lands a Reports menu becomes worth it. Documented; flagged for the polish pass once a second `/admin/reports/*` page exists.
- **Aggregation in Python after a per-stock-take lines fetch.** A single `GROUP BY` query with `CASE WHEN ...` in the SUMs would be tighter, but cross-DB (SQLite + Postgres) `FILTER` / signed-sum support diverges and the per-stock-take batch in Python keeps the code readable. At v1 scale (tens of stock takes per quarter, tens of lines per take) the difference is sub-ms. Documented; flagged for the perf pass if the lines table ever grows past tens of thousands of rows.
- **Window default 90 days vs R1's `top_days` default 30.** Different defaults are deliberate — variance trend is a slower signal (a stock take a quarter) so a wider window is more informative. A user expecting the same "last 30 days" lens as the top-consumed widget might be surprised; the form input is the override. Documented in the route docstring.
- **No per-item / per-category drill-down.** The table aggregates at the stock-take level. A manager wondering "*which* item has the most variance" still has to click through to the detail page. A future R4b polish could pivot the table — but the dashboard's top-consumed already answers a related question (which items are flowing fastest); variance + consumption rarely correlate. Out of scope for v1.
- **No CSV export from the variance-trend page.** R5 is the export slice. The dashboard's COGS card and the top-consumed table also lack CSV. Out of scope for R4.
- **Decimal scale on totals inherits whatever the line variances were stored at.** A stock take with `Decimal("2.0000")` variance + a stock take with `Decimal("3")` variance produces a totals sum of `Decimal("5.0000")` (scale 4 dominates). Same wart as M3 / M4 / ST3's audit shapes. The template renders it without quantising; e.g. `variance-trend-total-net` for a single-line stock take with variance=-2 will render as `-2.0000` (the column quantisation), but the integration tests use `to_contain_text("-2")` rather than exact-string matches to avoid the wart. Acceptable; flagged for a future R-series quantise-on-read pass.
- **`_scope_label` duplicated** between `app/stock_takes.py` and `app/reports.py`. Two callers, six lines each — extraction would save ~6 lines but introduce a `_labels.py` module that's used by exactly two callers. Same posture as `_parse_non_negative_decimal_required` duplicated between `purchase_orders.py` / `movements.py` and `_is_leaf` duplicated between `items.py` / `field_defs.py`. Flagged for extraction once a third caller arrives.
- **Workshop is server-side gated to 403.** The dashboard route already blocks Workshop, so a Workshop user has no path to even see the variance-trend link. Pinned by `TestVarianceTrendRoleEnforcement::test_workshop_get_is_403`.
- **Totals card always renders, even when zero rows.** A blank-state user sees the framing ("Totals over the last 90 days: stock takes=0, ...") rather than a hidden card. Trade-off: a noisier empty state vs. consistent framing. Picked consistent framing because the all-zero card is the right answer to "have we run any stock takes recently".
- **No exclusion of archived items from the aggregate.** A line on a completed stock take whose item has since been archived still contributes its variance to the totals — historical record of "how much error did we have when this was active". Documented; pinned by being unaddressed in the integration tests (no archived-item test). Could be questioned later but the audit-history posture (archived items still surface in audit / history views per MISSION §3) is the right default.
- **No date-range filter (only window-in-days)**. A manager wanting "Q1 2026 only" has to compute the days-back as of today. A `?from=YYYY-MM-DD&to=YYYY-MM-DD` extension would mirror R1's COGS form. Out of scope for R4; flagged for a polish slice.
- **Line counts are fetched in a single batched IN-list query.** Worst case is one round-trip per stock take in the window (which at v1 scale is fine), but the current implementation is one fetch followed by Python grouping — single round-trip. Pinned by inspection of the route handler; no test directly counts queries.
- **`_load_trend_rows`'s scope-label resolution doesn't filter by `archived_at`.** An archived node / location is still labelled "Category: X" / "Location: Y" without a "(archived)" suffix. Documented; flagged. Same posture as the dashboard's top-consumed table (which doesn't suffix archived items either) but inconsistent with the reorder dashboard's archived-supplier suffix.
- **Form's `<input type="number" min=1 max=365>` is a soft client-side hint** — the server-side `_coerce_days` is the canonical guard. A power user submitting `?days=400` via curl gets the default-90 result, not a 400. Same posture as R1.

---

**Self-critique notes (rolling) — ST3:**

- **No "uncommit" route.** Once `completed_at` is set the row is read-only — no UI to undo a commit. Corrections must be made via fresh manual-adjustment movements (M4) outside the stock-take flow. Same posture as PO5's "no un-receive" + PO2b's "cannot un-cancel". MISSION §3 doesn't require unbreaking the state machine; the audit log preserves both events. Documented; flagged for a polish slice if a real shop hits the case.
- **No per-line note input on the commit form.** The operator can't attribute *why* a particular line had a variance (e.g. "found in second cupboard", "damaged batch"); the audit row's `movements` list carries direction + variance + cost but no operator note. `StockTakeLine.notes` exists but is unused. A polish slice could surface it; ST3 keeps the commit form short. Self-critique flag.
- **Default unit-cost lookup is N+1 query** (one `_last_unit_cost` call per positive-variance line on the GET render). At v1 scale (tens of items per stock take) this is sub-millisecond. At hundreds it'd want a single batch query joined to the lines. Flagged.
- **All-zero stock take is a hard 400, not a soft no-op.** A stock take where every count matches the system perfectly cannot be committed; the operator just ignores the row. Trade-off: forcing a real adjustment vs. allowing a "we counted and everything was fine" record. Picked hard 400 because committing nothing writes a confusing audit row + no movements. Documented; pinned by `TestCommitValidation::test_no_variances_is_400`.
- **Insufficient-stock error path is single-error.** First failing negative-variance line aborts the whole transaction; the operator sees only that line's shortage, fixes it (re-counts or accepts the new available qty via re-counting), re-submits, and may then see the *next* shortage if there is one. Acceptable for v1; a multi-error mode would need a "validate-without-mutating" pass through `consume_fifo` first. Flagged.
- **All commit movements share one `reason` field** (`f"stock take #{N}"`). Per-line nuance (which line / direction / variance) lives in the audit row's `movements` list, not on the movement row. Reading `stock_movements` in isolation, all commit-batch rows look identical apart from `qty` + `total_cost`. Acceptable — the audit row is the canonical attribution. A future polish could include the variance signal in the reason (e.g. `f"stock take #{N} +3"` / `-2`).
- **`commit_lines` filtering happens server-side per render.** A user typing into the count input doesn't see the commit form refresh until they save (the count save round-trips). HTMX could swap the commit form in real time on count changes — out of scope.
- **The error-render path on insufficient stock re-renders the full detail page** (count form + commit form + status), not just the commit form. Re-uses `_detail_context` for symmetry with the GET render. The operator's typed `unit_cost_<id>` inputs are preserved through the round-trip via `commit_form_values`; their typed counts are *not* preserved across this round-trip because counts and commit live in two separate forms — but counts have already been saved by the time commit is attempted, so the round-trip preserves the on-disk count state.
- **Decimal scale wart on `total_cost` audit values** — `"7.500000"` for positive (qty scale-4 × form-cost scale-2 = scale-6) and `"4.00000000"` for negative (qty scale-4 × layer-cost scale-4 = scale-8). Same wart as M3 / M4. Pinned by `TestCommitAuditShape` with explanatory comments. Acceptable; future R-series can quantise on read.
- **`StockTakeLine.committed` flips True before the `db.commit()` lands.** A rollback (insufficient stock on a later line) reverts the flag along with the movement; pinned by `TestCommitInsufficientStock::test_partial_failure_leaves_no_state`. ORM-level: `line.committed = True` is queued in the unit-of-work; the `db.rollback()` call drops the change before flush.
- **No DB-level CHECK constraint** that `completed_at >= started_at`, or that a `committed=True` line lives only on a stock-take where `completed_at IS NOT NULL`. Same posture as ST1 / ST2's lifecycle invariants — route layer is the v1 enforcement point. Flagged for a P-series tightening pass.
- **Status badge on the detail page hard-codes English** ("scheduled" / "in_progress" / "completed"). Same posture as ST1 / ST2. i18n out of scope for v1.
- **Atomic-rollback drops the in-flight movements** that were inserted but not yet committed. SQLAlchemy unit-of-work tracks both inserts and column mutations; `db.rollback()` reverts both. Pinned by the partial-failure test. Important for the cost-engine invariants — a half-committed stock take could leave layers + qty in an inconsistent state.

---

**Self-critique notes (rolling) — ST2:**

- **No "abort stock take" route.** Operator who clicked Start by mistake (e.g. the manager wanted to re-pick the scope after seeing the preview) has to ignore the in-progress row — there's no UI to cancel. The audit log preserves the start. Same posture as ST1's missing cancel route. Both are queued for a polish slice; ST2 doesn't make this worse.
- **Single-page count form.** Every line on the stock take is rendered as one big form, one row per item, all submitted together. For tens of items (the v1 expected scale at UC) this is fine — it fits on one screen with normal scrolling. For hundreds the form gets long + the save round-trip walks every input. A future polish slice could paginate with `?page=N` and the partial-save shape (lines whose key isn't in the form are left unchanged — already implemented for the stale-tab defence; same shape would carry the paginated-save case).
- **Variance baseline is `current_qty` snapshotted at start time.** A stock-in or stock-out *during* an in-progress count would shift `current_qty` but `system_qty` on the line stays put — variance becomes "what we expected at start" minus "what we counted on the floor". By design (per MISSION §3 "see variance vs. system" — the system at the time of the count, not at commit time). ST3 commits using the line's `system_qty`, not `item.current_qty`, so the variance is the true delta the operator measured.
- **Empty-scope on start is a hard 400.** A scheduled stock take whose scope no longer resolves to any active items (e.g. all items archived in the meantime) can't be started — operator either picks a different scope by scheduling a new stock take, or unarchives items. The friendlier "start anyway and record an empty count" was rejected: v1's mental model is "a count means counting items"; an empty count writes a confusing audit row. Pinned by `TestStartValidation::test_zero_items_in_scope_is_400`. Documented.
- **No in-form errors on count validation.** A non-numeric or negative `counted_<id>` returns a bare 400 page; the operator hits Back and re-types. Same posture as every other form outside M3 / M4's data-dependent stock-shortage carve-out. The friendlier in-form error sweep is a polish concern across all forms.
- **`StockTakeLine.notes` column is still unused.** ST1 added it; ST2 doesn't surface it. ST3 may use it for variance reasons (per MISSION §3 "Adjustment movements... required reason"); the operator might want to type "found in second cupboard" against an excess line. Out of scope for ST2; flagged for ST3 to decide whether the per-line note maps to the adjustment movement's `reason` or stays on the stock-take line.
- **No "re-count this line" affordance — just edit + submit.** The form already supports re-counting (the input pre-fills with the prior `counted_qty` if any; the operator types a new value, submits, the audit log gets a new `stock_take.counted` row showing the change). Trade-off: every save touches every changed line + writes one audit row per save. A future enhancement could add a per-line "save just this line" button (HTMX'd) for big-form ergonomics.
- **Audit row's `lines` array is per-save, not cumulative.** Two operators (or two saves by the same operator) produce two `stock_take.counted` rows with separate `lines` deltas. Reading the audit log in order reconstructs the count history; the line's *current* values are on the row itself. Same posture as PO5's per-receive `purchase_order.received` audit rows. Documented.
- **No pagination clamping on the detail page.** The route doesn't accept `?page=N` for the count form yet. If a stock take has 500 lines, the page renders all 500 inputs — slow first paint (Jinja loop) but no DB cost. Flagged as a perf follow-up if real shops hit it.
- **Status-derived badges hard-coded English** (`"scheduled"` / `"in_progress"` / `"completed"`). Same posture as ST1's status labels. i18n out of scope for v1.
- **No DB-level constraint on the lifecycle invariant** (started_at-without-completed-at-is-in-progress; both-set-is-completed). Same posture as ST1's XOR scope invariant — route layer is the v1 enforcement point. Flagged for a P-series tightening pass.
- **Decimal scale wart on variance audit** — `variance` is the difference of `counted_qty` (parsed at the operator's input scale, e.g. `Decimal("10")`) and `system_qty` (read back at the column's scale 4, e.g. `Decimal("8.0000")`). The result inherits scale 4 (`Decimal("2.0000")`). The audit row carries `"2.0000"` not `"2"`. Same wart as M3's stock-out audit shape (`total_cost` carries scale 4 because `layer.unit_cost` is read back at scale 4). Pinned by `TestCountsAuditShape::test_only_changed_lines_in_audit` with a comment explaining the inheritance. Acceptable; future R-series can quantise on read if a uniform shape is wanted.
- **Engine isolation pinned by two dedicated tests.** `TestEngineIsolation::test_start_writes_no_engine_state` and `test_counts_writes_no_engine_state` confirm `item.current_qty`, `cost_layers`, `cost_layer_consumptions`, and `stock_movements` are untouched. ST3 will be the slice that exercises those paths.
- **Detail-link from list page is "View →" not status-aware.** The link points at the same URL regardless of status; the destination's render branch handles the right surface. Trade-off: a manager scanning the list might want a "Start" or "Continue counting" hint per row. The status badge in the row already differentiates, so the link's label staying generic is fine. Documented.
- **No "scheduled date is past" warning on the scheduled detail page.** A stock take scheduled for 2026-01-01 viewed today (2026-05-07) renders the same as one scheduled for tomorrow. Could add a subtle `<small>` "(scheduled date has passed)" hint. Flagged for a polish slice.

**Plan:**

- **Three new routes** on the existing `/admin/stock-takes` prefix in `app/stock_takes.py`:
  - `GET /admin/stock-takes/{stock_take_id}` — Manager + Office (Workshop + pending → 401/403; anon 401). 404 unknown id. Three render branches gated on the derived status:
    - `scheduled` (both timestamps null) — shows scope summary + list of items currently in scope (with `current_qty` for context) + a "Start counting" button (POST form). Empty-scope branch hides the button + surfaces a `stock-take-no-items-note`.
    - `in_progress` (`started_at` set, `completed_at` null) — shows the count form (one big form with per-line inputs + a "Save counts" submit), summary counters (`counted` / `uncounted` / `with_variance`), and a `<details>`-wrapped read-only list of unchanged items.
    - `completed` (both timestamps set) — shows the read-only summary table (system_qty / counted_qty / variance per line). ST2 doesn't write this state; the branch is forward-looking for ST3.
  - `POST /admin/stock-takes/{stock_take_id}/start` — Manager + Office. Validates: 404 unknown; 400 if not in `scheduled` state ("already started" / "already completed"); 400 if scope resolves to zero active items ("scope contains no items to count"). Resolves in-scope items via `_resolve_scope_items`, creates one `StockTakeLine(system_qty=item.current_qty, counted_qty=None, variance=None, committed=False)` per item, sets `started_at = now()`, writes a `stock_take.started` audit row with the line snapshot, commits, redirects to detail. Idempotent against double-clicks via the status guard.
  - `POST /admin/stock-takes/{stock_take_id}/counts` — Manager + Office (`async def` to read per-line dynamic keys via `await request.form()`, same precedent as PO2b's edit + PO5's receive). Validates: 404 unknown; 400 if not in `in_progress` state ("not in progress; start counting first"); per-line `counted_<line_id>` parses as a non-negative Decimal (blank → uncount; non-numeric / negative → 400). Lines whose key is missing from the form are left unchanged (defends against stale tabs). Computes a sparse diff in memory before mutating: only lines whose `counted_qty` actually changed are written; if zero lines changed, no audit row is written and the route flashes "no changes" (same posture as PO2b's no-op submit). Writes a `stock_take.counted` audit row with the per-line before/after diff. Redirects to detail.

- **Engine isolation:** ST2 doesn't touch `cost_layers`, `cost_layer_consumptions`, `item.current_qty`, or `stock_movements`. Variances are *recorded* (`StockTakeLine.counted_qty` + `StockTakeLine.variance`) but not *actioned* — ST3 is the slice that walks the lines, builds adjustment movements, and routes through `record_receipt` (positive variance) or `consume_fifo` (negative variance). Pinned by `TestEngineIsolation` tests.

- **Scope resolution** (`_resolve_scope_items(db, st) -> list[Item]`):
  - Both scope ids null → all `Item.archived_at IS NULL`.
  - `scope_node_id` set → items where `taxonomy_node_id == scope_node_id` OR `taxonomy_node_id` is a *child* of `scope_node_id` (the v1 taxonomy is two levels deep, so a top-level node selection includes its sub-categories — natural mental model: "count Raw Materials" includes "Raw Materials → Bullion"). Implemented as `WHERE taxonomy_node_id IN (scope_node_id, sub-category ids)`.
  - `scope_location_id` set → items where `location_id == scope_location_id`.
  - In all cases, exclude archived items.
  - Order by `Item.sku` for stable rendering.

- **Variance derivation** (`_compute_variance(counted, system)`): `counted - system` when `counted is not None` else `None`. Stored on `StockTakeLine.variance` as a signed Decimal (negative = shrinkage, positive = excess). The form renders the variance with a leading sign character (`"-2.0000"` / `"+1.5000"` / `"0.0000"`) plus a `data-variance-sign` attribute (`"neg"` / `"pos"` / `"zero"`) so future styling can colour-code it.

- **Audit shapes:**
  - `stock_take.started`: `before={"started_at": null}`, `after={"started_at": <ISO>, "lines": [{"line_id", "item_id", "system_qty"}, ...]}`. The lines snapshot pins what was in scope at the moment of starting. Decimals stringified via `str(decimal)`. New audit action.
  - `stock_take.counted`: `before={"lines": [{"line_id", "counted_qty": <prev str | null>}, ...]}`, `after={"lines": [{"line_id", "counted_qty": <new str | null>, "variance": <new str | null>}, ...]}`. Only entries for lines whose `counted_qty` *changed* (a no-op submit writes no audit row at all, same posture as PO2b's `purchase_order.updated`). The `before` carries only the changed field (counted_qty), `after` carries counted_qty + variance (since variance is derived from counted_qty + system_qty, the two move together).

- **Helpers** (added to `app/stock_takes.py`):
  - `_resolve_scope_items(db, st) -> list[Item]` — single SQL round-trip with the IN-list of node ids (or location id, or no filter); ordered by sku.
  - `_compute_variance(counted, system) -> Decimal | None` — `counted - system` or `None`.
  - `_format_variance(value) -> str` — signed string for template rendering (`"+1.5000"` / `"-2.0000"` / `"0.0000"`); `""` when None.
  - `_variance_sign(value) -> str` — `"pos"` / `"neg"` / `"zero"` / `""` for the data-attribute.
  - `_lines_for_stock_take(db, st_id) -> list[StockTakeLine]` — fetch ordered by item.sku (joined to items for the order).
  - `_count_progress(lines) -> dict` — returns `{counted, uncounted, with_variance}` integer triple for the summary counters.
  - `_can_start(st)` / `_can_count(st)` — predicates over the timestamp pair.

- **Templates / test-ids:**
  - New `stock_take_detail.html` with three render branches:
    - **Scheduled branch:** `stock-take-detail-heading` (carries the title + scheduled date), `stock-take-detail-status-badge` (`data-status="scheduled"`), `stock-take-detail-scope`, `stock-take-detail-scheduled-for`, `stock-take-detail-notes`. A read-only items-in-scope table with per-row `stock-take-scope-row` (`data-item-id`) and `stock-take-scope-row-sku` / `stock-take-scope-row-name` / `stock-take-scope-row-current-qty`. `stock-take-start-form` with hidden CSRF and `stock-take-start-submit`; the form is hidden + replaced by `stock-take-no-items-note` when zero items in scope.
    - **In-progress branch:** progress summary `stock-take-progress-summary` with `stock-take-progress-counted` / `stock-take-progress-uncounted` / `stock-take-progress-with-variance`. `stock-take-count-form` (action POST to `/counts`) with hidden CSRF; per-line `stock-take-count-row` (with `data-line-id`/`data-item-id`/`data-counted="true|false"`) carrying `stock-take-count-sku` / `stock-take-count-name` / `stock-take-count-system-qty` / `<input name="counted_<line_id>" data-testid="stock-take-count-counted-input">` / `stock-take-count-variance` (with `data-variance-sign`). Submit `stock-take-count-submit`. Empty-state `stock-take-empty-lines` when zero lines.
    - **Completed branch:** read-only table mirroring in-progress shape but with no inputs. Forward-looking; ST3 will write this state.
  - `stock_takes_list.html`: per-row gain a `stock-takes-row-detail-link` link to `/admin/stock-takes/{id}` (drops a "View" cell or wraps the existing scope cell). Existing test-ids preserved.

- **Validation order** (atomic — all 400 *before* any DB write):
  - **start**: 404 → 400 not-scheduled → resolve scope → 400 zero-items.
  - **counts**: 404 → 400 not-in-progress → fetch lines → parse every form field that matches `counted_<line_id>` → 400 on any non-numeric / negative → compute diff → write only changed lines → audit only if any changed.

- **Test coverage** (target ~50 new):
  - **Unit** (`tests/unit/test_stock_takes.py` ~6 new): `TestResolveScopeItems` — all-scope returns active items only; node-scope returns items at that node + children; node-scope excludes archived items; location-scope returns items at that location; excludes items in different scope; ordered by sku. `TestComputeVariance` — counted=10 system=8 → +2; counted=5 system=10 → -5; counted=10 system=10 → 0; counted=None → None. `TestFormatVariance` — signed string for each sign + None → "".
  - **Integration** (`tests/integration/test_stock_takes_routes.py` ~40 new):
    - **Detail role enforcement** (5): anon GET 401; pending 403; Workshop 403; Office / Manager / Admin 200.
    - **Detail render — scheduled** (4): unknown 404; scheduled with items shows start form + items table + scope summary; scheduled with empty scope (e.g. archived item) hides start button + shows no-items-note; status badge `data-status="scheduled"`.
    - **Detail render — in_progress** (3): in-progress shows count form + per-line inputs + progress summary; status badge `data-status="in_progress"`; no start form.
    - **Detail render — completed** (2): completed shows read-only table; no count form, no start form.
    - **Start role + validation** (8): anon 401; pending 403; Workshop 403; Office / Manager / Admin 303; 404 unknown; 400 already-started; 400 already-completed; 400 zero-items-in-scope (e.g. archived all items); failed validation writes no `started_at` flip + no audit + no lines.
    - **Start happy path — scope=all** (3): creates one line per active item; lines carry `system_qty=item.current_qty` at start time; archived items excluded; audit `stock_take.started` shape with line snapshot + ISO `started_at`; flash visible after redirect.
    - **Start happy path — scope=node** (2): only items at the node + descendants become lines; items in different node excluded.
    - **Start happy path — scope=location** (1): only items at that location become lines.
    - **Counts role + validation** (8): anon 401; pending 403; Workshop 403; Office 303; 404 unknown; 400 not-in-progress (scheduled / completed both reject); per-line non-numeric 400; per-line negative 400; failed validation writes no state change + no audit.
    - **Counts happy path** (5): single-line update sets `counted_qty` + `variance` (counted=12, system=10 → variance=+2); blank counted_qty resets to None (uncount); multi-line update touches only the changed lines; no-op submit (resubmit same values) writes no audit row + flashes "no changes"; missing line key leaves the line unchanged.
    - **Audit shape on counts** (2): only changed lines appear in `before`/`after` lines arrays; no-op submit writes no audit row at all.
    - **Engine isolation** (2): start writes no `StockMovement` + no `CostLayer` + no `CostLayerConsumption` + `item.current_qty` unchanged; counts writes no `StockMovement` + `item.current_qty` unchanged.
    - **List page detail link** (1): per-row `stock-takes-row-detail-link` href to `/admin/stock-takes/{id}`.
  - **E2E walk extension** (`tests/e2e/test_stock_takes_e2e.py`): after the existing schedule leg, the manager creates an item under "ST1 Materials" with `current_qty` = 0 (the ST1 walk archives the category at the end; we'll reorder so the count happens before the archive). Manager records a stock-in to bump `current_qty` to 50 (via `/admin/items/{id}/in` form, no need to call the engine directly). Office user navigates to the stock takes list, clicks the row's detail link, lands on the scheduled detail page, asserts the scope items table shows the seeded item with `current_qty=50.0000`, clicks "Start counting", asserts the redirect lands on the detail page in `in_progress` state with one count row pre-filled with `system_qty=50.0000` and an empty counted input. Office fills counted=48, submits, asserts the variance cell renders "-2.0000" and the progress summary shows `counted=1`, `uncounted=0`, `with_variance=1`. The `current_qty` on the item is unchanged (verified by visiting `/admin/items` and viewing the row). Cleanup archives the item then the category.

**Self-critique notes (queued — to fill in after impl):** in-form errors on counts validation (bare 400 today), no "abort stock take" route (operator who started by mistake has to ignore the row), no per-line note column rendered (`StockTakeLine.notes` exists but is unused — ST3 may use it for variance reasons), no descendant-of-descendant resolution (v1 taxonomy is 2-level so the IN-list of `(scope_node_id, *direct children)` is exact; an N-level taxonomy would need recursion).


**Self-critique notes (rolling) — ST1:**

- **No DB-level CHECK constraint on the XOR scope invariant.** The route layer is the sole guard against `scope_node_id` and `scope_location_id` both being set on the same row. Same posture as taxonomy leaf invariants and item-units qty-vs-unique rule (route layer is the v1 enforcement point). A direct DB write that bypasses the route could land an inconsistent row. Out of scope for v1; flagged for a P-series tightening pass.
- **Scope=all silently ignores submitted `scope_node_id` / `scope_location_id`** rather than 400ing. A user who toggles from `node` to `all` after picking a node will land "all items" with the picked id stripped, which is the friendlier UX than rejecting. Pinned by `TestScopeAllIgnoresIdInputs::test_node_id_ignored_when_scope_is_all`. Trade-off: a stale form could lose a deliberately-picked scope; but the form's radio is the source of truth, not the picker.
- **`stock_take_lines` table is created but no rows are written in ST1.** The schema lands now so ST2 doesn't need a follow-up migration. A reader of the codebase today sees an empty table and could wonder if it's dead code; the model's docstring + the migration's docstring both explain the staging.
- **`stock_movements.stock_take_id` FK is now active but no code path writes a non-null value.** ST3 will activate it when stock-take adjustments land. The migration is loud about activating an unused FK; an unused FK is zero risk (no rows pointing at it) but a future reader could be momentarily confused. Documented in the migration's docstring.
- **No "edit" or "cancel" route for a scheduled stock take.** Once scheduled, the operator cannot reschedule or cancel via UI — they have to ignore the row. Same posture as PO drafts before PO2b, and the cancel route landed in PO2b. ST2 is more important (start the count); a dedicated cancel route is queued as a polish slice. The audit row preserves the schedule even if a future cancel route arrives.
- **Scope label is hard-coded English** (`"All items"` / `"Category: …"` / `"Location: …"`). i18n is out of scope for v1. Translation would require centralising user-facing strings.
- **No "in-form errors" on validation 400** — bare 400 page, same posture as every other validation outside M3 / M4's data-dependent stock-shortage carve-out. The user re-types the form. Acceptable for v1; the in-form-error sweep across all forms is a polish concern.
- **Node dropdown ordering puts top-level rows first then children**, but Jinja prefixes a `↳ ` on rows with `parent_id` set rather than visually grouping them. A real `<optgroup>` per parent would be the proper UX but doesn't gracefully handle the v1 two-level hierarchy in HTML (an `<optgroup>` can't be selected itself; we'd need the top-level node also as an option *outside* its optgroup, which is awkward). The flat list with prefix is friendly enough at v1 scale (a workshop has tens of categories, not hundreds).
- **No "scope preview"** showing the count of items that would be in scope. A polish slice could add `<span data-testid="stock-take-scope-preview-count">N items</span>` when the user toggles. Out of scope for ST1; ST2 will know the count when it freezes lines (and store it on `system_qty`).
- **List query is 4 round-trips** (stock_takes + nodes + locations + creators). At v1 scale (tens of stock takes per quarter) this is sub-millisecond. A bigger refactor would use `SELECT … FROM stock_takes LEFT JOIN taxonomy_nodes … LEFT JOIN locations … LEFT JOIN users` — fine but adds query complexity for marginal gain. Same posture as PO list view's per-row line-count query.
- **No DB-level constraint that `scheduled_for >= today`.** A backdated stock take is a legitimate "we did this last week, recording it now" scenario. The form takes any date; the route accepts any ISO date. Defensible.
- **Empty state copy differs by tab** (open vs completed) but the difference is subtle. Acceptable — different empty states need different messages.
- **Status renders as plain text** (`scheduled` / `in_progress` / `completed`). No coloured pill / badge styling — the `data-status` attribute on the row is the styling hook for a future polish slice. Same posture as the PO status badge in the early PO slices.
- **The `created_by` cell shows the email**, which is fine but a manager looking at a long list might prefer the user's name. The `User` model has a `name` column; we just chose `email` for consistency with the manager checkouts admin view (`row.holder_email`). Could thread name through later.
- **`StockTakeLine.notes` column is unused in ST1.** ST2/ST3 will use it for per-line operator notes during the count. The column lands now to avoid a follow-up migration.
- **Workshop is excluded from the entire `/admin/stock-takes` surface** — the nav is hidden + the route is server-side gated. MISSION §3 places stock takes in the Office + Manager surface; Workshop's role is to scan items in/out, not run audits. A workshop user with a stale link gets 403.

- **The single SQL query joins four tables on every page load.** ``Checkout → Item`` (inner) + ``User`` (outer) + ``ItemUnit`` (outer). At v1 scale (tens of open checkouts at most) this is sub-millisecond on SQLite + Postgres. If real-world scale ever pushes it (hundreds of open checkouts; SQLite walking the join), the right fix is a denormalised "is_open" boolean on `Checkout` plus a covering index on `(returned_at, expected_return)`. Out of scope for v1; flagged.
- **Overdue derivation is in Python after the SQL fetch**, not in SQL. The `?show=overdue` SQL filter still uses `Checkout.expected_return < now` (server-side), so the SQL itself is narrow. The Python pass produces the per-row `is_overdue` flag + `days_overdue` integer for the template — same predicate, just re-evaluated for the row-shaped view dict. A future "all-SQL" approach would push the day-difference calculation into the database; today's value is "the days_overdue counter is computed off `now().date()` not the database's clock" which means a request that crosses midnight UTC could show the same row with two different counters in two consecutive renders. Acceptable: the unit is "days", and the date-line cuts at UTC midnight. Documented.
- **Sorting is Python-side, not DB-side.** `rows.sort(...)` re-orders after the join. Trade-off: the SQL query doesn't depend on `is_overdue` (a derived column), so we can't `ORDER BY` it without a CASE. The Python sort is O(n log n) over tens of rows — ms scale. Could push to SQL with `ORDER BY CASE WHEN expected_return IS NOT NULL AND expected_return < :now THEN 0 ELSE 1 END, checked_out_at DESC` if it ever shows up in profiling.
- **Archived items still surface in the list** with a "(archived)" suffix on the SKU. Documented in MISSION §3 ("Archived nodes are hidden from item creation but still appear in historical reports and on existing items"). A workshop user who's archived an item that's currently checked out could expect the row to disappear — but a checked-out tool is *still owned* by UC, and the manager needs to see "this is overdue and the item it's tagged to has been archived" to chase the borrower. Not a bug.
- **Days-overdue is a calendar-day delta, not a wall-clock delta.** If `expected_return` was 23:59 UTC yesterday and now is 00:01 UTC today, the days_overdue badge shows "1" — technically only 2 minutes have elapsed. The user-facing read is "the due date was yesterday, today the tool is one day overdue". Matches the date-input granularity (the form takes ISO dates, not datetimes). Acceptable.
- **The cross-item view doesn't surface `condition_note` from the original checkout.** A manager wondering "what condition was this in when it left?" still needs to click into the per-item `/checkout` page (where the C2 status block surfaces the note). C4 keeps the cross-item view focused on "who / what / when / overdue" — adding a condition_note column would make the table wider for marginal value at v1 scale. Flagged for a polish slice.
- **Filter tabs are GET-redirect links**, not a form. Same posture as the items list's `?show=active|archived`. The URL is bookmarkable + shareable ("send me the overdue tab"). Trade-off: a future "filter by holder" or "filter by item" would need a real form.
- **No CSV export from this view.** R5 is the export slice. The dashboard widget links here, but a real "send me the overdue list as CSV" needs a `?format=csv` rendering. Out of scope for v1 / C4.
- **No "remind the borrower" action surface.** A manager looking at an overdue row can't trigger a reminder email; they have to copy the email and send manually. Out of scope; the email backend (PO4) is currently used only for outgoing supplier POs, but reusing it for borrower reminders is a 1-2 iteration follow-up. Documented.
- **No DB-level constraint on the open-checkout invariant** (carried forward from C2 / C3). A partial unique index `(item_id, item_unit_id) WHERE returned_at IS NULL` would catch races. C4 doesn't introduce a new race surface but inherits the existing one. Same posture as the rest of the codebase (route layer is the sole guard at v1 scale). Flagged for a P-series tightening pass.
- **Dashboard widget pins on a single integer.** A future drill-down (showing a count breakdown like "3 overdue, 7 open") would mean the dashboard reads two numbers from the same query. Today the widget shows just the overdue count (it's the actionable one). Acceptable.
- **`overdue_count(db, *, now=None)` accepts an injected `now`** so the dashboard's render and the C4 page's query can share a single moment in time within a request, even though they're separate route handlers today. The dashboard uses the default `now=None` (calls `datetime.now(UTC)` itself); the C4 route also uses its own `datetime.now(UTC)`. Two separate requests = two separate `now()` values = potentially different counts if a row crosses overdue between them. Acceptable at v1 scale; a future "consolidated dashboard" slice could thread the same `now` through both reads.
- **The C4 query and the dashboard widget query are two round-trips, not one.** Inlining the dashboard's overdue count into the same query as the row list would save one SQL round-trip on the C4 page (which renders the count *and* the rows). Premature optimisation today — the count query is sub-millisecond, the row query is sub-millisecond, the page render is dominated by Jinja. If ever profiled as hot, combining them is a 5-line change.
- **No e2e walk for the qty-tracked overdue case.** The walk uses a unique-tracked item (CHK-A). Qty-tracked overdue rendering is exercised only in integration tests. Acceptable: the integration suite covers both the qty-tracked and the unique-tracked render paths exhaustively (5 + 4 tests respectively). The walk's value is end-to-end navigation, not data-shape coverage.
- **The "View item" / "Check in →" link points at the per-item `/checkout` page**, not the audit log or a dedicated history view. A manager wondering "what's the history of this checkout" has to read the audit log directly. Out of scope; the audit log read surface (a future R-series slice) is the right home for that.
- **No keyboard-shortcut to flip between filter tabs.** `aria-current="page"` is set, but a hardcoded `accesskey="o"` / `accesskey="d"` would speed up power users. Premature; flagged for the P2 accessibility pass.

**Plan:**

- **New module `app/checkouts_admin.py`** rather than extending `app/checkouts.py` because the existing `checkouts` router has prefix `/admin/items` (per-item flow), and this slice needs `/admin/checkouts` (cross-item oversight). Two prefixes → two router objects (same precedent as `purchase_orders.py`'s `draft_router` + `list_router`). The module exposes one helper `_overdue_count(db) -> int` that the dashboard imports to wire the widget.

- **Route**: `GET /admin/checkouts[?show=open|overdue]` — Manager + Office (Workshop 403; pending 403; anon 401). Default `show=open` lists every checkout with `returned_at IS NULL`. `show=overdue` narrows to open AND `expected_return < now()`. Unrecognised values silently coerce to `open` (same posture as `?show=active|archived` in items list and `?status_filter=` in PO list). The route runs **one query** that joins `Checkout` to `Item` (RESTRICT FK) + outer-joins `User` (SET NULL FK) + outer-joins `ItemUnit` (nullable for qty-tracked). Ordering: overdue first (rows where `expected_return IS NOT NULL AND expected_return < now()`), then by `checked_out_at DESC, id DESC`. Read-only — no mutations, no audit.
